# DECISIONS.md — cuento

Why the design is the way it is. AGENTS.md defines *how* to work; PLAN.md defines *what* to build, in order; this file records *why*. When they conflict, this file wins for rationale.

Seeded at p00.1 from the settled-decisions table in PLAN.md. Later steps append one line per non-trivial choice (see AGENTS "Ambiguity"). Entries are append-only in spirit: supersede rather than silently rewrite.

## Settled decisions (D1–D26)

| ID | Decision | Rationale |
|----|----------|-----------|
| D1 | Amounts stored as `int64` in the currency's **minor units**; exponent per currency from `currencies` table. | Exact arithmetic; JPY/BHD-style exponents cost nothing to support. |
| D2 | **Net-debit** signed amounts (debits +, credits −). Every transaction sums to exactly 0 in its currency — and to 0 **within each fund** (D20). Signed vs DR/CR is display-only, per user. | Single column; mixed revenue/expense subtrees subtotal naturally. |
| D3 | Transactions are **single-currency**. Cross-currency flows = two transactions through a multicurrency **FX Clearing** account (equity-class). Its converted balance on reports is cumulative FX gain/loss. GnuCash-style per-split value/amount pair rejected for schema+UI complexity; revisit if clearing proves awkward. | Keeps the zero-sum invariant trivial and honest. |
| D4 | Audit = append-only `*_versions` tables: entity id + `change_id` + `valid_from` + `op(create/update/delete)` + full snapshot of business columns. Current tables are the denormalized latest state. State as of time T = row with max(`valid_from`) ≤ T per entity, excluded if `op='delete'`. Versions tables never see UPDATE/DELETE. | Fast current-state queries, mechanical point-in-time, pure append. |
| D5 | v1 audit surface: per-transaction history UI + per-entity as-of store queries + integrity check that current == latest version. Whole-report "books as edited at time T" is supported by the data but deferred as a feature. | Keeps the report toolkit single-plane for v1. |
| D6 | **sqlc** (queries) + **goose** (migrations, embedded). Forward-only migrations; runner backs up the db file before applying. No down migrations. | SQL stays visible/optimizable; backup beats theoretical rollbacks. |
| D7 | Driver: `modernc.org/sqlite` (pure Go). | CGO-free static binary, trivial cross-compile; perf ample at this scale. |
| D8 | Hosting: GCE **e2-micro always-free VM** + persistent disk + **Litestream → GCS** (free 5 GB). TLS via in-process autocert. Cloud Run rejected: ephemeral FS + scale-to-zero vs a single-writer SQLite file. | One binary, one VM, one systemd unit. |
| D9 | Auth primitives: scs sessions (SQLite store), argon2id, stdlib `http.CrossOriginProtection` (fallback nosurf), `html/template` escaping + strict CSP, `x/time/rate` on login. | Nothing hand-rolled; everything provable via route-registry tests. |
| D10 | Permissions: per-user `txn_perm ∈ {none,read,write}` + per-report-group read grants; `is_admin` implies everything. Report groups are declared in code and synced to the db at startup. Permissions are org-global in v1 (per-subsidiary grants → backlog, Q2). | Matches stated needs; no RBAC machinery. |
| D11 | Tree rules: A/L/E children must match parent type exactly; revenue and expense may interleave freely under R/E parents. Placeholders (accounts with children) hold no splits. | Balance sheet stays clean; mixed groupings stay possible — the chart holds *natural* categories, since programs are a dimension (D24). |
| D12 | FX conversion happens only in reports: balance-sheet figures at the closing (as-of) rate; P&L activity at each transaction-date rate; rate lookup = latest on-or-before date, direct pair then reciprocal. Rates stored as REAL; conversion rounds half-even at final aggregates. | Standard treatment; storage stays integer-exact. |
| D13 | Splits in a **finalized** reconciliation are locked (amount/account/txn/date/fund); editing requires an audited unreconcile first. Reconciliation is per `(account, currency)` and spans all funds — a bank statement covers one balance. | Statements stay provable; a key reason funds are a dimension, not currencies (D20). |
| D14 | **Bilingual UI (en, es) in v1**, extensible: `internal/i18n` embedded key→string catalogs + `t` template func; missing key falls back to en; a parity test enforces identical key sets across catalogs; adding a language = adding one catalog file. No CLDR or i18n dependency. Supersedes the earlier English-chrome-only decision. | The bookkeepers work in Spanish; catalogs are a page of code, not a framework. |
| D15 | Dependency allowlist: modernc.org/sqlite, pressly/goose/v3, sqlc (tool), alexedwards/scs/v2 (+sqlite3store), alexedwards/argon2id, golang.org/x/crypto (autocert), golang.org/x/time, nicksnyder/go-i18n/v2 + BurntSushi/toml + golang.org/x/text (the D14 bilingual catalog stack), google/go-cmp (tests). Additions need a DECISIONS entry *and* explicit human acknowledgment (AGENTS rule 1). (i18n stack added to this row p18.4 — it was the D14 catalog implementation and had been omitted here; see the p18.4 note.) | Lightweight by construction. |
| D16 | Date/number formats are small enumerations implemented and tested in `internal/money` — no CLDR dependency. Date entry uses text inputs (never `input[type=date]`). | Users pick from a handful of formats; browsers don't get a vote. |
| D17 | IDs are `INTEGER PRIMARY KEY AUTOINCREMENT` on financial tables (no rowid reuse after delete — audit-friendly). | Cheap referential permanence. |
| D18 | **Subsidiaries**: `subsidiaries` is a tree with exactly one root; each has a `base_currency`. Accounts map to **one or more** subsidiaries via `account_subsidiaries`, with the invariant **parent set ⊇ union of children's sets** (superset; assigning a sub auto-propagates to ancestors). Every transaction belongs to **exactly one** subsidiary and all its split accounts must include it. Report scope = a chosen subsidiary **consolidated with all descendants**; the root is full consolidation. Default report currency = the scoped subsidiary's base currency. | NetSuite-shaped without OneWorld machinery. |
| D19 | **Intercompany**: cross-subsidiary funding = paired transactions through due-to/due-from accounts flagged `intercompany`. Consolidated reports whose scope covers both sides collapse flagged accounts after asserting they net to zero per currency; a nonzero net renders as a warning row. Elimination journal entries are out of scope. | The flag makes consolidation honest and cheap. |
| D20 | **Restricted funds are a split dimension with fund-level conservation.** `funds` documents grants; a fund scopes to **one or more subsidiaries** via `fund_subsidiaries` (not inherited) and optionally to a **program subtree**. Every split carries `fund_id` (NULL = unrestricted); every transaction must sum to zero **within each fund**. Sub-currency modelling rejected: identical semantics but breaks single-statement reconciliation (D13), multiplies the currency/rate surface, and cross-currency conversion would mint pseudo-currencies. GAAP "released from restrictions" is **derived** in reporting, not journaled. | All the tracking power of the sub-currency idea, none of the collateral damage. |
| D21 | **Functional expenses (990 Part IX)** are a fixed enum `program | management | fundraising`. Expense accounts carry a **default** class; every expense split **requires** a class (prefilled, overridable); non-expense splits must be NULL. Trigger-enforced. Part IX is natural × functional — a matrix, so a dimension, not a duplicated hierarchy. | One report renders Part IX; the tree stays single and clean. |
| D22 | Import source is the **cleaned full-ledger CSV**. `cmd/ledgerimport` is driven by a reviewable mapping file: per source account → {type, parent, subsidiaries, default functional class}; per row → subsidiary and fund (defaults: root subsidiary, unrestricted) with optional source-column overrides. | The export is already a ledger; converting it beats re-keying history. |
| D23 | Negative restricted-fund balances (spending a grant past its receipts) are surfaced as **warnings** by `cuento check` and on fund pages — never blocked at write time. | Backdated entries make hard blocks hostile; visibility beats prevention. |
| D24 | **Programs are a dimension**: `programs` tree with a single seeded root ("General"); every **revenue and expense** split carries `program_id` (required; prefilled from the account default, else root); A/L/E splits carry none. Programs are org-global (Q5). The chart holds *natural* categories; mission structure lives in the program tree. Program and functional class are **orthogonal**. | 990 needs program-level revenue and expenses; duplicating programs in the tree was the same mistake as functional duplication. |
| D25 | **990 line mapping**: seeded `form990_lines` reference table (Parts VIII, IX, X); `accounts.form990_code` nullable with **effective code = own or nearest ancestor's** (inheritable). Not hard-required: 990 reports render an explicit **Unmapped** bucket instead of dropping rows; a warning check flags active R/E leaves with activity but no effective code. | One field, set ~10 times, and year-end becomes running four reports. |
| D26 | **Two-step go-live**: the production db is produced by `cmd/ledgerimport` from the cleaned CSVs + a reviewed mapping file, rehearsed during p09.4 (locally; mapping gitignored beside the source data). Deploy = (1) build db + `cuento check --strict`, (2) ship db + binary. The historical mapping assigns subsidiaries, funds, programs, functional classes, and 990 codes up front. | Import is the deployment path, not an afterthought. |

## Open questions (defaults in effect until answered)

- **Q5** — Programs scopeable per subsidiary vs org-global? Default: **global** (per-sub scoping → backlog). Affects p07, p08.
- **Q6** — Seed full Form 990 line set vs 990-EZ subset? Default: **full 990** (supersets EZ). Affects p05.1, p15.11.

Resolved (2026-07): Q1 (funds scope to subsidiaries, not inherited — D20), Q2 (permissions global — D10), Q3 (reports split with/without donor restrictions; per-grant = fund statement), Q4 (hosting, FX, "development" = fundraising column).

## D15 allowlist expansion — i18n + TOML (added 2026-07-12 at the human's request)

The human explicitly authorized adding a TOML parsing library and (conditioned on "lightweight, not taking over the project") an i18n library. Acknowledgment: 2026-07-12. Decision:
- Adopt **`github.com/nicksnyder/go-i18n/v2`** as the i18n engine, which brings **`github.com/BurntSushi/toml`** (the TOML grant) and **`golang.org/x/text`** (CLDR plural rules + language matching). go-i18n is library-shaped — it does not invert control; the boring-frontend/single-binary posture holds. `x/text` adds ~a few MB of CLDR tables to the CGO-free binary; accepted for correct en/es pluralization.
- This **supersedes D14's** "hand-rolled minimal parser, no CLDR/i18n dependency" clause and the p03.4 hand-rolled parser. The `internal/i18n` public facade (`T`, `Langs`, `{{t}}`, en-fallback, and the catalog-parity test) is **preserved**; catalogs move to the go-i18n TOML message format; pluralization is available where counts appear.
- These three modules are now on the D15 allowlist. No YAML lib is added (go-i18n's yaml unmarshaler is an unused transitive; catalogs are TOML).
- **Direct-require note (2026-07-12):** all three land as **direct** requires in `go.mod`, not the two-indirect shape the adoption task sketched. `go get ...go-i18n/v2/i18n` pulls only go-i18n + x/text (verified: it does **not** vendor BurntSushi/toml transitively). `internal/i18n` then imports `toml` directly (the prescribed `RegisterUnmarshalFunc("toml", toml.Unmarshal)`) and `x/text/language` directly (`NewBundle(language.English)` takes a `language.Tag`, no string form), so `go mod tidy` correctly marks all three direct. This is honest and reproducible (`make gen` stable); it deviates only from that task's descriptive "indirect" expectation, not from rule 1 — every module is D15-allowlisted.

## Functional testing (Playwright) — added 2026-07-11 at the human's request

The human explicitly asked for browser-based functional tests, **superseding AGENTS rule 12's original "no browser automation dependency" clause** (acknowledgment: 2026-07-11). Decisions:
- A **Playwright** end-to-end suite lives under `e2e/` (Node/npm, test-only). It is **not** a Go dependency (D15 untouched) and is **never** imported by the shipped binary or the frontend runtime — the boring-frontend rules (no framework/bundler/CDN, strict CSP) still govern the app itself.
- The suite drives the **real** `cuento serve -dev`: a fixture builds the binary, creates a temp SQLite db, seeds a known admin (via `cuento user add --admin`) plus any data a spec needs, launches serve on an ephemeral port, and tears it all down.
- Run via `make e2e` — **opt-in, separate from `make test`** (it needs a browser; `make test` stays hermetic per AGENTS). Chromium is provided by Playwright's own download.
- The suite **grows with the UI**: the harness (pE.1) is built now against the login flow (the only real page so far); every later UI phase (11–17) adds specs for its real user flows as part of that step's work. Functional coverage of a delivered UI flow is expected before its phase is considered done.

## Implementation notes (appended per step)

- **p00.2** — `make lint` runs golangci-lint's bundled gofumpt formatter *and* the standalone `gofumpt` binary; the two disagreed on import grouping (standalone splits the module-local `cuento/...` import into its own block, the bundled one merged it). Set `formatters.settings.gofumpt.module-path: cuento` in `.golangci.yml` so both produce the split form. Tooling reconciliation only; no design impact.
- **p00.3** — Pinned the Go toolchain to **1.25.12** (`go 1.25.12` in `go.mod`). govulncheck flagged 9 stdlib vulnerabilities (crypto/tls, crypto/x509, net, net/url, os, net/textproto) present in the locally-installed 1.25.7 and all fixed by ≤1.25.12; `GOTOOLCHAIN=auto` auto-downloads it. Keeps the vuln scan clean without touching any allowlisted dependency (D15). Bump the pin as later patches land.
- **p00.3 (DoD clarification, per human 2026-07-11)** — There is no hosted CI and the human manages pushes themselves. The definition of "green on the repo host" for **every** step in this project reduces to: `make lint test check` plus `go vet`, `golangci-lint`, `gofumpt -l`, `go test ./...`, `govulncheck ./...` all pass **locally**. The GitHub Actions workflow was **removed 2026-07-11 at the human's request** (they don't use GitHub CI); the local-green DoD stands unchanged — these are the checks to run locally before a step is "done".
- **p04.1** — Versioned tables seed with full audit consistency: a migration that seeds a versioned business row also inserts its `changes` row (actor = system user 1, fixed epoch timestamp `'1970-01-01T00:00:00Z'`, `kind='seed'`) and its `*_versions` `op='create'` row (`valid_from == changes.at`), so Z3/Z5 hold uniformly with no seed special-casing. The `subsidiaries_versions` snapshot column set (`parent_id, name, base_currency, active, sort_order`) is documented in the migration; p04.2's `InsertSubsidiaryVersion` query must write exactly those. Single-root is enforced by a **pair** of triggers (BEFORE INSERT + BEFORE UPDATE): on INSERT the AUTOINCREMENT `NEW.id` is unassigned, so the guard checks plain existence of another root (an `id <> NEW.id` clause would compare against NULL and never fire); on UPDATE it excludes the row with `id <> NEW.id`. The **program root (p07.1)** gets the same seed-with-version + single-root-trigger-pair treatment. **Deferred instance:** the system user (seeded in 00002 before `users_versions` existed) has NO version row yet — when **p06.1** creates `users_versions`, that migration MUST backfill a `op='create'` version row for user id 1 (excluding `password_hash`, rule 5) or Z3 will flag `users`.
- **p04.2** — Version-append convention established concretely (the pattern p05/p07/p08 copy): inside the funnel's `fn`, the entity op does its LIVE write FIRST, then appends the version row via a **snapshot-from-live** query (`InsertSubsidiaryVersion` = `INSERT ... SELECT` from the just-written live row), so the version row is byte-identical to the live row (Z3 cannot diverge) and `valid_from == changes.at` **by construction** — both structural, never asserted. **All validation lives inside `fn`** (cycle/root/active-children checks read the tx-bound `*sqlc.Queries`), so a rejected op returns its error out of `fn` and the funnel rolls the change row back — rejected ops leave **no audit trace** (asserted by the blocked-op no-trace tests). Deactivate is `op='update'` (the entity persists), never `'delete'`. Op mapping: create→`create`, rename/move/base-currency/deactivate→`update`. **Tooling quirk:** sqlc v1.31.1 **miscounts byte offsets** when a query `.sql` file contains multi-byte UTF-8 (e.g. em-dashes in comments), silently corrupting the generated SQL constants for the *whole* file (not just the offending query). Keep every `.sql` query file **pure ASCII**. Also: sqlc's sqlite parser rejects `sqlc.arg()`/`@name` and mangles numbered `?N` params inside an `INSERT ... SELECT ... WHERE` form, so `InsertSubsidiaryVersion` uses plain positional `?` (each param used once: op, change_id, entity_id) — the store wraps the resulting `Op/ID/ID_2` field names behind one `insertSubsidiaryVersion` helper.
- **p05.2** — Account ops copy p04.2's funnel/version discipline with three deliberate departures. (1) **Composite-key versions:** `account_names`/`account_subsidiaries` version rows key on `(account_id, lang)` / `(account_id, subsidiary_id)`; their `InsertAccountNameVersion`/`InsertAccountSubsidiaryVersion` copy `InsertSubsidiaryVersion`'s snapshot-from-live shape, changing only the `entity_id`/WHERE. `testutil.AssertVersionedName`/`AssertVersionedSub` filter on the composite key (the single-id `AssertVersioned` stays for `accounts`). (2) **Removal inverts live-write-first:** a membership removal is `op='delete'` whose snapshot is the *last-known* membership, so `removeSub` inserts the version row **before** deleting the live row (an add keeps the normal live-first order). (3) **Subsidiary-set asymmetry (D18):** `parent set ⊇ union of children's` is over the **account tree**, not the subsidiary tree — assigning subsidiary `A1` to an account does **not** add `A1`'s subsidiary-tree ancestors; report scoping consolidates descendants at read time (D18). **Create propagates, move rejects (resolved asymmetry):** `CreateAccount`/`SetAccountSubsidiaries` **auto-propagate** an assigned sub UP the account-ancestor chain (each ancestor missing it gains a membership + `op='create'` version; an ancestor already holding it is a no-op with no version row); `UpdateAccount` moves **reject** with `ErrSubMismatch` when the new parent's set does not cover the mover's. Removing a sub is blocked while a **direct child** still maps it (`ErrSubInUseByChild`); the split-usage half of that guard is **deferred to p08** (no `splits` table yet) as a tagged `// TODO(p08)` + a documented test note. **Functional-class-on-non-expense** is rejected cleanly with a typed `ErrFunctionalClassNotExpense` before the trigger fires (Build text said "validate cleanly" but named no error). **990 type check** matches the account's `type` against `form990_lines.account_types` by **CSV membership** (some lines allow >1 type), not equality (`Err990TypeMismatch`). **`Effective990Codes` resolves the nearest-ancestor code IN GO** from a flat `(id, parent_id, own_code)` fetch: sqlc v1.31.1's sqlite analyzer cannot resolve a *carried* recursive-CTE column in the output projection (it reports the carried column "does not exist"), so a value-carrying downward CTE is not expressible — the in-memory walk over the small chart is the store-wrapped alternative.
- **p06.1** — Credentials/perms/settings on `users` + the auth primitive. **The invariant (rule 5):** `users_versions` has **no `password_hash` column** and `InsertUserVersion` (snapshot-from-live) selects every users column **except** it, while `CreateUser`'s live `InsertUser` **does** write the hash — that asymmetry is the whole step, proven by `TestUsersVersionOmitsPasswordHash` (PRAGMA table_info has no such column; a `SELECT *` scan of the latest version row finds the secret in no column; the live row does hold it). **System-user version backfill (the p04.1-deferred instance):** 00006 inserts `changes` id **2** (the only prior change is id 1, 00004's root-subsidiary seed; 00003/00005 seed none) and a `users_versions` `op='create'` row for user id 1 via `INSERT...SELECT` from the just-ALTERed live row (so the snapshot equals the post-ALTER defaults by construction and cannot drift), keeping Z3/Z5 uniform — without any hash. `AssertVersioned` needed no change (single-id entity). **`report_groups`** is code-synced reference data (D10), **not** versioned (no twin) and **unseeded** here — the startup sync fills it in p06.3. **`user_report_grants`** + its composite version twin (`entity_id=user_id`, snapshot `group_name`, like `account_subsidiaries`) are schema-only this step: grant writers/version-append land in p13.2, so grant FKs are exercised by **direct SQL** tests, not a store method. **argon2id (`internal/auth`, D9/D15, the ONLY place it is called):** `Hash`/`Verify` wrap `argon2id.DefaultParams` (v1.0.0): Memory 65536 KiB (64 MiB), Iterations 1, **Parallelism = `runtime.NumCPU()`** (machine-dependent — encoded into each PHC string, so verification is self-describing; a fixed value for reproducible cross-host cost is a one-line future tuning), SaltLength 16, KeyLength 32. **`go get github.com/alexedwards/argon2id`** (allowlisted D15, no extra ack needed) is the only new **direct** dep; it transitively pulls `golang.org/x/crypto` (also D15) as **indirect**. That brings govulncheck finding **GO-2026-5932** (`golang.org/x/crypto/openpgp` unmaintained; Fixed-in: N/A) as an **uncalled/informational** finding — govulncheck exits 0, "code affected by 0 vulnerabilities" — because cuento never imports that subpackage; it does **not** block the DoD. **sqlc regen note:** after 00006 widens `users`, `GetUser`'s explicit-column projection makes sqlc emit a bespoke `GetUserRow` (was `sqlc.User`); the fields it scans are unchanged so the existing `sqlc/users_changes_test.go` still compiles. `InsertUserVersion` uses the `INSERT...SELECT...WHERE` positional-`?` form (generated `Op/ID/ID_2`), wrapped behind `insertUserVersion` like the subsidiary/account helpers; `users.sql` kept pure ASCII.
- **p05.3** — `Tree`'s name resolution became a **COALESCE fallback chain requested-lang → en → any** (D14), replacing the p05.2 `LEFT JOIN ... COALESCE(an.name,'')` in **both** `AccountTree` and `AccountTreeBySubsidiary` (updating only one is the obvious latent bug; the test exercises both the nil-filter and subFilter paths). The chain is three **correlated subqueries** on `account_names` (requested lang, then `'en'`, then `ORDER BY lang LIMIT 1` for the deterministic "any"), with a trailing `''` so an account with no names at all still resolves to a value. Two sqlc v1.31.1 sqlite-analyzer quirks shaped the final SQL: (1) an unaliased `account_names` inside a correlated subquery that also references the outer `tree.id` makes the analyzer flag `lang`/`name` as **"column reference ambiguous"** — each subquery gets its own table alias (`an1`/`an2`/`anx`) with every column qualified; (2) a bare `COALESCE(<subqueries>, '')` is typed by sqlc as `interface{}` (not `string`), which would break the `TreeRow.Name string` mapping, so the whole expression is wrapped in `CAST(... AS TEXT)` to pin the generated column to `string`. No store-Go change was needed (the mapping is unchanged); the `AccountTreeBySubsidiaryParams` fields (`Lang`, `SubsidiaryID`) kept their names despite the param **order** flipping (lang now precedes subsidiary in the SQL), and the store uses named-field structs so the reorder is invisible. **Test-data deviation:** the "any" case needs an account with *neither* the requested lang *nor* `en`, but `CreateAccount` mandates an `en` name and there is no remove-name API — so the test raw-`DELETE`s the seeded `en` row from `account_names` after creation (raw SQL in store tests is already in-convention, e.g. `nameAsOf`). The task's "build with CreateAccount/SetAccountName" cannot otherwise reach the any-branch.
- **p06.2** — Web sessions + login + the security middleware spine every later web step inherits (D9, rule 13). **`Handler` signature changed** to `Handler(cfg web.Config, db *sql.DB, st *store.Store)` (Config carries `Version` + `Dev`); the p00.2 `Handler(version)` callers/tests were updated. `serve` now `db.Open`s after migrating (it needs the `*sql.DB` for both the store and the scs store) and gained a **`-dev`** flag (the Makefile `run` target already passed it). **Middleware chain (outer→inner, so headers wrap even deep errors and cross-origin rejects before any work):** `secureHeaders → crossOrigin (stdlib http.CrossOriginProtection) → scs LoadAndSave → auth (resolve current user from session id, re-read each request so perm/locale changes need no re-login; missing/disabled ⇒ anonymous, not error) → lang (user locale → ?lang query → lang cookie → en)`. **scs session table:** created by goose migration **00007** (`sessions(token TEXT PK, data BLOB NOT NULL, expiry REAL NOT NULL)` + `sessions_expiry_idx`) so goose stays canonical (rule 4) — NOT scs auto-create. Schema **verified against the installed library source** `github.com/alexedwards/scs/sqlite3store@v0.0.0-20251002162104-209de6e426de` (its `Find`/`Commit`/`Delete` raw SQL uses `token`/`data`/`expiry` with `expiry` a `julianday()` REAL; default table name `sessions`); matches the library README DDL exactly. `sessions` is scs-owned infra, **not** a versioned business table (no `_versions` twin, no `changes` wiring, no seed). **Cookie:** name `cuento_session`, `HttpOnly`, `SameSite=Lax`, `Path="/"`, `Secure = !Dev`, 12h Lifetime / 2h IdleTimeout. **Uniform auth error / no enumeration (rule 13):** unknown user, wrong password, AND disabled account all return the **same** 401 + identical body (`auth.invalid`). Timing is equalized too, not just the body: a fixed **decoy argon2id hash** (built once at startup via `auth.Hash`) is verified-and-discarded on the unknown-user / passwordless / DB-error paths so every attempt spends one argon2 verify regardless of whether the username exists. On success: `RenewToken` (session-fixation defense) then `Put(user_id)`. **CSP** (strict, no inline script, rule 12): `default-src 'self'; script-src 'self'; style-src 'self'; img-src 'self'; connect-src 'self'; font-src 'self'; object-src 'none'; base-uri 'none'; frame-ancestors 'none'; form-action 'self'` — plus `X-Content-Type-Options: nosniff`, `Referrer-Policy: same-origin`, `Cross-Origin-Opener-Policy: same-origin`, `X-Frame-Options: DENY`. HTML `no-store` is set by the HTML render path (`render`), NOT the header middleware, so `/static` + `/healthz` keep their own caching (p10 owns asset headers). **Rate limit** (`x/time/rate`): keyed by **IP+username**, burst 5, refill 1 token/30s, checked **before** any argon2 work (so throttling actually saves the hashing cost); over-limit ⇒ **429** with the login page + `auth.rate_limited`. Limiter map is bounded (cleared wholesale at 4096 keys — the simplest bound that only ever loosens, never locks out). Client IP = direct `RemoteAddr` only (never a spoofable forwarded header). **`{{t}}` per-request localization:** templates parse once with a stub `t`; `render` clones the set and rebinds `t` to a closure over the resolved lang before Execute (html/template's func map is what carries per-request state), so `?lang=es` renders the Spanish catalog. **New login keys** (`auth.login_title/username/password/sign_in/invalid/rate_limited`) added to BOTH catalogs (parity test stays green). **"Subsequent request authenticated" tested without p06.3 routes:** `GET /login` redirects (303) when identity resolves, so the success test asserts the cookie authenticates without mounting a throwaway route that p06.3's registry-completeness test would later reject. **Store reads added** (rule 2 permits reads via sqlc): `CredentialsByUsername` (`UserByUsername` query) and `UserByID` — both NEW queries; `GetUser` untouched (its projection is pinned by `sqlc/users_changes_test.go`). **Deps:** `scs/v2`, `scs/sqlite3store`, `x/time` added (all D15-allowlisted, no extra ack); `go mod tidy` flipped them direct. No non-allowlisted direct dep (sqlite3store's own test-only `mattn/go-sqlite3` is a go.sum build-list entry, not in our require graph). govulncheck exit 0 (the single uncalled `x/crypto/openpgp` GO-2026-5932 finding from p06.1 persists, informational). All `.sql`/migration files kept pure ASCII (p04.2 quirk).
- **p06.3** — The route registry + provable enforcement every later web step plugs into (rule 8, D10). **`Perm`** is a small value type (`{kind, group}`), not an interface, so `routes()` is a plain declarative table and the matrix switches on it exhaustively: markers `Public/AnyUser/TxnRead/TxnWrite/Admin` (package vars) + the `ReportGroup(name)` constructor (the only variant carrying data — a report route's Perm is its group, Appendix B). **`Route{Method, Pattern string; Perm; Handler http.Handler}`** — `http.Handler` not `http.HandlerFunc` so the static `FileServer` mounts without wrapping. **Single registry / single mount:** `(s *server).routes()` declares EVERY route (healthz/static/login GET+POST/logout migrated in from p06.2's manual `mux.HandleFunc` block, which is deleted) plus a minimal authenticated landing; `(s *server).Mount()` is the ONLY site a route attaches to a mux — it iterates `routes()`, wraps each handler in `enforce(perm, h)`, and wraps the whole mux in the p06.2 security `chain()` (so `auth` populates the current user before `enforce` reads it). `NewApp` now just calls `Mount()`. No route exists outside `Mount` — the "mux corresponds exactly to the registry" guarantee is **structural** (Go's `http.ServeMux` has no enumeration API), backed by the reachability + catch-all-404 checks. **Landing = `GET /{$}`** (exact-match anchor), deliberately NOT `GET /`: a bare `/` is a catch-all that swallows every unmatched GET and defeats `TestRouteRegistryComplete`'s unregistered-path-404 assertion. It renders `home.tmpl` (new i18n keys `home.title/home.welcome`, `auth.sign_out`, in BOTH catalogs — parity green). **Enforcement policy, encoded ONCE in the pure `decide(perm, user, hasGrant) outcome`** (D10, `is_admin` short-circuits everything before any perm/grant check): Public→everyone; else anon→`RedirectLogin`; then AnyUser→allow, TxnRead→`{read,write}`, TxnWrite→`write`, ReportGroup→`hasGrant(name)`, Admin→(non-admin already excluded); else `Forbid`. **The 302/303 split is load-bearing:** enforcement's anon→/login bounce uses **302** while every handler redirect (logout, already-authed `/login`) uses **303**, so the matrix's `Allow` check (`!=403 && !(302→/login)`) catches "authorized user wrongly bounced to login" yet lets logout's legit 303→/login pass — without the split, `Allow` could only be `!=403` and would miss that bug. **Grant resolution is lazy:** `grantChecker` queries `store.ReportGrants` ONLY for a `ReportGroup` route with a concrete user (anon/admin already decided; non-report perms never call it), so `authMiddleware`'s hot path (every request incl. /healthz, /static) never loads grants; a grant-read error **fails closed** (denies). Grants live on neither `CurrentUser` nor the session — resolved per-request. **Matrix auto-extends from the registry:** `TestPermissionMatrix` iterates `srv.routes()` (never a hardcoded list) × 6 personas and asserts the real handler's response `outcomeMatches` what `decide` computes from the route's Perm — so a route APPENDED to `routes.go` in p11+ is enforced-and-checked with zero test edits. `decide` is the single source of truth (no re-expressed expectations); `TestDecidePolicy` proves `decide` itself across all 6 Perms × 6 personas **including `ReportGroup`**, whose HTTP coverage waits for p15's report routes (the registry has none yet — "do not invent feature routes"). **Personas driven by SESSION INJECTION, not login** (task sanctions "inject the session/user"): `mintCookie` writes a fresh scs session row per request (`Put(user_id)` under the same key `authMiddleware` reads, `Commit`), so the matrix pays no argon2/rate-limit cost AND logout's `Destroy` can't contaminate later requests in the sweep (each carries its own token) — the route-outer/persona-inner loop would otherwise have logout blank every persona before `/{$}` is reached. **Report-group startup sync (D10):** `web.SyncReportGroups(ctx, st)` (the web package owns the code-declared set because route Perms reference the names) → `store.SyncReportGroups` does an **idempotent `UpsertReportGroup`** per name — OUTSIDE the write funnel, like currencies (`report_groups` is reference data, NOT versioned: no `changes`/`_versions` wiring, rule 2 permits reference upserts via sqlc). Wired into `serve` after `db.Open`, before listening; safe every boot; nothing is deleted (a vanished group keeps its FK). **Reversible choice recorded:** the code-declared set is a single placeholder `_placeholder` (`codeReportGroups()`) until p15 declares the real report groups — the mechanism is real, the content is a stub; `TestPermissionMatrix`'s ReportsOnly persona is granted it via **direct SQL** (grant writers land in p13.2; raw SQL in tests is in-convention, p05.3). **Store additions (reads/reference-upsert only, no funnel):** `ReportGrants(userID)` (new `ReportGrantsForUser` query) + `SyncReportGroups`/`UpsertReportGroup`; `report_groups.sql` kept pure ASCII. No new dependency (scs already direct from p06.2); `go.mod`/`go.sum` unchanged; govulncheck exit 0 (the p06.1 informational `x/crypto/openpgp` finding persists).
- **p06.4** — The `cuento user add|passwd|disable` CLI + the serve bootstrap hint. **Password input = one line from STDIN** (a prompt to stderr only when stdin is a char device; a piped line otherwise), NOT a `-password` flag: a flag leaks the secret into shell history/process args, while a stdin line works interactive AND scripted/tested. The factored funcs (`userAdd(ctx, st, username, display, admin, password)`, `userPasswd(ctx, st, username, password)`, `userDisable(ctx, st, username)`) take the password as a plain string so tests call them directly with a real migrated temp db, bypassing I/O; empty password rejected. **System actor bound INSIDE the factored funcs** (`store.WithActor(ctx, store.Actor{ID:1})`), not just in dispatch, so the guarantee holds for any caller and tests pass a plain `context.Background()`. **Two new versioned store methods**, both op='update', both reusing the EXISTING `insertUserVersion(..., "update", id)` snapshot-from-live helper so rule-5 hash exclusion is automatic (no new version query): `SetUserPassword` (live `UPDATE users SET password_hash` — the new secret enters only the live table; `TestSetUserPasswordVersionOmitsHash` proves the snapshot omits it) and `DisableUser` (live `UPDATE users SET disabled_at = now`; disabled_at IS in the snapshot so the audit trail records the disabling). New sqlc queries are plain `UPDATE`/`SELECT COUNT`/`SELECT id` (the p04.2 `INSERT...SELECT` numbered-param quirk does not apply); `users.sql` kept pure ASCII. Also added reads `UserIDByUsername` (passwd/disable take a username; a miss → typed `ErrUserNotFound`, a clean CLI message not a panic) and `CountHumanUsers` (`WHERE id <> 1`). **`user add` defaults:** `txn_perm='none'` (admins imply all, D10; per-perm management is the admin UI p13.2), `--display` falls back to the username. **Flag handling — interspersed parse (`parseInterspersed`):** stdlib `flag` stops at the first positional, so `user add carol --admin` silently dropped `--admin` and `user passwd frank -db /p` silently used the DEFAULT db (a silent wrong-target write); the loop re-parses around each positional so flags work in any position and a value-taking flag (`--display "Name"`) is never mistaken for the username. `parseUserAdd` is factored pure + unit-tested (`TestParseUserAddInterspersed`) to lock the regression — the end-to-end tests bypass the parser, so the `--admin` bug only bites at the flag layer. **Bootstrap hint:** `serve` calls `st.CountHumanUsers`; zero ⇒ `log.Printf` a pointer to `cuento user add <username> --admin`. It is operator-facing console output (same class as the existing serve log lines), NOT a UI string — no i18n catalog entry; a lookup error is non-fatal (never block startup on a hint). **Known pre-existing quirk (NOT p06.4, out of scope):** `db.Open` (p01.1) `url.PathEscape`s the path into the `file:` DSN, so an ABSOLUTE `-db /path` escapes `/`→`%2F` and modernc resolves it relative to cwd — harmless within one process (tests use absolute temp paths and pass because migrate+open share the cwd) but means cross-invocation `-db` with an absolute path is cwd-sensitive; the default db path works end to end. Not touched here (would mask a real p01.1 bug). No new dependency (bufio/flag/io are stdlib); `go.mod`/`go.sum` unchanged; `make lint test check` + govulncheck exit 0 (the p06.1 informational `x/crypto/openpgp` finding persists).
- **p07.1** — Programs (D24), the second single-root dimension, are structurally **subsidiaries MINUS base_currency**: `00008_programs.sql` copies 00004's shape — the live table, the `programs_versions` twin (snapshot cols `parent_id, name, active, sort_order`), the single-root **trigger pair** (BEFORE INSERT checks plain existence since AUTOINCREMENT `NEW.id` is NULL; BEFORE UPDATE excludes `id <> NEW.id`), and the **audit-consistent seed** of root "General" (id 1). The seed's `changes` row is **id 3** (id 1 = 00004 root-subsidiary seed, id 2 = 00006 system-user backfill; 00003/00005/00007 seed no change). **Distinct names throughout (package `store` and the sqlc query package are shared namespaces):** sqlc queries `InsertProgram/GetProgram/UpdateProgram/InsertProgramVersion/ProgramTree/ProgramDescendants/CountActiveProgramChildren` (NOT the subsidiary `SubTree/Descendants/CountActiveChildren`); `*Store` methods `ProgramTree()`/`ProgramDescendants(id)` (a `Descendants` method already exists); errors `ErrProgramSecondRoot/ErrProgramParentMissing/ErrProgramRootImmovable/ErrProgramHasActiveChildren/ErrProgramNotFound`. **`ErrCycle` is REUSED** (same meaning; accounts.go already does). Deactivate mirrors all four subsidiary reject paths incl. the active-children block — "blocks new use only" is the op='update'-not-'delete' *semantic* (history intact; the split-based blocks-new-use assertion is tagged for p08), not the absence of a children guard. **`default_program_id` accounts ripple (the correctness core):** 00008 `ALTER accounts ADD COLUMN default_program_id INTEGER REFERENCES programs(id)` (the column deferred from 00005) AND `ALTER accounts_versions ADD COLUMN default_program_id INTEGER` — the version snapshot must capture it or **Z3 (current == latest snapshot) diverges** for any account touched after p07.1. Four `accounts.sql` queries updated: `InsertAccount` (add param), `UpdateAccount` (add to SET), `InsertAccountVersion` (add to the snapshot SELECT), and `GetAccount` — the last projects `default_program_id` **LAST** to match the table's PHYSICAL column order (ADD COLUMN appends), so sqlc keeps mapping the result to the `sqlc.Account` model rather than emitting a bespoke `GetAccountRow` that `accounts.go`'s `GetAccount() (sqlc.Account, ...)` and `validateMove` depend on. **Silent-NULL regression guarded:** `UpdateAccount`/`DeactivateAccount` do read-modify-write; `next := cur` carries `cur.DefaultProgramID`, and every `UpdateAccountParams` literal (3 call sites) now maps `DefaultProgramID`, so an unrelated update never NULLs it — proven by `TestAccountDefaultProgramREOnly` (set on a revenue acct, update an unrelated field, assert both live + latest-snapshot still hold it). **Default-program R/E-only enforcement (D24):** `CreateAccount`/`UpdateAccount` take an optional `DefaultProgramID`; non-R/E → `ErrDefaultProgramNotRE` (checked early in Create before the tx); inside `fn`, `checkDefaultProgram` validates existence (`ErrDefaultProgramMissing`) and active (`ErrDefaultProgramInactive`) — **two error names beyond the task's `ErrDefaultProgramNotRE`**, the minimal split for "missing" vs "inactive". `UpdateAccount` treats a non-nil **0** as CLEAR (NULL), a positive value as set. All existing account/subsidiary tests still pass (the ripple is column-append-only; no test asserted a fixed accounts column count). Migration + `programs.sql` + `accounts.sql` kept pure ASCII (p04.2 byte-offset quirk applies to migrations too since sqlc reads them as schema). No new dependency; `go.mod`/`go.sum` unchanged; `make lint test check` + govulncheck exit 0 (the p06.1 informational `x/crypto/openpgp` finding persists).
- **p07.2** — Funds (D20), the restricted-fund split dimension, are schema-only this step (`00009_funds.sql`; store ops are p07.3). `funds` has the `restriction IN ('purpose','time','perpetual')` CHECK, `program_id -> programs(id)` FK (optional program-subtree scope), and **date GLOB CHECKs** on `start_date`/`end_date` (`IS NULL OR ... GLOB '[0-9][0-9][0-9][0-9]-[0-9][0-9]-[0-9][0-9]'`). `fund_subsidiaries(fund_id -> funds, subsidiary_id -> subsidiaries, PK (fund_id, subsidiary_id))` carries the scope; the **>=1-subsidiary minimum is store-enforced (p07.3), not a schema constraint**. **No seed row** (unrestricted = absent `fund_id`, D20; no "general fund"): so **no `changes` row and no seed version rows** this migration -- the last change id stays 3 (00008's program seed), and there is no seed-consistency test. **Two version twins:** `funds_versions` is the standard single-id shape (entity_id = fund id; snapshot cols `name, funder, purpose, restriction, program_id, start_date, end_date, notes, active`); `fund_subsidiaries_versions` is the **composite shape like `account_subsidiaries_versions`** (entity_id = fund_id, snapshot `subsidiary_id`, op create/delete for membership -- no 'update'; index `(entity_id, subsidiary_id, valid_from)`) -- documented in the migration for p07.3's `InsertFundVersion`/`InsertFundSubsidiaryVersion`. Both twins carry **no CHECK/FK on snapshot columns** (only `change_id -> changes`), matching `accounts_versions`: a snapshot records history, it does not re-validate it. **Deviation from the task's listed date test (AGENTS method-1):** the task listed `start_date='2025-13-99'` as a rejection sample, but the authoritative `transactions.date` GLOB (Appendix A) is **shape-only** (digit count + dashes), which the task also specified verbatim -- and `'2025-13-99'` matches that shape (month/day are still digits), so it is *accepted*. Rather than diverge from `transactions.date` (rule 4: migrations are truth; schema consistency), the loose pattern was kept and the rejection sample swapped for a shape-invalid string (`'2025-1-1'`, wrong digit count); `'not-a-date'` rejects, `'2025-01-01'`/NULL accepted. `make gen` regenerated only the four expected `sqlc` models (`Fund`, `FundSubsidiary`, `FundsVersion`, `FundSubsidiariesVersion`) -- sqlc parsed all CHECKs/GLOBs without error, no query files needed (direct-SQL tests). Migration + test kept pure ASCII (00008 convention). No new dependency; `go.mod`/`go.sum` unchanged; `make lint test check` + govulncheck exit 0 (the p06.1 informational `x/crypto/openpgp` finding persists).
- **pE.1** — The Playwright functional-test harness (`e2e/`, test-only; the "Functional testing" section above is the settled decision, this is the build note). **Pinned `@playwright/test@1.53.2`** — chosen *empirically*, not from memory: the pre-installed browser is `~/.cache/ms-playwright/chromium-1179`, and each candidate version's `node_modules/playwright-core/browsers.json` was read for its bundled `chromium.revision` until it matched **1179** (1.49.1→1148, 1.52.0→1169, 1.53.0→1178, **1.53.1/1.53.2→1179**, 1.54.0→1181). `npx playwright install --dry-run chromium` confirms 1.53.2 resolves to the cached `chromium-1179` (chromium 138.0.7204.23), so `npm ci` downloads **no** browser. Bump the pin only to another version whose bundled revision still matches a cached browser, else a browser download appears in `make e2e`. **Fixture design (`e2e/fixtures.js`, worker-scoped `server` fixture):** free port allocated in **Node** (listen on `127.0.0.1:0`, read the assigned port, close — NO Go change to resolve the port, per the task's preferred approach); a temp dir + db under `os.tmpdir()`; then `cuento migrate -db <db>`, `cuento user add e2eadmin --admin -db <db>` with the password piped on **stdin** (newline-terminated; the CLI reads one line), and `cuento serve -dev -db <db> -addr 127.0.0.1:<port>`; readiness by polling `GET /healthz` (Public, no auth) for 200; teardown SIGTERMs serve (SIGKILL after 5s) and removes the temp dir. **The p06.4 `db.Open` cwd-sensitivity quirk is handled structurally:** all three child processes (migrate / user add / serve) are spawned with the **same cwd (repo root) and the same `-db` value**, so `url.PathEscape` resolves them to one physical file — otherwise `user add` seeds a db that `serve` never opens and a correct password returns `auth.invalid`. `bin/cuento` is built **once** via `globalSetup` (`make build`, idempotent). **`login.spec.js` drives the REAL page** (`templates/login.tmpl`): selectors `#username` / `#password` / the submit `<button>`; the uniform error is `p[role="alert"]` (rendered `{{t .Error}}`, key `auth.invalid`). Three cases: wrong password → alert visible + still on `/login`; unknown user → same uniform error (no enumeration); valid `e2eadmin` creds → 303 to `/` (authenticated `home.tmpl` landing, no `#password` present). **Opt-in via `make e2e`** (builds the binary, `cd e2e && npm ci && npx playwright test`) — deliberately **OUT of `make test`** (which stays hermetic: no browser, no network per AGENTS). `e2e/node_modules`, `test-results`, `playwright-report`, caches gitignored (`e2e/.gitignore`); `package.json` + `package-lock.json` + config + specs + fixture committed. **No Go code touched, no Go dependency added** (Playwright is Node-only, D15 untouched); `go.mod`/`go.sum` unchanged; `make lint test check` + govulncheck exit 0 (the p06.1 informational `x/crypto/openpgp` finding persists). `npm audit` reports advisories in Playwright's own dependency tree — test-only, never shipped or imported by the binary/frontend (rule 12), so they do not bear on the Go build.
- **p07.3** — Fund store ops (`internal/store/funds.go`, D20). Copies the account composite-membership discipline (p05.2) but is **deliberately simpler**: `fund_subsidiaries` is a **FLAT set** (>=1, store-enforced by `ErrFundNoSubsidiary`) with **NO ancestor propagation and NO superset invariant** — there is no `addSubWithPropagation` analogue; `addFundSub` inserts a membership directly then versions it op='create' (live-write-first), and `removeFundSub` versions op='delete' **BEFORE** the live DELETE (the snapshot-from-live removal ordering, mirroring accounts). Both the fund row and every membership are written under **ONE** `write()` change (`TestCreateFundVersioned` asserts change count +1). **`UpdateFundInput.Subsidiaries` set-semantics (the choice):** nil = leave the set unchanged; a non-nil slice = the full DESIRED set, diffed against the current set (adds op='create', removes op='delete'), and an empty/deduped-empty desired set is rejected with `ErrFundNoSubsidiary` (>=1 must remain) — chosen over an add/remove-delta shape because desired-set matches the accounts `SetAccountSubsidiaries` idiom and makes "still >=1 after the change" a single check. **Program scope** reuses the accounts `*int64` convention (nil unchanged / non-nil 0 clears / positive sets) and is validated **existence-only** via the existing `GetProgram` (task: "must exist if set" — no active check, which would be untested gold-plating); a missing program is `ErrFundProgramMissing`. **p08-deferred split guards (NOT silently skipped):** `UpdateFund` carries a `// TODO(p08)` before each membership removal (block removing subsidiary S while splits reference the fund in S — splits table absent until p08.1); `TestNarrowSubsBlockedBySplits` is `t.Skip`-tagged with the matching TODO, and `TestCloseFundBlocksNewUse` is tagged (the post-time block is p08) but asserts the close is versioned + active=0 now. **`CloseFund`/`ReopenFund`** are op='update' (never 'delete', rule 14) sharing a `setFundActive` body. **`ActiveFunds(subsidiaryID)`** JOINs funds+fund_subsidiaries filtered by `active=1 AND subsidiary_id=?`, `ORDER BY funds.id` (deterministic option source, D20/Q1). **Deviation from the listed test set (AGENTS method-1):** the task/PLAN listed `TestCreateRequiresAtLeastOneSub`, but p05.2 (accounts) already declared that exact name in the shared `store` package — renamed to `TestCreateFundRequiresAtLeastOneSub` (a compile-forced disambiguation; the DoD requires distinct names). `testutil.AssertVersionedFundSub` added (mirrors `AssertVersionedSub`, filters `entity_id=fund_id AND subsidiary_id`). `funds.sql` pure ASCII; generated version params wrapped behind `insertFundVersion` (`Op/ID/ID_2`) and the composite membership helpers (`Op/ID/FundID/SubsidiaryID`). No new dependency; `go.mod`/`go.sum` unchanged; `make gen` reproducible, `make lint test check` + govulncheck exit 0 (the p06.1 informational `x/crypto/openpgp` finding persists).
- **p08.2** — Transaction post/update/delete (`internal/store/transactions.go`, D2/D18/D20/D21/D24) — the CORE financial logic. **Validate-on-tx-bound-q (the TOCTOU close):** all validation runs inside the funnel's `fn` on the tx-bound `*sqlc.Queries` the funnel passes, NOT on `s.q` before `write()`. `validateAndResolve` loads currency/subsidiary/accounts/funds/programs on the SAME tx that inserts, so an account deactivated or a fund closed between validate and insert cannot slip through. **Shared validate+resolve for Post AND Update:** one function returns `[]resolvedSplit` (program/functional class DEFAULTED before insert so the triggers never fire on the happy path); Update diffs RESOLVED values (not raw input) against the live split — an omitted-but-already-defaulted program/class counts as *unchanged* and gets no version row (the subtle `TestUpdateDiffsSplits` trap: a naive raw-input or re-version-everything diff passes balance tests but fails the per-split version-row COUNT assertion). **Two-tier zero-sum + error order:** overall sum==0 is checked FIRST (`ErrUnbalanced`), THEN per-fund-group sum==0 (`ErrFundUnbalanced`, NULL fund_id = the single "unrestricted" group, handled explicitly in a Go map keyed by 0). Per-fund-zero implies overall-zero, so overall must trip first or the two errors are indistinguishable; the two imbalance fixtures reach distinct errors. **Program-vs-function defaulting asymmetry (D24 vs D21):** program ALWAYS resolves for an R/E split (input -> account `default_program_id` -> **root program looked up by `parent_id IS NULL`**, never hardcoded id 1) then must be active (`ErrInactiveProgram`); A/L/E splits must carry no program (`ErrProgramOnBalanceSheet`). Functional class CAN fail: an expense split with no class and a NULL account default raises `ErrExpenseNeedsFunction` (p05.1's trigger bans class on non-expense but does NOT require it on expense, so an expense account can have a NULL default — this typed error, not the trigger, is the real content of `TestPostExpenseRequiresFunction`); a non-expense split with a class -> `ErrNonExpenseFunction`. Fund-program subtree scope (`ErrFundProgramScope`) applies to **R/E splits only** (the A/L/E cash side tagged the fund carries no program and is fine); the subtree membership is resolved in Go from `ProgramSubtreeIDs` (sqlc's sqlite analyzer rejects a recursive-CTE alias in an outer EXISTS/WHERE — same limitation as `Effective990Codes`). **Update-diff rule:** replace-set by split id — present&changed -> live update + `splits_versions` op='update'; present&identical -> NO version row; existing-but-absent -> live DELETE + op='delete' (captured BEFORE the delete, snapshot-from-live removal order); no id -> insert + op='create'. The txn header ALWAYS gets an op='update' version on an edit (the change row anchors the edit; keeps the header as-of a clean LIMIT-1 lookup) — a consciously-chosen consistency point. **Soft-delete (rule 14):** `DeleteTransaction` sets `deleted=1` + ONE `transactions_versions` op='delete'; splits are left untouched (no split delete-versions) — the as-of query excludes the txn by its own delete row. **As-of reconstruction (D4/D5):** `TransactionAsOf(id, at)` reads the header via `TransactionVersionAsOf` (latest `valid_from<=at`, absent/excluded if op='delete') and the split SET via `SplitVersionsAsOf` (all split versions for the txn with `valid_from<=at`, ordered `entity_id, valid_from DESC, id DESC`), then takes the FIRST row per `entity_id` in Go (dropping op='delete') — resolved in Go, like `Effective990Codes`, so every SQL param is single-use (avoiding the p04.2 numbered-param quirk on reusing `at`). Tiebreak matches `AssertVersioned`. `TestTransactionAsOf` uses `WithClock` (post@T0, edit1@T1, edit2@T2) and asserts the reconstructed split SET membership AND each split's values at the middle state. **Date validation:** the schema GLOB is shape-only, so the store parses the date with `time.Parse("2006-01-02")` and round-trips it (rejects `2025-13-99` etc. with `ErrBadDate`) before insert. **Completed p08 guards (grep `TODO(p08)` in `internal/` now CLEAN):** `SetAccountSubsidiaries` (accounts.go) blocks removing sub S from account A while `SplitUsesAccountInSubsidiary` finds a split on A in a non-deleted txn of S (`ErrSubInUseByChild` extended); `UpdateFund` (funds.go) blocks removing S from fund F while `SplitUsesFundInSubsidiary` finds a split tagged F in a non-deleted txn of S (new `ErrFundSubInUseBySplit`). `TestNarrowSubsBlockedBySplits` un-skipped; the split half of `TestRemoveSubBlockedByChildOrSplits` un-skipped (via `testRemoveSubBlockedBySplit`). **Concurrency finding: PASSES AS-IS, no `BEGIN IMMEDIATE` needed.** Verified: `db.Open` sets `MaxOpenConns(4)` (genuine overlap possible, not a trivially-serial pool of 1) + WAL + `busy_timeout` 5000ms; the funnel writes the `changes` row FIRST with no in-tx read before it (store.go), so concurrent posters serialize on the first write via WAL's single-writer + busy_timeout rather than deadlocking read-then-write. `TestConcurrentPostsSerialize` (8 goroutines, channel barrier) is green under `-race -count=5` with distinct change ids and no "database is locked". **Minimal payee support:** `CreatePayee(name)` (versioned op='create'); payee_id optional on the txn (autocomplete is p12.3). **Currency-active** has a named requirement but no listed test — smallest choice `ErrInactiveCurrency`, no bespoke test added. `transactions.sql` pure ASCII; version-append params wrapped behind `insertTransactionVersion`/`insertSplitVersion`/`InsertPayeeVersion` (`Op/ID/ID_2`). No new dependency; `go.mod`/`go.sum` unchanged; `make gen` reproducible, `make lint test check` + govulncheck exit 0 (the p06.1 informational `x/crypto/openpgp` finding persists).
- **p08.3** — The integrity suite (`internal/ledger`, `cuento check`), AGENTS rule 7's "verified by cuento check" half. **Structure:** `Check(ctx, db) ([]Violation, error)` runs a reviewed registry `[]check{Rule, Severity, SQL}` (in `checks.go`) of **const SQL strings** — the ONE sanctioned exception to sqlc-only (rule 6), static and reviewed here as a set. Every check SQL returns exactly ONE text column (a detail naming offending ids) and one row per violation; no rows == passed. `Violation{Rule, Severity(Error|Warning), Detail}`; `HasErrors` drives the exit code. **Rules implemented now:** Z1 (txn sums to 0), Z2 (splits on leaves), Z3 (current == latest version snapshot, ALL versioned tables incl. composite `account_names`/`account_subsidiaries`/`fund_subsidiaries` and a dangling-membership branch), Z4 (`pragma_foreign_key_check()` table-valued fn — the modernc driver supports it), Z5 (every `*_versions.change_id` -> real change, all 12 twins incl. `user_report_grants_versions`), Z6 (orphan splits), Z7 (account tree acyclic, bounded upward walk), Z10 (per-fund-group zero-sum, NULL=unrestricted via `COALESCE(fund_id,-1)`), Z11 (split account mapped to txn sub), Z12 (parent sub-set superset of children), Z13 (fund scoped to txn sub), Z14 (functional_class iff expense), Z15 (program iff R/E + inside fund's program subtree when both set, subtree via recursive CTE in `NOT IN`), Z16 (subsidiary+program trees acyclic AND exactly one root each), Z17 (warning: intercompany accounts net 0 per currency), Z18 (warning: negative restricted-fund balance), Z19 (warning: active R/E leaf with activity lacking an effective 990 code, nearest-ancestor via recursive CTE). **Z8/Z9 DEFERRED to p16.1** (they reference `reconciliations`/`splits.reconciliation_id`, absent until p16.1): kept in the registry as clearly-marked placeholders whose SQL is `sqlDeferred` (`SELECT '' WHERE 0`, always zero rows) + a `// TODO(p16.1)` — so the numbering/registry is stable and p16.1 is a pure fill-in; NO reconciliation checks were invented against absent tables. **Z18 SIGN SENSE (the one recorded design choice):** the task's literal "sum of ALL split amounts per (fund,currency)" is **provably vacuous** — Z10 forces every txn to net zero WITHIN each fund group, so the total is ALWAYS 0 on Z10-clean data and could only go negative when Z10 already fired, never independently surfacing the D23 overspend. So Z18 tracks the fund's **cash/asset balance** instead (the task's own clarifying clause, "a restricted-fund cash/asset balance going negative is the flag"): net-debit `SUM(amount) < 0` over the fund's splits **on ASSET accounts**, per currency. Because the whole fund nets to zero, that asset sum equals unexpended restricted resources; it goes negative exactly on "receive 50k then spend 90k" (each txn fund-balanced) — the genuine overspend. Non-expense applications (building purchase, loan principal) move between assets and never false-positive. Proven by a store-built (not tampered) `TestZ18NegativeRestrictedFund` that raises Z18 with **zero Error violations**. **CLI (`cuento check [-db PATH] [--strict]`):** opens the db (reads only), runs `Check`, prints violations `SEVERITY RULE: detail` in a deterministic order (errors first, then rule, then detail) + a summary; exit logic factored into the pure, unit-tested `checkExitCode(vs, strict)`: **1 on any Error always; 1 on any Warning too under --strict; 0 otherwise** (a deliberate non-zero exit rides up via an `exitError{code}` that `main` unwraps with `errors.As`, so violations print without a spurious `log.Fatalf` line). **make check WIRED** (stub replaced): `check: build`, then a FRESH `mktemp` db is migrated and `cuento check`ed — an empty migrated db (seeded roots, no splits) must be CLEAN (exit 0); the temp db is trapped-and-removed (hermetic). `fixtures/sample.db` is p09.3 and gitignored, so the default does NOT depend on it — but if it happens to exist locally, `make check` also runs `cuento check --strict` on it. **Tests-first (observed):** with `Check` temporarily neutered to return nil, all 21 negative/warning tests failed for the right reason ("want rule ZN flagged; got rules []" — detection missing) while the two clean-pass tests passed; restoring `Check` turned every test green. Negative tests corrupt a THROWAWAY copy with raw SQL, dropping the guarding trigger where one blocks the corruption (a `dropTriggers` helper; the task sanctions bypassing triggers on a throwaway db) — Z2/Z14/Z15-presence/Z16-root need a trigger dropped, Z4 uses a bad `transaction_id` on a valid leaf so no trigger fires. **Warning tests build their condition THROUGH the store** (not by tampering) so no Error rule (esp. Z3) cascades — Z17 posts a one-sided intercompany leg, Z18 a store-valid overspend, Z19 a store-valid uncoded expense leaf with a posted txn. No new dependency; `go.mod`/`go.sum` unchanged; `make lint test check` + govulncheck exit 0 (the p06.1 informational `x/crypto/openpgp` finding persists).
- **p08.4** — Balance queries (`internal/store/balances.go` + `internal/db/queries/balances.sql`), the READ-ONLY backbone for registers/fund pages/program pages/reports (Appendix E over these, p15.2). Six store methods: `SubtreeBalancesAsOf`, `PeriodActivity`, `FundBalancesAsOf`, `FunctionalActivity`, `ProgramActivity`, `RegisterPage`. **Scope-closure (D18):** each scoped aggregate closes the subsidiary descendant set with an inline `WITH RECURSIVE scope(id)` (base = the scope sub itself, so a leaf scopes to just itself) and joins `t.subsidiary_id IN (SELECT id FROM scope)`. sqlc v1.31.1 DOES accept a recursive CTE referenced in an outer `WHERE ... IN (subquery)` (verified by `make gen`) — the Go-side per-sub merge fallback was NOT needed (this is a NARROWER limitation than p08.2's "recursive-CTE alias in an outer EXISTS/WHERE" note: an `IN (SELECT id FROM cte)` subquery resolves; a bare CTE-alias column in the outer clause does not — see RegisterPage). **Money stays int64 (rule 3):** sqlc types a bare `SUM()`/`SUM() OVER()` as `sql.NullFloat64` (REAL) — every aggregate is wrapped `CAST(... AS INTEGER)` so the generated column is `int64` and no float ever touches money (SQLite returns the exact integer sum at runtime; the CAST only pins the static type). **Unrestricted fund (D20):** represented as **fund id 0** via `COALESCE(sp.fund_id, 0)` (the generated `FundID` is a non-null `int64`), matching Appendix E's zero-FundID convention that p15.2 builds on. **`FundBalancesAsOf` is ASSET-side only (recorded design choice, Z18 precedent):** a sum over ALL of a fund's splits is IDENTICALLY zero for every (fund, currency) — every txn nets to zero within each fund group (D20/Z10) and scoping/date filter whole transactions, so the total measures nothing. Restricting the join to `accounts.type = 'asset'` yields the fund's cash/asset position = unexpended restricted resources (grant received then partly spent shows the remainder), the same reasoning as p08.3's Z18. `FunctionalActivity`/`ProgramActivity` do NOT have this problem: their `functional_class IS NOT NULL` / `program_id IS NOT NULL` filters keep only the one-sided expense/R-E leg (present iff expense/R-E, D21/D24), dropping the balancing cash counterpart, so the sum is non-zero and meaningful. **`RegisterPage` window + keyset:** the running balance is a SQL window `CAST(SUM(amount) OVER (PARTITION BY currency ORDER BY date, split_id ROWS UNBOUNDED PRECEDING) AS INTEGER)` (per-currency: one account is usually single-currency but FX Clearing is multi). Total order `(date, split_id)` throughout (split id is globally unique + monotonic, so no txn-id tiebreak needed) — window ORDER, final ORDER BY, and cursor tuple all IDENTICAL. **KEYSET PAGING IS APPLIED IN GO, not SQL:** the window must see the WHOLE filtered set before the cursor cuts a page (else page 2's running balance restarts); but sqlc resolves a windowed-CTE's DERIVED columns only in a terminal SELECT/ORDER BY projection — it REJECTS them in an outer `WHERE` (verified: two-CTE and qualified-alias forms both fail `column "split_id" does not exist`). So the query returns the full filtered/windowed/ordered set and the store seeks past the cursor + takes `limit+1` rows in Go (the sanctioned "post-process in Go where sqlc can't express the construct"). The window still runs in SQL over the whole set, so the running balance is exact and continues across pages (tested: page-2 first-row running continues page-1's last, not restart). `RegisterPage(account, cursor, filters, limit)` returns `(page []RegisterRow, next RegisterCursor, hasMore bool, err error)`; `limit <= 0` = single page of everything after the cursor. **Optional filters (date range, free text on txn/split memo + payee, fund, subsidiary, program) via `(? = 0 OR col = ?)` pairs:** each filter binds a 1/0 active flag AND the compared value as TWO positional `?` (the `?N`/`@name` reuse form is mangled by sqlc's sqlite parser, p04.2 quirk), so the store passes each filter value twice (text three times: txn memo, split memo, payee name); an inactive filter short-circuits on `? = 0`. **Tests-first (observed):** with all six method bodies neutered to `return nil, ...`, all 10 balance tests failed for the right reason (assertion failures "cell N/CCY missing" / "page = 0 rows, want K" — the small hand-computed dataset built through the store fine, only the reads returned empty); restoring the bodies turned every test green. The dataset is a root + 2 child subs, 2 asset + 1 revenue + 1 expense account, a grant fund + unrestricted, root + educ programs, 6 non-deleted transactions across dates/subs/funds/programs/currencies (USD + MXN, one multi-currency FX-clearing account) plus a **7th soft-deleted** transaction asserted excluded from every method. Reused accounts.go's `nullInt64Ptr`/`nullStringToPtr` and added the int64 inverse `nullInt64ToPtr`. `balances.sql` pure ASCII (p04.2). No new dependency; `go.mod`/`go.sum` unchanged; `make gen` reproducible, `make lint test check` + govulncheck exit 0 (the p06.1 informational `x/crypto/openpgp` finding persists).
- **p08.5** — Account merge (`internal/store/merge.go` + two queries in `transactions.sql`). `MergeAccount(ctx, src, dst)` folds a source leaf into a destination leaf under **ONE** `write()` change (one `changes` row anchors every version row — `TestMergeRepointsSplitsAndRecons` asserts change count +1). **Validations (all on the tx-bound `q`, p08.2 TOCTOU discipline; typed sentinels):** `src == dst` → `ErrMergeSelf` (checked before the tx); src is a leaf (`AccountIsLeaf`) → else `ErrMergeNotLeaf`; dst is a leaf → else `ErrMergeIntoPlaceholder` (two distinct errors for the two accounts); dst active → else `ErrMergeIntoInactive`; **STRICT `src.Type == dst.Type`** → else `ErrMergeCrossTypeClass`; dst's subsidiary set ⊇ src's (via `subSet`, mirroring `validateMove`) → else `ErrMergeSubsetSubs`. **"same type" vs "type-class" reconciliation (the recorded choice):** the step body says "same type", PLAN p08.5 says "same type-class" — they diverge only for revenue↔expense (which `typeCompatible` treats as compatible). Merge uses **strict type equality**, NOT `typeCompatible`, because splits are repointed **snapshot-from-live with no re-defaulting**: a revenue split (functional_class NULL, program set) moved onto an expense account, or an expense split onto a revenue account, is an **invalid split** — `trg_splits_function_matches_type_update` / `trg_splits_program_matches_type_update` fire on the repoint UPDATE (verified they exist BEFORE UPDATE in 00010) and Z14/Z15 would flag it. Strict equality is both the safe reading and the correct one; no listed success test needs a cross-type merge. **Repoint mechanics:** `SplitIdsByAccount(src)` captures the split ids **FIRST** (before any write — after the first repoint a `WHERE account_id` lookup would confuse moved splits with dst's pre-existing ones); then per id `RepointSplitAccount(dst, id)` (live `UPDATE splits SET account_id`) followed by `insertSplitVersion(..., "update", id)` — snapshot-from-live AFTER the update, so the new op='update' snapshot records `account_id = dst`. `SplitIdsByAccount` is **NOT** filtered by `transactions.deleted` ("every splits row" moves, so src ends fully clear and Z2 sees no split stranded on the deactivated source — a soft-deleted txn's split moves too). Only src's captured splits get op='update' rows; **dst's existing splits are never versioned**. **Append-only audit (rule 5/14, D4):** the pre-merge op='create' split versions (account_id=src) are left UNTOUCHED — that is what keeps as-of history intact (`TestMergeHistoryIntact`: `TransactionAsOf` at a time BEFORE the merge still shows the split on src, after shows dst; ordered create@T0 < merge via an injected `WithClock`). **Deactivate src** inline (`active=0`, op='update', every other column carried through) — NOT via the public `DeactivateAccount` (which would open its own change), so it rides the SAME merge change. **dst is NEVER written** — its functional default / default program / 990 code are trivially kept (`TestMergeFunctionDefaultKept` compares the full dst row before/after). **Reconciliations repointing is DEFERRED to p16.1** — the `reconciliations` table and `splits.reconciliation_id` do not exist yet (p16.1); a `// TODO(p16.1): repoint reconciliations from src to dst` marks exactly where it belongs (right after the split repoint), the merge doc-comment notes it, and `TestMergeRepointsSplitsAndRecons` carries the same TODO — it asserts the **splits** repointing now, the recon half is tagged for p16. Each Blocked test satisfies every OTHER constraint so only the target error fires. **Tests-first (observed):** a stub `MergeAccount` returning `ErrMergeNotImplemented` (rather than a no-op, which would falsely pass `TestMergeFunctionDefaultKept`) made all six tests fail on behavior — the Blocked tests on "want ErrMergeX; got not-implemented", the others on the merge call erroring; implementing turned all six green. Two new queries (`SplitIdsByAccount :many`, `RepointSplitAccount :exec`) pure ASCII, positional `?`; `make gen` reproducible. No new dependency; `go.mod`/`go.sum` unchanged; `make lint test check` + govulncheck exit 0 (the p06.1 informational `x/crypto/openpgp` finding persists).
- **p09.1** — The canonical synthetic fixture (Appendix D), the one dataset CI/goldens/integrity tests use (real data never enters, rule 11). **Package placement is a recorded deviation from the step text.** PLAN says "in `internal/testutil/`", but that is **impossible without breaking store's tests**: `internal/store`'s tests are `package store` (internal) and import `testutil` for `NewDB`/`AssertVersioned`; the moment `testutil` imports `store` (which the fixture needs), the store test binary becomes `store(test) → testutil → store`, an import cycle Go forbids for internal test packages. So the store-importing builder lives in a leaf subpackage **`internal/testutil/fixture`** (`fixture.New(t) *Fixture` with `DB`/`Store`/`IDs`/`Expected`); `internal/testutil` stays store-free. Moving `NewDB`/`AssertVersioned` out to break the cycle the other way would touch every store test — the subpackage is the smallest reversible choice. **Root rename, not a second root (single-root trigger):** `New` renames the seeded root subsidiary (id 1, "Organization") to "Rio Verde Internacional" via `UpdateSubsidiary` (an update version row), then `CreateSubsidiary` adds "RV Estados Unidos" (USD) and "RV Mexico" (MXN); root program "General" (id 1) gains children Educacion + Food Pantry. **23 accounts** (2 placeholder parents Revenue/Expenses + 21 natural leaves), 2 funds (Beca Agua 2025 scoped {MX,US} program Educacion; Building Fund scoped {US}), **29 transactions (28 non-deleted, 63 splits)** 2025-01→2026-06. **The three warning-trap decisions (the fixture must trip EXACTLY Z19):** (1) **Z19 = one leaf.** Event Income is the deliberately-unmapped active R/E leaf — the Revenue placeholder parent carries NO 990 code and Event Income none, so it inherits nothing (Unmapped bucket); its three siblings carry own codes (Contributions VIII.1f, Government Grants VIII.1e, Program Service Fees VIII.2). The Expenses parent DOES carry IX.24e so every expense leaf inherits it (none unmapped), with Bank Fees overriding to IX.11g (the leaf-override for `Effective990Codes`) and Salaries own IX.7, Occupancy own IX.16. Event Income is posted activity (gala tickets) so Z19 fires; asserted by id in the test. (2) **Z18 stays silent:** Z18 is per-(fund,currency) asset-side, so the USD "multi-sub scope" spend in RV Estados Unidos against Beca Agua would drive the fund's USD asset balance negative — a small USD Beca Agua receipt in the US sub (2,000.00) precedes it, keeping the USD asset balance non-negative. (3) **Z17 stays silent / D3 single-currency:** both Due-from/Due-to are USD, so the intercompany pair is modelled entirely in **USD equal-and-opposite** — the MX child leg's USD debit lands on FX Clearing (the only USD-capable MX account besides Due-to), keeping each leg single-currency while the flagged accounts net zero per currency. **Deferrals (tables absent — NOT built):** `exchange_rates` is p14 (every exported aggregate is native-currency, no conversion) and the finalized 2026-05-31 Checking US reconciliation is p16; both have documented **no-op seam methods** (`(*Fixture).ExtendRates`/`ExtendReconciliation`) so p14/p16 slot in without reshaping `New`, and the transactions are designed so the reconciliation can be added later without renumbering (Checking US carries restricted + unrestricted splits and leaves two 2026 uncleared items). **Exported aggregates are an out-of-band hand tally, not query-reversed:** `Expected` (in expected.go) captures per-sub trial-balance-zero-per-currency, specific account balances, fund balances (incl. unrestricted fund id 0), functional-matrix cells, per-program activity, effective-990 rollups (incl. the Unmapped bucket, code ""), and intercompany-net-zero — computed independently from the transaction amounts (a separate tally proving per-fund zero-sum and per-sub trial-balance-zero), so `TestFixtureKnownAggregates` genuinely validates the p08.4 queries rather than comparing a query to itself. **Deterministic monotonic clock** (`store.WithClock` advancing 1s per change from a fixed base) gives every change row a distinct increasing timestamp, so the twice-edited transaction (fund + program changed across edits) has orderable versions for later as-of tests. **Tests-first (observed):** with `build` stubbed to skip the transaction posts, both tests failed on assertion MISMATCH (empty ledger's balances/funds/functional/program cells absent, no Z19 activity) — not undefined symbols; restoring the posts turned both green. `ledger.Check` on the fixture: **0 Error violations, exactly 1 Warning (Z19 naming Event Income)**. No new dependency; `go.mod`/`go.sum` unchanged; `make gen` reproducible, `make lint test check` + govulncheck exit 0 (the p06.1 informational `x/crypto/openpgp` finding persists).
- **p09.3** — `cmd/ledgerimport` (LOCAL-ONLY, never deployed) converts the cleaned full-ledger export (docs/ledger-export.md) into a cuento db by DRIVING `internal/store` (rule 2/7 -- every produced row is validated by the same invariants; the importer opens no tx and writes no SQL of its own). **Mapping format is CSV + JSON, NOT YAML (the one recorded design substitution):** PLAN/D22/D26 say "mapping.yaml", but rule 1 / D15 forbid a yaml dependency. Two stdlib-parseable files carry the same information: an **account-mapping CSV** (`encoding/csv`) -- one reviewable row per distinct source account (`source_acct, cuento_type, cuento_parent, subsidiaries(;-sep), functional_class_default, default_program, form990_code, name_en, name_es`) -- and a **global config JSON** (`encoding/json`, `DisallowUnknownFields` so a mapping typo fails review loudly) carrying the subsidiary tree (country->{name,base_currency}), program tree (kat->name), fund derivation (donor->{name,funder,purpose,restriction,subsidiaries,program}), functional-class map (kls->program|management|fundraising), base/FX-clearing/opening-balance account names, and row filters (skip_countries, opening_balance_typs). This is a within-allowlist substitution, no `go.mod` change. **Two subcommands, cores factored to take `io.Reader`/`io.Writer`/`*store.Store` so tests drive them with SYNTHETIC content (rule 11 -- the real `fixtures/source/` file is opened only at RUNTIME by the CLI wrapper in `main.go`, never in a test; I never read it):** `runAccounts` collects distinct source accounts (union of every `country` they appear under -> subsidiaries; `stmt` A/L/I/E/O -> type; `parent` -> cuento_parent; `kls`/`kat` best-guesses) and emits the reviewable skeleton; `runBuild` renames the seeded root subsidiary (id 1) + creates children (single-root trigger, never a 2nd root), creates programs under seeded root "General" (id 1), funds, the account tree (topo-sorted parent-before-child), payees, and transactions grouped by `tid`. **Amounts are exact (rule 3, the doc's core hazard #2):** `NetDebit = money.Parse(db) - money.Parse(cr)` over the AUTHORITATIVE `db`/`cr` columns with `money.NumberPlain` (dot-decimal), NEVER `ndb`/`fndb`/`v` (float-subtraction noise) and NEVER `ParseFloat` -- a blank amount side maps to 0 (money.Parse rejects ""); a zero net-debit split is dropped (the `amount <> 0` CHECK). Exponents come from `store.Currencies` (D1), not hardcoded. **FX-clearing decomposition (D3, hazard #1):** a `tid` group is bucketed by split `currency`; each single-currency bucket is posted as its OWN transaction, its residual (splits don't net to zero within the currency) balanced by a counter-leg on the configured **FX Clearing** account so each leg independently sums to zero. Both legs' amounts come from the source **authoritative db/cr** (via `NetDebit`); **`xrt` is NOT used for amounts** -- computing a leg from a 6-dp float rate would reintroduce exactly the float noise rule 3 forbids, so the source's own two currency legs stand as the exact amounts. **Counter-legs are computed PER FUND, not just per currency (the load-bearing correctness point):** the store enforces zero-sum WITHIN EACH FUND GROUP (D20/Z10), so a bucket's residual is grouped by `fund_id` (NULL = the unrestricted group) and one FX-Clearing counter-leg is emitted per fund with a nonzero residual, CARRYING that fund -- a per-currency-only counter-leg would net a restricted fund group nonzero and the store would reject the whole transaction (a cross-currency grant is exactly this case; asserted by a restricted multi-currency tid in `TestImportedBooksBalance`). FX Clearing is equity, so a fund-tagged counter-leg needs no program (A/L/E carry none). A single-currency group posts directly. **Opening balances (D22, hazard #8):** a group whose `typ` is in `opening_balance_typs` routes its residual to the per-subsidiary `Equity:Opening Balances` account. **Non-balancing groups are SURFACED, never force-balanced (hazard #4):** a genuine single-currency imbalance routes the residual to Opening Balances AND appends a `BuildResult.Warnings` line; if the store still rejects a group (`ErrUnbalanced`/`ErrFundUnbalanced`), the import catches it, warns, and CONTINUES -- amounts are never nudged onto an existing split. `main.go`'s `build` runs `ledger.Check` on the produced db and exits non-zero on any Error (the D26 rehearsal gate). **Payee source is configurable (`Config.PayeeColumn`, default "" = no payees):** the task's "payee-ish column as configured" -- `desc` (the multi-line memo) would mint thousands of junk payees on real data, so which column feeds the payee is a p09.4 tuning knob;
