  - **CONVERSION: NONE — native, per-currency rows (like the sibling p15.8/p15.9 activity reports).** `ProgramActivity(..., RateNone)`. A program is a mission/management dimension read in the money each grant/spend occurred in; the 990 preparer (Part III) wants native figures, and native makes hand-verification direct against the native oracle. (`ProgramActivity`'s convert path is RateClosing, so a converted variant is deliberately NOT used here.)
  - **RECONCILIATION — two distinct checks (do NOT sum the rolled columns; that double-counts, since General already contains its children).** (a) **Tree rollup:** the rolled cells match `ProgramActivity` / the General-column vertical net == total R/E per currency == p15.9 `chTotal`. (b) **Sum-across-programs == total R/E** is asserted at the **RAW partition** (General-direct + Educación + Food Pantry from the non-rolled oracle): USD net-debit −3,567,500, MXN −9,140,000. Both proven explicitly, not left to `checkGolden`.
  - **DRILL wiring + a new `Drill.ProgramIDs` program-SET (the one framework touch, mirroring the p15.9 `Drill.FundIDs` fund-set exactly).** A LEAF program's cell drills with the single `ProgramID`; a ROLLUP cell (a program WITH descendants, e.g. General) drills across the program SUBTREE via `ProgramIDs = ProgramDescendants(program)` (self + subtree), and the **web drill handler + test helper loop `account SET × program SET`, calling the EXISTING single-program `DrillSplits` per pair** — pure Go composition, ZERO SQL change (`DrillFilter` already has a `ProgramID` filter). Encode/Decode round-trip under a `progs` key. `TestProgramStatementLeafDrillReconciles` (Educación × Program Supplies × MXN → 500,000) and `TestProgramStatementRollupDrillReconciles` (General × Program Supplies × USD → 60,000 + 150,000 + 0 = 210,000) reconcile.
  - **HAND-VERIFIED numbers** (root scope, native, 2025-01-01..2026-06-30; golden `testdata/program_statement.{txt,csv}`). **Net per program:** General USD 3,567,500 / MXN 9,140,000 (== org R/E == p15.9 chTotal); Educación USD 170,000 (rev 320,000 − exp 150,000) / MXN 9,500,000 (rev 10,000,000 − exp 500,000); Food Pantry MXN −150,000 (0 rev − 150,000 exp).
  - No new dependencies (stdlib `context`, `sort`), no new sqlc query (reuses `ProgramActivity`/`ProgramTree`/`ProgramDescendants`/`DrillSplits`/`Tree`); `go.mod`/`go.sum` unchanged. **Reused the existing `web/accounts.go` `programOption{ID,Name}` type** (identical shape) rather than redeclaring. New i18n keys `reports.params.program` + `reports.program_statement.{title,all_programs,col.account,col.currency,section.revenue,section.expenses,total.revenue,total.expenses,net}` in BOTH catalogs (all leaves, no dotted-key collision; program-column headers are the stored program NAMES, not catalog keys). Program names are stored proper nouns (single `Name`) surfaced as verbatim column headers via `i18n.T`'s passthrough (the p15.5 period-label precedent). `make lint test check` + `govulncheck ./...` exit 0 (the p06.1 informational `x/crypto/openpgp` finding persists); `make golden` no-diff. **e2e** `e2e/tests/reports.spec.js` (+1 test): seeds a child program + an expense account + a program-tagged expense, opens the COMPARATIVE view (program selector + program columns + Revenue/Expenses/Net + a net report-total row + a drill link), picks the single program (3-column subtree view), and fetches the CSV — STRICT CSP (no `page.waitForFunction`), MUTATES only unique-named rows (worker-db safe).

- **p15.11 (report: 990 package — the year-end IRS Form 990 filing package)** — One labeled SECTION per Part (III, VIII, IX, X) in a SINGLE report Table (`internal/reports/form_990.go`), the last real report; it **COMPOSES the four sibling reports' toolkit paths** so its numbers reconcile to them (the cross-checks are the point). GROUP = `tax` (the already-declared group shared with p15.7). Non-obvious calls:
  - **FISCAL-YEAR param = the PERIOD param (From/To), no new `ParamsSpec` field.** The "fiscal year" is expressed as the existing period control (From..To = the org's fiscal year resolved to a from–to); `ParamsSpec{Period: true, Currency: true}`. **Part X's balance-sheet as-of is DERIVED internally as `To` (the fiscal-year END)** — a 990 balance sheet is the position at year-end, and using `To` makes Part X reconcile to p15.4 run as-of the same date. No separate as-of control (deliberate: the report author derives it, so the form shows one period, not a redundant date).
  - **THE LOAD-BEARING CHOICE: match EACH source report's conversion mode exactly** ("be consistent with the reports being cross-checked so the numbers actually match"), so three different rate modes coexist in one report: **Part VIII** revenue at **RateTxnDate → USD** (p15.5's flow), **Part IX** functional expenses at **RateClosing → USD** (p15.7), **Part X** balances at **RateNone + convert at the closing rate on `To`** (p15.4), **Part III** program activity **RateNone → native per currency** (p15.10). Unifying them would break a cross-check.
  - **SHARED 3-column shape `[Line/Account, Currency, Amount]` for all four Parts** (a section-header row per Part). A converted Part emits one USD row per line; native Part III emits per-currency rows. This keeps ONE Table (one Column set) the generic renderer + golden dump + CSV serve unchanged, and lets each amount line DRILL to its accounts' splits (`DrillPeriod` for III/VIII/IX, `DrillAsOf(To)` for X). **A line drills only when its underlying accounts span a SINGLE NATIVE currency** (the p15.7 rule): a multi-native-currency line (Part VIII's VIII.1e Government Grants = USD 200,000 + MXN 10,000,000; Part IX's IX.24e = USD 370,000 + MXN 860,000) has a converted figure summed across currencies that no single currency-filtered drill reconciles, so it is left non-drillable — `partVIII`/`partIX` fetch native activity (`RateNone`) alongside the converted, compute the native-currency SET per effective code, and `periodLineDrill` gates on `len(ccys)==1`, carrying the ONE native currency (not the display currency USD). Part III's per-currency rows and Part X's single-native-currency account cells drill directly.
  - **Part VIII — revenue by effective line (== p15.5):** per-account `Activity(RateTxnDate→USD)` filtered to **`type=="revenue"`** (NOT `reAccounts`, which is R+E) → the converted USD leaf map → `Group990("VIII","USD",leaf)` (Group990 does NO conversion, so convert per-account FIRST, at Activity's grain — the same grain p15.5 sums). Displayed +inflow (net-debit credit → ×−1). **Buckets: VIII.1f 5,275,000 · VIII.1e 781,594 · VIII.2 120,000 · (Unmapped) Event Income 300,000 = Total 6,476,594 == p15.5 total revenue** (asserted by running the income statement and comparing). Note 781,594 (txn-date, month-by-month) ≠ the closing-rate 752,486 — matching p15.5 is the whole point.
  - **Part IX — functional-expense line totals (== p15.7):** `FunctionalMatrix(RateClosing→USD)`, each line total = Σ the three functional classes (footing), grouped by `EffectiveCodes` under `Part990Lines("IX","expense")`. Cross-check runs the p15.7 report and asserts each Part IX line total == p15.7's per-line **Total column**, and grand == p15.7 grand = **2,375,014**. (IX.7 1,650,000 · IX.11g 2,500 · IX.16 305,000 · IX.24e 417,514.)
  - **Part X — balance sheet at year-end (== p15.4):** p15.4's net-asset + intercompany-elimination logic lives INSIDE `runBalanceSheet` (not a shared method), so at a consolidated (root) scope Part X **replicates the IC elimination** reusing the existing toolkit methods (`isConsolidated`, `store.IntercompanyAccountIDs`, `BalancesAsOf`, `restrictedNetAssets`) — assets/liabilities converted at the closing rate, net-assets `with` = restricted funds' asset-side balances, `without` = plug − with, `A = L + NA`. Cross-check runs the actual p15.4 report as-of `To` and asserts each line equal: **Total assets 248,128.04 = Total L+NA 248,128.04; NA without 189,268.92 + with 55,859.12 = 245,128.04** (matches p15.4's committed golden byte-for-byte).
  - **Part III — program service summary (== p15.10):** "top-level program" = **exactly the program set p15.10's COMPARATIVE view emits** (General, Educación, Food Pantry — every program in tree pre-order), driven by the IDENTICAL `ProgramActivity(RateNone)` call, each program a labeled group with a Revenue then Expense line per currency (native, ×−1 rev / ×+1 exp). PLAN's own p15.10 line calls this set "all top-level programs as comparative columns", so this matches the PLAN's vocabulary. **NO cross-program grand total** — General is a rollup that already folds in Educación + Food Pantry, so summing the groups would double-count (like p15.10's un-summed side-by-side columns). Cross-check compares each program group's per-currency figure to p15.10's section-total column for that program (absent==0 on both sides, since p15.10 shows a 0-row for a currency a program lacks).
  - **EVERY section renders an explicit Unmapped bucket** (Z19 — never drop rows), even when empty: Part VIII's is NON-empty (Event Income, no effective code → 300,000); Part IX / Part III are structurally empty (every expense inherits IX.24e; every R/E split carries a program, D24); Part X is a BY-ACCOUNT section (accounts shown by name, summed into the totals), so its Unmapped bucket is a **non-double-counting MEMO** — the fixture's A/L accounts DO carry no 990 code but span USD+MXN, so the memo renders 0 (a multi-currency memo is not drillable and never re-added to a total; the accounts are listed by name, not dropped). Four buckets total (one per Part). Asserted present via `TestForm990UnmappedBucketsPresent`.
  - **DRILL reconciliation:** `TestForm990PartVIIIDrillReconciles` turns the VIII.1f Contributions line's `Drill` into `store.DrillFilter`s (looping the account set, as the drill route does), sums the drilled NATIVE splits, and asserts `−sum == cell.Minor == 5,275,000` (USD 1:1). Line drills span the mapped accounts (`AccountIDs` from `EffectiveCodes`); Part III program drills carry the p15.10 program SET (`ProgramIDs` for rollup, `ProgramID` for a leaf).
  - No new dependencies (stdlib `context`, `sort`), **no new sqlc query** (reuses `Activity`/`FunctionalMatrix`/`ProgramActivity`/`BalancesAsOf`/`Group990`/`Part990Lines`/`EffectiveCodes`/`restrictedNetAssets`/`isConsolidated`/`ConvertMinorAt`/`DrillSplits`/`Tree`); `go.mod`/`go.sum` unchanged. **No framework change** — the shared Table/Cell/Drill shapes carried everything (unlike p15.9/p15.10 which added `Drill.FundIDs`/`ProgramIDs`). One new toolkit helper `Toolkit.accountTypes` (account→type map, one tree read/run). New i18n keys `reports.form_990.{title,col.line,col.currency,col.amount,unmapped,part.iii,part.viii,part.ix,part.x,iii.revenue,iii.expenses,viii.total,ix.total,x.total_assets,x.total_liabilities,x.na_without,x.na_with,x.total_net_assets,x.total_liabilities_net_assets}` in BOTH catalogs (all leaves, no dotted-key collision — `part.*` and `x.*` are distinct prefixes with no bare-prefix value). **990 LINE labels stay STORED reference text** (`form990_lines`, D25) rendered verbatim as `TextCell` via `lineLabel`/`PartLine` — NOT catalog keys (p15.7's precedent). `make lint test check` + `govulncheck ./...` exit 0 (the p06.1 informational `x/crypto/openpgp` finding persists); `make golden` no-diff (golden `testdata/form_990.{txt,csv}`). **e2e** `e2e/tests/reports.spec.js` (+1 test): seeds an UNMAPPED revenue receipt (→ Part VIII Unmapped bucket) + a program-tagged expense on an IX.16 account, opens the package over the fiscal year, sees the four Part headers + `(Unmapped)` + the Part VIII/IX totals + the Part X balancing row + a drill link, and fetches the CSV — STRICT CSP (no `page.waitForFunction`), MUTATES only unique-named rows (worker-db safe).

- **p15.12 (reports: index + recipe — the last step of Phase 15)** — A `GET /reports` index page (`internal/web/reports.go` `reportsIndex` + `templates/reports_index.tmpl`) listing the reports the CURRENT user may access, grouped by report group, each a link to a concrete `/reports/{id}`; plus `internal/reports/README.md`, the "adding a report" checklist. Non-obvious calls:
  - **PERM MODEL: the route is `AnyUser`; the PAGE filters its own contents by grant.** The index is visible to any logged-in user (anon → 302 login, like every AnyUser route), but it lists a group's reports only if the user holds that group's grant (or is admin). An ungranted non-admin therefore gets a **200 empty index** (the `reports.index.empty` message), never a 403 — the page is a directory, not a gated resource. The permission matrix picks the AnyUser route up with zero edits (every logged-in persona → 200).
  - **FILTERING REUSES THE ENFORCEMENT PATH so it can't drift.** The handler does NOT re-implement grant logic: it loads grants ONCE via `s.grantChecker(ctx, u, ReportGroup(""))` and, per registered report, includes it iff `decide(ReportGroup(rep.Group), u, checker) == outcomeAllow` — literally the check `enforce()` runs on `GET /reports/{id}`. **Gotcha encoded in a comment:** `grantChecker` returns the always-false stub for any non-`permReportGroup` perm, so passing `ReportGroup("")` (not `AnyUser`) is REQUIRED — else the closure never loads grants and the index lists nothing. `decide` short-circuits admin → allow-all before consulting the closure. Result: a report appears on the index iff its route would allow the user — no second source of truth.
  - **GROUPING/ORDER:** sections in `reports.Groups()` order (financial/funds/programs/tax — the grant-UI order), reports within a section in `Registry.All()` (registration) order; a section renders only when it has ≥1 permitted report. Group section LABELS are localized (`reports.group.{financial,funds,programs,tax}`) — the human-facing index shows labels, while the raw group NAMES stay reference values in the admin grant UI (p13.2).
  - **NAV:** registering `/reports` lights up the pre-existing `nav.reports` entry (its route was previously unregistered, so `visibleNav` filtered it out). The nav entry keeps its `ReportGroup("")` Perm — `navPermits` already reads that as "any grant OR admin", so a no-grant user sees NO nav link but CAN still reach the empty index by URL (the route is AnyUser). This asymmetry is deliberate: the nav is a "you have reports" signal; the page is a directory. No nav edit needed (data-driven, honest-link machinery).
  - **README location: `internal/reports/README.md`** (the checklist's steps are all about files IN that package: `<id>.go`, the sqlc query, `registry.go Default()`, the i18n catalogs, `.WithDrill`, the golden `testdata/`). References `trial_balance.go` as the exemplar (the code already calls it that). Steps documented AS THEY NOW EXIST + what a new report gets for free (route/perm-matrix/index/rendering auto-cover it — a code-only addition).
  - No new dependencies (stdlib only), no new sqlc query, no framework change; `go.mod`/`go.sum` unchanged. New i18n keys `reports.index.{title,empty}` + `reports.group.{financial,funds,programs,tax}` in BOTH catalogs (all leaves; `reports.index.title`/`.empty` avoid a bare `reports.index` leaf-vs-prefix collision). The existing reports' logic/goldens are untouched. `make lint test check` + `govulncheck ./...` exit 0 (the p06.1 informational `x/crypto/openpgp` finding persists); `make golden` no-diff (no report golden changed). **Per-persona tests** (`internal/web/reports_test.go`): admin sees every registered report link + all four group labels (no-dead-links: each registry id is an href); a `financial`-only grantee sees trial_balance but NOT fund_activity/program_statement/functional_expenses/form_990 and none of the funds/programs/tax section labels (href matched with a trailing quote so substrings can't false-positive); a no-grants user gets 200 + the empty message + zero links; anon → 302. **e2e** `e2e/tests/reports.spec.js` (+1 test): admin opens `/reports`, sees a grouped report-list section, clicks the trial-balance link, lands on `/reports/trial_balance` with its params form + table — STRICT CSP (no `page.waitForFunction`), READ-ONLY (worker-db safe).
- **p16.1 (db: reconciliations + split lock — D13)** — Migration **00014** adds `reconciliations(id, account_id→accounts, statement_date GLOB YYYY-MM-DD, statement_balance INTEGER, currency→currencies, status DEFAULT 'open' CHECK(open/finalized), notes)` + its standard single-id `reconciliations_versions` twin (snapshot cols `account_id, statement_date, statement_balance, currency, status, notes`; the version-append + AssertVersioned land in p16.2), then `ALTER TABLE splits ADD COLUMN reconciliation_id INTEGER REFERENCES reconciliations(id)` (+ index `splits_reconciliation`), then the lock trigger. No seed row (no `changes`-id shift). File pure ASCII.
  - **`reconciliation_id` is LIVE-ONLY, NOT versioned** (the deferred-from-00010 column, D13): which reconciliation a split is cleared against is OPERATIONAL metadata, not audited business content — clearing/unclearing must NOT mint a new split VERSION (the audited reconciliation event is *finalization*, recorded on `reconciliations`/its twin). So the column is added to `splits` but **NOT** to `splits_versions`, and `InsertSplitVersion`'s snapshot column set stays exactly the 00010 set — a clearing toggle changes no versioned column, so **Z3/Z5 stay clean** with no store-path change. The p08.2 `SplitsByTransaction` reader was extended to also SELECT `reconciliation_id` (keeping its sqlc return type `[]Split` rather than a bespoke Row struct after the model gained the column); its consumers ignore the field, and `splitUnchanged` compares only the business columns, so no store behavior changed.
  - **`trg_split_locked_when_finalized`** (BEFORE UPDATE on splits): guards EXACTLY `amount, account_id, transaction_id, fund_id, reconciliation_id` (NULL-safe `IS NOT` in the WHEN clause) and RAISE(ABORT)s when the OLD **or** NEW `reconciliation_id` points at a `status='finalized'` recon — so it also blocks moving a split INTO or OUT OF a finalized recon and re-pointing between recons. NOT guarded: memo, position, program_id, functional_class (non-financial; matches the p16.2 "memo/payee allowed" store rule). D13's "date" lock is a `transactions` column — enforced store-side in p16.2, deliberately NOT a trigger here. **UPDATE-only by design:** the trigger guards UPDATE of the financial columns; DELETE / soft-delete of a finalized-cleared split is NOT trigger-blocked here — that lock lives store-side in p16.2 (this keeps the schema trigger to the row-local UPDATE subset, per the "guard sensibly" division of AGENTS rule 7).
  - **Z8/Z9 now active** (were `sqlDeferred` placeholders; `sqlDeferred` deleted as unused). **Z8** (Error, no status filter): every cleared split (reconciliation_id NOT NULL, non-deleted txn) must be on its recon's `account_id` and carry its recon's `currency` (currency lives on the split's txn, D3) — a cross-account/cross-currency clearing is wrong regardless of status. **Z9** (Error, finalized only): for each finalized recon, `opening + Σ(cleared split amounts) = statement_balance`, all net-debit minor units (D2, no sign flip); `opening` = the prior finalized recon's `statement_balance` for the SAME `(account_id, currency)` by `(statement_date, id)` order, COALESCE 0 for the first — the statement chain. Both find nothing on a db with no reconciliation rows, so the fixture/`make check` stay clean; the fixture does NOT yet exercise Z9 (no recon rows until p16.2 builds one), so `ledger_test.go` carries the dedicated clean+violating recon cases (built via direct SQL). **Soft-deleted-txn exclusion (deliberate, a p16.2/p09.4 landmine):** both Z8 and Z9 restrict to non-deleted txns (`t.deleted = 0`), so soft-deleting a transaction whose split is cleared in a FINALIZED recon drops that split from Z9's sum and Z9 WILL fire — which is the correct property (a finalized statement's underlying txns must not silently vanish), but it means the Appendix D fixture's "one deleted transaction" must NOT overlap the finalized Checking US recon's cleared splits, or the fixture goes red. **Sign convention pinned for p16.2/p16.3:** `statement_balance` is stored net-debit signed (D2-consistent) so Z9 is a plain integer equality; the workspace UI converts for display.
  - Updated the pre-existing `TestTransactionsSplitsVersionsTablesExist` (00010's test): it asserted `splits.reconciliation_id` must NOT exist ("deferred to p16.1") — flipped to assert it now exists on `splits` but still stays OFF `splits_versions` (the live-only invariant). `make lint test check` + `govulncheck ./...` exit 0 (p06.1 informational `x/crypto/openpgp` finding persists); `make check` clean on a fresh migrated db. No new deps; sqlc regen only (new `Reconciliation`/`ReconciliationsVersion` models + `Split.ReconciliationID`).

- **p16.2 (store: reconciliation lifecycle — D13/D20)** — `internal/store/reconciliations.go` + `internal/db/queries/reconciliations.sql` (pure ASCII, positional `?`, `make gen` reproducible), the store-level split lock in `transactions.go`'s `UpdateTransaction`, and the `ExtendReconciliation` fixture seam. All four lifecycle methods run through the write funnel as ONE change; validation lives inside `fn` on the tx-bound `q` (p08.2 TOCTOU discipline), so a rejected op rolls the change row back with no audit trace.
  - **Methods.** `StartReconciliation(ctx, accountID, currency, statementDate, statementBalance) (id, error)` — creates an OPEN recon; validates `validDate` (`ErrBadDate`), account exists+**reconcilable**+active (`ErrNotReconcilable`), currency exists+active (`ErrReconciliationCurrency`), and **one open recon per (account, currency)** (`CountOpenReconciliations>0 → ErrOpenReconciliationExists`); versioned op='create'. `SetSplitReconciled(ctx, reconID, splitID, on bool)` — clears/unclears `splits.reconciliation_id`; only while the recon is OPEN (`ErrReconciliationNotOpen`); on clear validates split account == recon account (`ErrSplitReconAccount`), split currency (from its txn, D3) == recon currency (`ErrSplitReconCurrency`), and not on a soft-deleted txn (`ErrSplitDeleted`). `Finalize(ctx, reconID)` — open→finalized, versioned op='update', with the zero-difference gate below. `Reopen(ctx, reconID)` — finalized→open (`ErrReconciliationNotFinalized` otherwise), versioned op='update'.
  - **"Reconcilable account" / "currency valid for it" (the pinned definitions):** accounts carry a `reconcilable` flag (00005) and are **multi-currency** (`default_currency` is a default, not a constraint — FX Clearing holds USD+MXN), so a recon may only START on `reconcilable=1 AND active=1`, and "currency valid" reduces to **currency exists + active** (the statement decides the currency; not tied to the account's default). **One open recon per (account, currency)** chosen per D13 (a finalized recon does not block a new one — that is the statement chain).
  - **`SetSplitReconciled` DOES emit a `changes` row.** `splits.reconciliation_id` is LIVE-ONLY / NOT versioned (00014), so clearing UPDATEs that one column and mints **no split version** — but it STILL goes through the funnel (AGENTS rule 2 is non-negotiable), so a `changes` row anchors the tx boundary + actor. The live-only decision is only about skipping the split-VERSION append, not skipping audit. (High-frequency clearing is a cost observation, not a license to bypass the funnel.)
  - **Finalize's zero-difference gate MIRRORS ledger Z9 byte-for-byte** — the tie that makes "Finalize succeeds ⇒ Z9 passes" true. `opening` = `PriorFinalizedStatementBalance` (prior FINALIZED recon's `statement_balance` for the same `(account, currency)`, ordered `statement_date DESC, id DESC`, strictly before this one, COALESCE 0 — identical to Z9's opening subquery). `cleared` = `ReconciliationClearedSum` (net-debit `SUM(amount)` of splits cleared against this recon joined to **non-deleted** txns — identical to Z9's inner SUM). `opening + cleared != statement_balance → ErrReconciliationDifference`. Both aggregates `CAST(... AS INTEGER)` so sqlc types them `int64` (a bare `COALESCE`/`SUM` types as `interface{}`); the recon-id param is `CAST(? AS INTEGER)` because `reconciliation_id` is a nullable column. **Tested** by `TestFinalizeRequiresZeroDifference`, which chains TWO finalized recons so the **opening chain is actually exercised** (opening≠0 on the second) plus the rejection path.
  - **Store-level edit block (`ErrSplitReconciled`, `TestEditReconciledTxnBlocked`) is WIDER than the DB trigger.** The p16.1 trigger is BEFORE UPDATE on `splits` and cannot see a header date/currency change or a split DELETE. So `UpdateTransaction` fetches `FinalizedReconciledSplitIDs(txn)` and, when any exist, returns the clean typed `ErrSplitReconciled` BEFORE the trigger fires for: **header date change** (D13's "date" lock lives on the txn), **header currency change** (would break Z8 on a cleared split), **deletion** of a locked split (would silently drop it from Z9's sum), and **amount/account/fund change** of a locked split (the trigger's guarded set). **memo/payee/position/program stay editable** (a memo-only `UpdateSplit` leaves the guarded columns equal so the trigger never fires anyway). Editing is allowed again after `Reopen`. Right-reason verified: neutering the block makes the DATE and DELETE cases return `<nil>` (trigger blind) and the amount/account/fund cases hit the raw `RAISE(ABORT)` instead of the typed error.
  - **`ExtendReconciliation` seam (the D13/D20 payoff).** Opt-in (New does not call it; `Expected.Reconciliation.ID == 0` until called). Finalizes the **2026-05-31 Checking US (USD)** reconciliation over the account's restricted (Beca Agua / Building Fund) AND unrestricted splits against ONE statement — a statement is about the bank account, not the fund. Statement balance **3,673,500** = the Checking US USD live balance (Expected 3,593,500) with the two UNCLEARED items backed out (+155,000 May rent, −75,000 June donation); opening 0 (first finalized recon). The two uncleared txn ids (2026-05-25 rent, 2026-06-10 donation) are now **captured into `IDs`** (previously discarded `post` returns) so the seam clears the **complement** of live non-deleted Checking US/USD splits — split ids are **queried live, not hardcoded** (the edited txn's Checking US split is a 3rd-generation id). No transaction is renumbered. `cuento check` / `ledger.Check` stay clean (Z8/Z9 pass); `TestReconSpansFunds` asserts the cleared set contains both `fund_id NOT NULL` and `fund_id NULL` splits against the one recon and the two items stay uncleared.
  - **AssertVersioned coverage:** `TestReconciliationLifecycle` asserts create→'create', Finalize→'update', Reopen→'update' via `testutil.AssertVersioned`, and that clearing mints NO split version (live-only). `TestReconciliationReopenAudited` uses `testutil.LatestVersionActor` to prove the reopen version names the acting user.
  - **Deviation:** the PLAN names the reopen test `TestReopenAudited`, but `funds_test.go` already defines that symbol in package `store` (Go forbids duplicates) — renamed to `TestReconciliationReopenAudited`. `make lint test check` + `govulncheck ./...` exit 0 (p06.1 informational `x/crypto/openpgp` finding persists).

- **p16.3 (web: reconciliation workspace — D13/D20)** — `internal/web/reconcile.go` + templates `reconciliations.tmpl` (list) / `reconcile.tmpl` (workspace) + recon `app.css` block + `e2e/tests/reconcile.spec.js`. Store read surface added in `internal/store/reconciliations.go` (+ four queries in `reconciliations.sql`, pure ASCII / positional `?`, `make gen` reproducible): `ReconcilableAccounts`, `ReconciliationsForAccount`, `ReconciliationWorkspaceSplits`, `ReconciliationSummaryFor`. The store owns the lifecycle + validation (p16.2); the web layer only renders and translates typed errors.
  - **URL scheme:** `GET /reconciliations` (TxnRead, list) · `POST /reconciliations` (TxnWrite, start) · `GET /reconciliations/{id}` (TxnRead, workspace) · `POST /reconciliations/{id}/splits/{sid}/toggle` (TxnWrite) · `POST /reconciliations/{id}/finalize` (TxnWrite) · `POST /reconciliations/{id}/reopen` (TxnWrite). Chose a flat `/reconciliations` resource (not `/accounts/{id}/reconcile`) so the list is one page across all reconcilable accounts and a recon has a stable id-addressed workspace. All six in the registry (rule 8) so the perm matrix auto-covers them; `routes_test.go`'s `newMatrixApp` now seeds a reconcilable account + an OPEN recon (id 1) with a nonzero statement so the reachability probe substitutes `{id}->1`/`{sid}->1` and hits real resources (finalize returns a clean 422 guard, reopen 409 on an open recon — both "reachable", not 404).
  - **Perms:** LIST + WORKSPACE VIEW = **TxnRead**; start/toggle/finalize/reopen ACTIONS = **TxnWrite** (a bookkeeping mutation — clearing splits / finalizing the statement chain). `TestReconPermsReadCannotAct` asserts explicitly beyond the matrix: a `read` user GETs list+workspace (200) but its toggle/finalize/start POSTs 403, while a `write` user's toggle succeeds (200).
  - **The TARGETED-swap toggle (the p16.3 anti-jank requirement).** The cleared toggle is a NATIVE `<button id="recon-toggle-{splitID}" hx-post=".../toggle" hx-target="#recon-row-{splitID}" hx-swap="outerHTML">`. The handler flips `SetSplitReconciled` (derived from the split's CURRENT cleared state so a repeated POST round-trips) and returns the `recon-toggle-response` PARTIAL: the flipped `<tr>` (targeted swap into the row) PLUS an OUT-OF-BAND swap of the sticky `<div id="recon-summary" hx-swap-oob="true">` (cleared total + difference chip + the Finalize button's disabled state). NOTHING above shifts, so scroll + focus survive. **Proven no-full-reload:** the handler test asserts the response has no `<html>`/no `app-nav` (a partial, not a document) and the difference reflects the flip; the e2e installs a `window` sentinel and asserts it SURVIVES two toggles while `#recon-diff-chip` text updates (400 -> 150 -> 0), i.e. a targeted swap not a nav.
  - **Space affordance = native focusable button, ZERO JS (CSP-safe).** The toggle is a real `<button>`, so Space activates it natively — no keydown ES module. The toggle swaps the whole row (destroying the focused button); htmx's focus-restore-by-id brings focus back to the same-id `recon-toggle-{splitID}`, which is what makes REPEATED Space work. The e2e drives the SECOND toggle by `page.keyboard.press('Space')` on a focused toggle and asserts BOTH the flip AND that focus survived the swap (`toBeFocused()`) — the requirement is verified, not assumed.
  - **Finalize-disabled-until-zero is SERVER-authoritative.** The disabled state is `Summary.Finalizable = (Difference == 0)` from `ReconciliationSummaryFor`, which REUSES Finalize's own two queries byte-for-byte (`PriorFinalizedStatementBalance` opening + `ReconciliationClearedSum` cleared) — so the button is enabled iff Finalize would accept. A client that POSTs a forced/stale nonzero finalize is rejected cleanly: the handler maps `ErrReconciliationDifference` to a **422** (re-render, never a 500), `ErrReconciliationNotOpen`/`NotFinalized` to 409, `NotFound` to 404. `TestFinalizeAtNonzeroRejectedCleanly` asserts the 422 (not 500) and the recon stays open; `TestFinalizeDisabledUntilZero` asserts the button's disabled attr flips with the difference.
  - **htmx-driven Finalize (a recorded gotcha).** Finalize was first a plain `<form method=post>` submit; it produced NO network request after the summary was OOB-swapped by a toggle (trace: `/finalize` in DOM snapshots, absent from the network log) — a **native form submit on a swapped-in node does not fire** (htmx re-wires hx-* triggers, not native submit handlers). Fix: put `hx-post` **on the BUTTON** (not the form) so htmx binds the button's click trigger when it processes the OOB content; the wrapping `<form method=post action=>` stays as the no-JS fallback. On success `redirectAfterForm` emits `HX-Redirect` back to the workspace (now the finalized read-only view). The e2e finalizes DIRECTLY after the toggles (no reload — a real user does not reload) and reaches the finalized view, so the fix is validated in the real flow.
  - **Workspace split set.** `ReconciliationWorkspaceSplits` lists the recon account's non-deleted splits IN the recon's currency (D3) that are UNCLEARED or cleared against THIS recon; splits cleared in a PRIOR finalized recon are EXCLUDED (they are folded into the opening balance, so showing them double-counts) and soft-deleted-txn splits are excluded (matches Z9). Uncleared rows sort first (stable within date order). **Recon is per (account, currency):** the start form defaults the currency to the account's `default_currency` (a bank account is single-currency) — no multi-currency picker.
  - **Start form** goes through the p10.3 form-error convention: date via `money.ParseDate`, balance via `money.Parse` (rule 10, never `strconv`/`time.Parse`), each `StartReconciliation` typed error mapped to a (field, i18n key) pair (`error.recon.*`) with autofocus; on the list, an account with an OPEN recon renders a "continue" link to its workspace instead of a start form, so a double-start is a non-event. After finalize the workspace renders read-only with a Reopen action — this doubles as "the finalized recon shows" (p16.4 owns the statement report + per-account history; NOT built here).
  - i18n: `recon.*` + `error.recon.*` in BOTH catalogs; the leaf/parent collision (go-i18n derives dotted ids from nested tables) was watched — `recon.finalize` is a leaf, so the blocked-hint is `recon.finalize_blocked` (NOT `recon.finalize.blocked`, which would redefine the `recon.finalize` table). **e2e stability: the full parallel suite (40 specs) ran 15x green with zero flakes** (this step adds htmx swap interactions, so the run was the load-bearing check per the task). `make lint test check` + `govulncheck ./...` exit 0 (p06.1 informational `x/crypto/openpgp` finding persists). No new deps; `go.mod`/`go.sum` unchanged.

- **p16.4 (web+reports: recon history + statement report — D13/D20)** — `internal/reports/reconciliation_statement.go` (the report) + golden test + `testdata/reconciliation_statement.{txt,csv}`; web param plumbing in `internal/web/reports.go`; history section in `internal/web/reconcile.go` + `reconciliations.tmpl`; two store reads + two queries in `internal/store/reconciliations.go` / `reconciliations.sql` (pure ASCII, positional/`CAST` params, `make gen` reproducible). Completes Phase 16.
  - **New report group `reconciliation`** — added to `reports.Groups()` (the code-declared set). It flows UNCHANGED through `codeReportGroups()` → `SyncReportGroups` (synced to `report_groups` at startup, `TestReportGroupsSynced`), the admin grant UI (p13.2 iterates the set), the permission matrix (the mounted `/reports/reconciliation_statement{,.csv,/drill}` routes are gated `ReportGroup("reconciliation")`, picked up by the matrix test automatically), and the `/reports` INDEX (p15.12 buckets by group). Only two code touches beyond the group string: the `reports.group.reconciliation` label (both catalogs) and `registry_test.go`'s pinned group list (a NON-golden test, allowed). The index/grant coverage is auto (iteration): `TestReportsIndexAdminSeesAll` asserts every registered report+group appears; a new `TestReportsIndexReconciliationGrant` asserts a user granted ONLY `reconciliation` sees the statement report + its section and NOT the financial reports; `TestReportsIndexGrantFiltersGroups` gained `reconciliation_statement` to its must-NOT-appear list.
  - **Statement detail report (`reconciliation_statement`)** — takes a report-SPECIFIC `Reconciliation` param (added to `Params`/`ParamsSpec`, mirroring Account/Fund/Program), parsed from `?reconciliation=` OR the `?recon=` alias and validated against the real FINALIZED-recon set (an open/unknown id drops → empty Table, the nothing-to-show rule). Renders one columnar Table: a STATEMENT-INFO preamble (account name resolved via `store.AccountName(p.LangOr())`, statement date, statement balance, currency, status), the OPENING balance (`ReconciliationSummaryFor`, i.e. `PriorFinalizedStatementBalance` — the statement chain), the INCLUDED (cleared) SPLITS (register-row shape: date→txn link, payee/description, fund, amount), the CLEARED TOTAL, and CLOSING = opening + cleared. **The chain is asserted**: the golden test re-derives Σ(emitted split cells) == cleared, opening(0)+Σ == closing == statement balance, all from the report's OWN cells. **NOT scoped and NOT converted (the D13/D20 payoff):** a recon spans ALL funds AND subsidiaries, so the included set is identified by the recon id alone — the new `ReconciliationClearedSplits` query has the SAME predicate as `ReconciliationClearedSum` (`reconciliation_id = ? AND t.deleted = 0`), so the identity holds. The subsidiary scope selector still renders (D18, every report scoped) but is INERT on this report (documented no-op). No period/currency controls (a finalized statement is a fixed artifact).
  - **Golden (fixture-derived, DATA RULE 11):** the report over the fixture's finalized 2026-05-31 Checking US recon (`f.ExtendReconciliation(t)`, the OPT-IN seam). Hand-verified: statement balance **3,673,500** (USD 36,735.00), opening **0**, cleared total **3,673,500**, closing **3,673,500 == statement balance**; the **17** cleared splits appear (== `f.Expected.Reconciliation.ClearedCount`), the two uncleared txns (May rent, June donation) ABSENT. CSV parses + matches (the `Supplies (v3, final)` line proves CSV comma-escaping). No existing report golden changed (`make golden` diff = only the two new files).
  - **History page (scheme):** EXTENDS the p16.3 `/reconciliations` list (TxnRead) with a "Finalized reconciliations" section, rather than a dedicated `/reconciliations/history` — the list is the natural home (the reconciler is already there) and it avoids a second route/nav entry. One row per FINALIZED recon per account (account, statement date, statement balance, finalized date), each linking to `/reports/reconciliation_statement?reconciliation={id}`. An account with none contributes no rows (`TestReconHistoryEmptyForAccountWithNone`).
  - **"finalized-by/when" (the one judgment call):** there is NO `finalized_at` column (00014). The finalize timestamp lives ONLY in the audit trail — `reconciliations_versions.valid_from` of the `op='update', status='finalized'` snapshot (MAX for a reopened+refinalized recon). **Kept OUT of the report Table (→ the golden)** so the golden never couples to the fixture's clock/change-count; status=`Finalized` conveys the state. **Put ON the history page** (`FinalizedReconciliationsForAccount` reads it via the version twin; rendered as its DATE portion via the existing `dateOnly` helper + `money.FormatDate`, since `money` has no datetime formatter — rule 10). "Finalized-by" (a `changes→users` join) was treated as skippable ("if available").
  - i18n: `reports.reconciliation_statement.*` (title, choose, cols, info labels, status.open/finalized, opening/cleared_total/closing/unrestricted), `reports.params.reconciliation`, `reports.group.reconciliation`, and `recon.history.*` — all in BOTH catalogs (`TestCatalogParity` green). e2e: extended `reconcile.spec.js` to open the finalized recon's statement report from the history link and assert statement info + the two included splits + the 400.00 chain (one `npx playwright test` run green, 40 specs). `make lint test check` + `govulncheck ./...` exit 0 (p06.1 informational `x/crypto/openpgp` finding persists). No new deps; `go.mod`/`go.sum` unchanged.

- **p16.5 (store+web: reconciliation-lock hardening — extends D13)** — closes two gaps in the Phase-16 SPLIT-level lock that the p16.1 trigger + p16.2 store block did not cover. `internal/store/transactions.go` (`DeleteTransaction`), `internal/store/reconciliations.go` (`Reopen` + `ErrReconciliationNotLatest`), one new read query in `reconciliations.sql`, and the two web handlers that surface the typed errors. No schema/migration change, no new deps (`make gen` reproducible; new query only).
  - **Gap 1 — void was NOT blocked (the real hole).** The `trg_split_locked_when_finalized` trigger fires on split UPDATE only; it cannot see a transaction soft-delete. So voiding a txn whose split is cleared in a FINALIZED recon silently dropped that split from the recon's balance — Z9 would flag it AFTER the fact (both Z9 and the recon cleared-sum restrict to `t.deleted = 0`, the deliberate p16.1 exclusion), but it was not PREVENTED. **Fix:** `DeleteTransaction` now MIRRORS `UpdateTransaction`'s lock — BEFORE `SoftDeleteTransaction` it calls `q.FinalizedReconciledSplitIDs(ctx, id)` (the SAME helper) and returns the existing typed `ErrSplitReconciled` when any split is locked; the rejected write rolls the change back (no audit trace), so the txn stays live. Reopen the recon to void. **Load-bearing proof (`TestVoidReconciledTransactionBlocked`):** the void returns `ErrSplitReconciled` + `deleted=0` + `ledger.Check` stays Z9-clean; after `Reopen` the same void succeeds (`deleted=1`). No over-block: `TestVoidOpenReconciledTransactionAllowed` voids a txn cleared only in an OPEN recon.
  - **Gap 2 — Reopen had no in-order guard.** `Reopen` reopened ANY finalized recon regardless of a LATER finalized recon on the same (account, currency); reopening out of order lets edits land under a later finalized statement / corrupts the opening chain. **Fix:** new `ErrReconciliationNotLatest` + a new read query `HasLaterFinalizedReconciliation` — the byte-mirror of `PriorFinalizedStatementBalance`'s "prior" bound (`SELECT EXISTS(... status='finalized' AND account_id=? AND currency=? AND (statement_date > ? OR (statement_date = ? AND id > ?)))`, same param shape, `EXISTS→bool` idiom copied from `HasAccountSubsidiaryMap`, pure ASCII / positional `?`). `Reopen` calls it on the tx-bound `q` after the not-finalized check; if a later finalized recon exists it returns `ErrReconciliationNotLatest` (the user backs up newest-first). **Proof (`TestReopenBlockedWhenLaterFinalizedExists`):** two finalized recons E(Jan)/L(Feb) — `Reopen(E)`→`ErrReconciliationNotLatest` (stays finalized), `Reopen(L)` succeeds, then `Reopen(E)` succeeds; `TestReopenSingleFinalized` proves a lone finalized recon still reopens.
  - **Web mapping (no 500 on either user path).** The void flow is the LOAD-BEARING web change: `DeleteTransaction` now returns `ErrSplitReconciled` on a user action, and the old `default → serverError` would make that a 500. The `void` handler gains an `errors.Is(err, store.ErrSplitReconciled)` arm that re-renders `void.tmpl` at **409** with an error banner (`voidReviewModel.ErrorKey = "void.error.reconciled"`) — the txn is still live so `buildVoidReview` succeeds — never a 500 (`TestVoidReconciledTxnRejectedCleanly`: 409 + localized banner + txn stays live, then reopen makes the void redirect through). `reconReopen` gains an `ErrReconciliationNotLatest` arm mapped to a plain **409** alongside the existing not-finalized conflict (minimal — matching the established treatment, never a 500). New i18n key `void.error.reconciled` in BOTH catalogs (`TestCatalogParity` green).
  - `PATH=... make lint test check` + `govulncheck ./...` exit 0 (p06.1 informational `x/crypto/openpgp` finding persists); `make check` clean. No web-template/route additions beyond the banner line; `go.mod`/`go.sum` unchanged.

- **p17.1 (db: bank-CSV-import staging schema)** — Migration **00015** adds three OPERATIONAL/STAGING tables (pure ASCII; no seed, so no `changes`-id shift): `mapping_profiles(id, name, config TEXT DEFAULT '{}')` — the saved CSV column-mapping as opaque JSON (decoded with stdlib `encoding/json` at the store, p17.2; no `json_valid` CHECK, the store owns the shape); `import_batches(id, filename, account_id→accounts, subsidiary_id→subsidiaries, profile_id→mapping_profiles, uploaded_by→users, uploaded_at TEXT RFC3339)` — one upload, binding ONE target account AND ONE subsidiary; `import_rows(id, batch_id→import_batches, account_id→accounts, raw_json, parsed_date, parsed_amount INTEGER, parsed_payee, parsed_memo, status DEFAULT 'pending' CHECK(pending/posted/discarded), dedupe_hash, posted_transaction_id→transactions NULL)`. Two indexes: `idx_import_rows_dedupe(account_id, dedupe_hash)` and `idx_import_rows_batch(batch_id, status)`.
  - **Non-versioned (the core decision).** These are staging/reference data like `currencies`/`report_groups`, NOT bitemporal ledger tables: NO `*_versions` twin, no version trigger, no `changes` wiring here. They are NOT in the Z3/Z5 versioned-table UNIONs (which enumerate twins by hardcoded name — no twin ⇒ not included), so `cuento check` stays clean (verified: `make check` on a fresh migrated db reports "clean (no violations)"). **The audit is preserved WITHOUT versioning them:** a POSTED row links to its real, fully versioned ledger transaction via `posted_transaction_id` (the transaction p17.3 creates carries the whole audit), and a DISCARDED row's audit is the `changes` row p17.3 writes with a reason. The staging rows are disposable scaffolding around those two audited outcomes.
  - **`parsed_amount` is INTEGER minor units (rule 3)** — never REAL/float. `parsed_*` and `posted_transaction_id` are NULLABLE (an unparseable row can still stage for review; `posted_transaction_id` is set only on post). sqlc maps them to `sql.NullInt64`/`sql.NullString` (regen only, new `MappingProfile`/`ImportBatch`/`ImportRow` models; `make gen` reproducible).
  - **Dedupe-scoping DECISION: denormalized `account_id` on `import_rows` + a NON-UNIQUE index `(account_id, dedupe_hash)` + application-level LOOKUP, NOT a UNIQUE constraint.** `dedupe_hash = sha256(account|date|amount|normalized payee+memo)` is COMPUTED in p17.2; here it is just a column. Three reasons for this exact combination, each mapped to a downstream hint: (1) **NON-UNIQUE, not UNIQUE** — a legitimate idempotent re-upload (p17.3 `TestReimportFlagsDuplicates`) must be FLAGGED by a lookup, not crash at INSERT; a hard UNIQUE would error on the valid re-upload. (2) **Denormalized `account_id`, not join-through-`batch_id`** — dedupe must survive ACROSS batches (a re-upload is a new batch), so the scope must be a direct column, and the index must be genuinely per-account. (3) **Composite `(account_id, dedupe_hash)`, not bare `dedupe_hash`** — the "same hash under a DIFFERENT account is allowed" property (two banks can legitimately produce identical-looking rows) only holds if the scope key includes the account. `account_id` is a real FK so Z4 (`pragma_foreign_key_check`) stays clean. Drift between `import_rows.account_id` and its batch's account is a p17.2 store concern — deliberately NO trigger now.
  - **"account must map to that subsidiary" is a p17.2 concern, NOT a schema trigger.** The batch is two independent FKs (`account_id`, `subsidiary_id`); the cross-table `account_subsidiaries` membership check is not row-local, so per rule 7 it lives in the store (p17.2 `TestBatchSubValidated`), not in a trigger. (The p16.1 `trg_split_locked` precedent is row-local financial locking and does not license a cross-table trigger here.)
  - **The key test** (`TestDedupeHashScopedPerAccount`, direct SQL) defends BOTH halves of the decision: (a) stages the same `dedupe_hash` on account A (batch A1), asserts the staging-flow lookup `SELECT count(*) WHERE account_id=? AND dedupe_hash=?` = 1 (duplicate DETECTED); then re-uploads the SAME hash on A in a NEW batch (A2) and asserts the INSERT SUCCEEDS and the lookup now = 2 — this is the assertion that locks the NON-UNIQUE choice: a `UNIQUE(account_id, dedupe_hash)` index makes this INSERT fail (verified by a temporary swap — the test goes red with "UNIQUE constraint failed"), so a future edit adding UNIQUE cannot sail through green; (b) INSERTs the SAME hash under account B (a different batch) — accepted (not scoped away by a bare-hash unique) — and asserts A's scope stays = 2 while B's scope = 1 (identical-looking rows do not leak across accounts). Companion smoke tests: three tables exist and have NO version twins; valid insert; bad status rejected; all FKs (`import_rows.batch_id/account_id/posted_transaction_id`, `import_batches.account_id/subsidiary_id/profile_id/uploaded_by`) enforced. **Tests-first observed:** all failed on "no such table" before 00015, green after. `make lint test check` + `govulncheck ./...` exit 0 (p06.1 informational `x/crypto/openpgp` finding persists). No new deps; `go.mod`/`go.sum` unchanged.

- **p17.2 (web: upload + mapping + staging)** — The bank-CSV import flow: a TxnWrite user uploads a statement CSV, maps its columns, picks the target account + subsidiary, previews 20 parsed rows, and stages them (batch + `import_rows` persisted, duplicates flagged advisory). Posting is p17.3.
  - **Parser package `internal/bankimport` — PURE, table-tested, no DB/no document.** `Parse(raw []byte, cfg Config, exponent int) ([]ParsedRow, error)` produces `ParsedRow{Date, AmountMinor, Payee, Memo, Raw, Err}` — ONE per data row, with a PER-ROW `Err` (never a panic, never a whole-file abort) on a malformed row; a file-level fault (undetectable delimiter, unreadable CSV, zero data rows → `ErrNoRows`) returns a non-nil error and no rows. `Config` (the JSON shape stored on `mapping_profiles.config`, stdlib `encoding/json`): `delimiter` (auto-sniff or comma/semicolon/tab), `has_header`, `amount_mode` (`single` signed column OR `debit_credit` PAIR — exactly one non-blank/row; debit adds, credit subtracts → net-debit), `sign_flip` (invert the final amount), `date_format` (ISO/US/EU), and zero-based column indices `date_col/amount_col/debit_col/credit_col/payee_col/memo_col` (a negative index = unmapped optional column). **Table-tested modes:** delimiter sniffing (comma/semicolon/tab), header on/off, single-signed vs debit/credit pair (incl. both-blank / both-filled → per-row error), sign-flip (single + pair), each date format, malformed row (bad amount, short row) → per-row `Err` while a good row in the same file still parses, empty/header-only → `ErrNoRows`, currency symbols + thousands grouping + parens-for-negative. **Reuses `internal/money`:** amounts via `money.Parse` (NumberPlain; `parseMoney` pre-strips `$`/spaces/grouping commas/currency codes first, since `money.Parse` handles grouping/parens/DR-CR but NOT symbols), dates via `money.ParseDate` re-formatted to canonical ISO. The EU date-format test uses `13/01/2025` (invalid as ISO and US) to defeat `money.ParseDate`'s always-on ISO fallback masking a wrong layout.
  - **`dedupe_hash = sha256(accountID | date | strconv.FormatInt(amountMinor,10) | Normalize(payee) "\x1f" Normalize(memo))`, four parts joined by `|`.** Computed by ONE function `bankimport.DedupeHash`, called by BOTH the staging path (a parsed row) AND the ledger-split-derivation path (an existing posted split), so the two only collide on a truly identical event. **`Normalize`** = trim + lowercase + collapse-internal-whitespace (`strings.Join(strings.Fields(strings.ToLower(s))," ")`); **payee and memo are normalized SEPARATELY then joined by `\x1f`** (a fix for the aliasing bug where trailing whitespace adjacent to the separator leaked a stray space — normalizing the concatenation `payee+sep+memo` as a whole failed; separate-then-join is exact). **Amount sign:** `split.amount` is net-debit (D2) — a deposit into an asset bank account is a POSITIVE debit — and the parser's signed amount (after any flip) lands on the SAME sign, so both sides format identically via `FormatInt`. **Ledger-split dedupe key derivation** (query `LedgerSplitDedupeKeys`): for NON-DELETED splits on the account, `(txn.date, split.amount, payee-name, memo)` where payee = the transaction's payee name (empty if none) and memo = the SPLIT memo, falling back to the TXN memo when the split memo is empty. These are re-hashed in Go to the identical hash a matching bank row would produce.
  - **Dedupe FLAGGING (advisory, never enforced).** `StageImportRows` builds `existingDedupeSet(account)` from BOTH lookup sources — (1) `PendingOrPostedDedupeHashes` (hashes of pending/posted `import_rows` on the account, across ALL batches — a re-upload is a new batch) and (2) the re-hashed ledger-split keys above — then flags a staged row a duplicate if its hash is in that set OR already seen WITHIN the batch (a file listing the same line twice). A duplicate STILL stages as `pending` (the flag is for the p17.3 reviewer). `TestDedupeFlagsExistingSplitsAndPendingRows` posts a real ledger txn and stages a pending row in a prior batch, then re-uploads: the row matching the posted split and the row matching the pending row are both flagged (case/whitespace-varied to prove normalization); a genuinely new row is not.
  - **Store funnel, NO version append.** `CreateMappingProfile`, `CreateImportBatch`, `StageImportRows` all run through the write funnel (rule 2: one `changes` row for the tx boundary + actor) but SKIP the snapshot-from-live version append — the p17.1 non-versioned decision — exactly like `PutRates` and `SetSplitReconciled`. A whole batch's rows stage in ONE `write()` call (one atomic change). **Batch-sub validation** (`TestBatchSubValidated`): `CreateImportBatch` reuses `HasAccountSubsidiaryMap` INSIDE the funnel fn, rejecting a non-membership with the typed `ErrBatchSubsidiaryMismatch` so the change rolls back (no audit trace).
  - **Web flow / routes** (all TxnWrite — importing feeds the ledger): `GET /import` (upload + mapping form), `POST /import/preview` (parse the multipart CSV under the mapping, show 20 rows, NO batch created), `POST /import` (confirm: create the batch + stage all rows). **Subsidiary-first target selection** (`AccountEditorOptions(sub)` — leaf+active accounts mapped to the chosen subsidiary) structurally guarantees the account maps to the subsidiary; the store check is defense-in-depth. **Preview→confirm carry:** an htmx swap loses the `<input type=file>`, so the preview response carries the CSV forward as a `base64.StdEncoding` hidden field (one token) plus the mapping as hidden inputs; confirm RE-PARSES the carried bytes (preview-parse == stage-parse, deterministic), re-applying the size cap to the DECODED bytes (never trust a client hidden field's size). Confirm parses the carried form with `r.ParseForm` (urlencoded), only the initial upload is `ParseMultipartForm`. **All-or-nothing:** the parser flags rows per-row, but staging has no `error` status, so the PREVIEW handler 422s the WHOLE upload (naming the failing row) if ANY row has a parse `Err` — no batch is created — which is also the "bad CSV / bad mapping → clean 422, no batch" requirement. The 20-row PREVIEW cap is display-only; ALL rows stage. The mapping/preview/result are htmx innerHTML swaps into `#import-workspace` (bare partials `import-preview`/`import-result`); a confirmed row flagged duplicate shows an advisory badge. **Profile save AND reuse:** the form offers a `<select name="profile_id">` of saved profiles; when one is chosen, `mappingFrom` loads its stored Config via `GetMappingProfile` (the inline mapping fields are ignored), and the preview flattens the resolved fields into the carried hidden inputs so confirm reads the same concrete values. Every confirmed batch also persists its exact mapping as a profile (named, if the user opted to save; else an auto-dated throwaway) so `import_batches.profile_id` records what produced it.
  - **EU decimal-comma amounts NOT supported (recorded assumption).** `parseMoney` forces `money.NumberPlain` and strips grouping commas, so US/plain decimals (`1,234.56`) parse but EU decimal-comma (`1.234,56`) does not. The step requires EU *dates*, not EU *amounts*; a bank exporting decimal-comma amounts is out of scope for p17.2. Defensible and reversible (a per-config number-format field could be added later).
  - **Tests:** parser table tests (every mode above) + `Normalize`/`DedupeHash` unit tests (stability across formatting, each-component-changes-hash, payee/memo boundary anti-alias). Store: `TestBatchSubValidated`, `TestDedupeFlagsExistingSplitsAndPendingRows`. Web (real mounted router + migrated db): upload→preview→stage happy path with a 25-row CSV proving the 20-cap displays but all 25 stage; a bad mapping → 422 + zero batches; a within-batch duplicate flagged in the result; a saved profile reused (a selected `profile_id` drives the parse even with a wrong inline mapping); perms (TxnRead→403 on GET/preview/stage, TxnWrite→200 GET). i18n `import.*` + `nav.import` in BOTH catalogs (`TestCatalogParity` green; leaf/table collisions avoided by renaming the colliding leaf keys `import.delimiter_label`/`amount_mode_label`/`date_format_label`/`preview_btn` so `import.delimiter.*` etc. can be tables). e2e `bank-import.spec.js`: the admin creates its own asset account, uploads a synthetic CSV with a repeated line, previews (htmx swap → `e2e-settled`), stages, and sees exactly one flagged duplicate — the full parallel suite (41 specs) ran **15× green**. `make lint test check` + `govulncheck ./...` exit 0 (p06.1 informational `x/crypto/openpgp` finding persists). No new deps (stdlib csv/json/sha256/strconv/base64); `go.mod`/`go.sum` unchanged; `make gen` reproducible.

- **p17.3 (web: review queue → post)** — Completes Phase 17. The reviewer works a batch's staged rows: post one to a real balanced ledger transaction (linking the row), or discard it with a reason. Four routes on `internal/web/imports_review.go`; store methods on `internal/store/imports.go`; the "edit & post" reuses the phase-12 editor via a mode flag on `txnEditorModel` (`ImportRowID`/`ImportBatchID`).
  - **Post = create + LINK in ONE change (atomic), NOT two writes.** `PostTransaction`'s body was extracted into a pure `postTransactionTx(ctx, q, changeID, in)` (a no-behavior-change refactor — every existing txn test still green). `PostImportRow(rowID, in)` runs ONE `write()` that: (1) re-reads the row's status on the tx-bound `q`, rejecting non-`pending` with typed `ErrImportRowNotPending`; (2) `postTransactionTx` (the store is the SOLE validator — the normal `validateAndResolve` enforces ≥2 splits + overall AND per-fund zero-sum); (3) `MarkImportRowPosted(txnID)` (status=posted, `posted_transaction_id` set). Two sequential writes were rejected: a crash between commits would leave a posted txn + a still-pending row → a re-post double-posts (a cardinal double-entry bug). The pending-guard (not atomicity alone) is what stops a double-SUBMIT double-posting; the `MarkImportRowPosted` UPDATE also carries `AND status='pending'` as a belt-and-suspenders. The posted transaction is the row's audit (the whole versioned entry); the staging row stays non-versioned (p17.1).
  - **Discard reason = the `changes.note`, NO new column.** `DiscardImportRow(rowID, reason)` rejects an empty/whitespace reason BEFORE the funnel opens (`ErrDiscardReasonRequired` — nothing written), else runs `write(kind="import.row.discard", note=reason, fn: pending-guard → set status='discarded')`. Per p17.1 the discarded row's audit IS that change; the schema was deliberately designed with no `discard_reason` column, so none was added. `TestDiscardRequiresReason` asserts empty→err with zero change rows, and reason→discarded + a change whose `note` equals the reason.
  - **"Edit & post" reuses the phase-12 editor with the subsidiary LOCKED.** A mode flag `ImportRowID` on `txnEditorModel` makes `transaction_form.tmpl` post to `/import/rows/{id}/post`, and locks the subsidiary: a `disabled` `<select>` (does not POST) plus a hidden `subsidiary` carrier, with the sub-change `hx-get` re-filter suppressed (the batch binds ONE sub, D of p17.1). The post handler IGNORES any posted subsidiary and uses the batch's. **Prefill:** row 0 = the batch-account line (signed parsed amount, date, payee name, memo — authoritative from the staged row). The counter-splits reuse the p12.3 payee template: the parsed payee is matched to a known payee by name via a NEW READ-ONLY `LookupPayeeByName` (never `EnsurePayee` at GET — creation is create-on-save on POST), and the template's splits (fund + program + functional class carried) become counter rows, EXCLUDING any split on the batch account (else the bank line doubles) and dropping accounts outside the locked sub. **D20 gotcha handled:** if a counter split carries a restricted fund, the bank line is given the SAME fund so per-fund zero-sum can hold (else the post 422s). No known payee / no template → the bank line + one empty counter row. The user adjusts to balance; the server re-validates.
  - **View perm = TxnWrite (recorded choice).** All four routes (`GET /import/batches/{id}`, `GET /import/rows/{id}/edit`, `POST /import/rows/{id}/post`, `POST /import/rows/{id}/discard`) are TxnWrite — the whole import-into-ledger workflow, incl. VIEWING the staging queue, is write-adjacent and the actions mutate the ledger, so a TxnRead user has no reason to work a queue. Matches the p17.2 `/import**` perm. The permission-matrix + registry-completeness tests pick these up automatically (rule 8) — the matrix app now seeds an import batch + a pending row (id 1) so the `{id}` routes resolve (post/discard on an empty/invalid body 422 — non-404, so "reachable").
  - **Batch progress indicator** ("N of T posted, D discarded, P pending") is computed in Go from the batch's rows (batches are tiny — no aggregate query). The queue re-derives the advisory duplicate flag for PENDING rows via `ImportRowsForBatchFlagged` (the SAME two-source set the staging pass used — pending/posted import rows across batches, counted so a row does not flag ITSELF, plus posted ledger-split keys), so a re-uploaded duplicate keeps showing flagged even though the flag was never persisted at stage time.
  - **Reimport idempotency** rides the p17.2 dedupe unchanged: `TestReimportFlagsDuplicates` posts a staged row, then re-uploads the identical line in a new batch — it stages but is flagged duplicate (its recomputed hash equals the posted row's stored hash, and exactly one txn exists on the account). No double post.
  - **i18n:** new `import.*` leaf keys added to BOTH catalogs; the p17.1 leaf/table-collision watch bit twice and was resolved by keeping leaves flat — `import.progress_posted/_discarded/_pending`, `import.discard_reason_*`, `import.posthdr_*` (so no `import.progress`/`import.post`/`import.discard` acts as both a leaf and a table). Form-error convention honored: an unbalanced post re-renders the editor at 422 with the imbalance routed to the totals bar (reusing `txnSubmit`'s `routeTxnError`/`renderFormError`); a missing discard reason re-renders the queue at 422 with `import.discard_reason_required`.
  - **Tests / DoD:** Store — `TestPostImportRowCreatesBalancedTxnAndLinks` (balanced txn with a fund+class counter, `AssertVersioned` on the txn, row linked posted, appears in the register, re-post→`ErrImportRowNotPending`), `TestPostImportRowUnbalancedRejected` (rolled back, row still pending), `TestDiscardRequiresReason`, `TestReimportFlagsDuplicates`. Web — prefill locks the sub + carries the payee-template fund+class, post links the row + register shows it, unbalanced→422 row-still-pending, discard 422-on-empty then discarded, and TxnRead→403 / TxnWrite→200 across all four routes. e2e `bank-import.spec.js` extended: stage a 2-row statement, follow the review link, "edit & post" one pending row (sub locked, add a counter to balance, post → back to the queue posted) and discard the other with a reason — the full parallel suite (42 specs) ran **15× green**. `make lint test check` + `govulncheck ./...` exit 0 (`cuento check` stays clean — `import_rows` non-versioned, no Z-rule touches it; the p06.1 informational `x/crypto/openpgp` finding persists). No new deps; `go.mod`/`go.sum` unchanged; `make gen` reproducible (3 new import queries + `postTransactionTx` extraction, all ASCII/positional `?`).

- **p18.1 (build: release binary)** — Starts Phase 18. The build version now surfaces on TWO runtime surfaces from ONE ldflags source. The wiring chain: `main.version` (a package var defaulting to `"dev"`) is overridden at release by `go build -ldflags "-X main.version=<git describe>"`; `serve` passes it into `web.Config{Version: version}`; `Config.Version` flows to `/healthz` (JSON `{"status":"ok","version":...}`) and, via `baseData.Version`, into the shell footer partial (`{{t "footer.version" .Shell.Version}}`).
  - **Mostly pre-scaffolded — tests CONFIRM, they did not DRIVE (recorded deviation from AGENTS method 1).** The Makefile `release` target, the `/healthz` JSON handler + `TestHealthz`, the footer template line, both `footer.version` catalog keys, and `baseData.Version` were all built as scaffolding in earlier phases. So the two listed surfaces already rendered before p18.1; a fresh footer test passes immediately rather than failing first. Rather than manufacture a false red, `TestFooterVersion` feeds a DISTINCTIVE `Config.Version` ("v9.9.9-footer-test") and asserts it renders inside the `<footer class="app-footer">` landmark — its discriminating power was verified by momentarily blanking the template's version expression (test goes red: "footer missing version string"). `TestHealthz` already asserted the configured version, so that surface was not duplicated. Only NEW code in this step: the footer test, the e2e footer assertion, a stale-comment fix in `main.go`, this note, and the PLAN tick.
  - **`make release` empirically verified (the load-bearing check).** `CGO_ENABLED=0 GOOS=linux GOARCH=amd64 go build -trimpath -ldflags "-s -w -X main.version=$(VERSION)"` where `VERSION ?= $(shell git describe --tags --always --dirty || echo dev)`. `--always` falls back to the short commit hash when there are no tags, so a release build's version is a real value (`15d6428`), never `"dev"`. Verified on the produced binary: `file` reports `ELF 64-bit ... statically linked ... stripped` (CGO-free static); `strings bin/cuento | grep 15d6428` finds the baked value (`-s -w` strips the symbol table but the version DATA string survives); and running it, `curl /healthz` returns `{"status":"ok","version":"15d6428"}`. NO `version` subcommand was added — the two required surfaces (healthz + footer) cover it and a subcommand would be over-build.
  - **e2e footer assertion is PATTERN-matched, never a literal.** The e2e binary is a plain `make build` (no ldflags), so its footer shows "Version dev". `shell.spec.js` asserts `footer.app-footer` contains `/Version\s+\S+/` — holds for both the "dev" e2e build and a real release describe string, so the spec cannot break on the build path. The version string itself is NOT translated; only the surrounding `footer.version` = "Version %s" label is a catalog key (present in BOTH en/es, parity green).

- **p18.2 (ops: config, TLS, deploy docs)** — `serve` gains a config layer over `CUENTO_*` env + flags, an autocert TLS branch, and the `deploy/` + `docs/deploy.md` ops artifacts for the D8 e2-micro + Litestream→GCS design.
  - **Config precedence: env is the base, an explicitly-passed flag overrides.** Four knobs, each with a flag mirroring an env var: `-data-dir`↔`CUENTO_DATA_DIR`, `-addr`↔`CUENTO_ADDR`, `-domain`↔`CUENTO_DOMAIN`, `-dev`↔`CUENTO_DEV`. `-db` is an explicit override with NO env twin (so the e2e harness's `serve -dev -db <relpath>` keeps resolving to its own file). Resolution lives in a PURE function `resolveConfig(env map[string]string, fs, set) Config` — no `os.Getenv`, no FS, no clock — so `TestConfigParsing` drives the full matrix without spawning a server. The load-bearing subtlety: the serve flags carry DEFAULTS (`-addr` etc.), and reading a flag value unconditionally would let a default clobber a set env var. So the flags default to `""`/`false` and resolution consults `set` (built by the caller from `fs.Visit`, which visits ONLY explicitly-passed flags) — a flag contributes only when in `set`. `TestConfigParsing` asserts this with the discriminating **env-only** case (env set, no args → env wins over the flag default), plus flag-overrides-env, defaults-when-neither, explicit-`-db`-wins-and-stays-relative, and the `CUENTO_DEV`/`-dev` toggles. `Config.DBPath` is `filepath.Join(DataDir, "cuento.db")` when `-db` is absent (Join, not Abs — Abs reads cwd and would break purity); `serve()` resolves `DataDir` to absolute BEFORE calling `resolveConfig` and re-derives the db path there, honoring the p06.4 db.Open cwd-sensitivity note in production while keeping the tested function hermetic.
  - **TLS decision: `UseTLS() = Domain != "" && !Dev`.** A domain set ⇒ TLS mode; empty ⇒ plain HTTP. `-dev` FORCES plain HTTP even if a domain leaks in from the environment — a non-Secure session cookie (the whole point of `-dev`) over real TLS is incoherent, so dev is always the local plain-HTTP path. This is a listener-mode decision the config test asserts directly (mode + `AutocertCacheDir()` + addrs), so no socket bind and no real-ACME network test is needed.
  - **TLS branch (autocert): :443 + :80 redirect + cache in the data dir.** When `UseTLS()`, `serve` runs `autocert.Manager{Prompt: AcceptTOS, HostPolicy: HostWhitelist(domain), Cache: autocert.DirCache(<data-dir>/autocert)}`, serves HTTPS on **:443** via the manager's `TLSConfig` (`ListenAndServeTLS("","")` — certs come from the manager, no cert/key files), and a **:80** listener running `m.HTTPHandler(nil)` (ACME http-01 challenges + 301-redirect everything else to HTTPS). BOTH servers shut down gracefully on SIGINT/SIGTERM (the single-server graceful path was split into `servePlain`/`serveTLS` sharing a `shutdown` helper; a failure on either listener tears down the other). The autocert cache and the data dir are `MkdirAll`'d at startup with wrapped errors, so a bad config (e.g. an unwritable data dir) fails clean, not with a panic. `serve -h` still exits 0 (flag.ErrHelp handled, not surfaced as a fatal).
  - **autocert is now a DIRECT dep (D15-allowlisted, no new ack needed).** D15 already allowlists `golang.org/x/crypto (autocert)`; it was an INDIRECT require, and importing `golang.org/x/crypto/acme/autocert` promoted it to a direct `require golang.org/x/crypto v0.52.0` (go.mod delta). autocert's `acme` package transitively pulls `golang.org/x/net/idna` (this is what made the first build fail on a missing `x/net/idna` go.sum entry), so `go mod tidy` added `golang.org/x/net v0.55.0 // indirect` to go.mod. `x/net` stays `// indirect` — a FORCED transitive of the pre-approved autocert, NOT a new direct/convenience dep, so it is not a D15 violation. No other deps added. Litestream is an EXTERNAL binary installed on the VM, never a Go import of cuento.
  - **deploy/ artifacts (static, review-quality, D8-shaped).** `cuento.service` — the server as a non-root `cuento` user with the `CUENTO_*` env, `Restart=on-failure`, `AmbientCapabilities=CAP_NET_BIND_SERVICE` + matching `CapabilityBoundingSet` (+ `NoNewPrivileges`) to bind :80/:443 without root, and hardening (`ProtectSystem=strict` with `ReadWritePaths=/var/lib/cuento` so the db/autocert/litestream writes still work, `PrivateTmp`, syscall filter, etc.). `litestream.service` — `litestream replicate` daemon. `litestream.yml` — `/var/lib/cuento/cuento.db` → a GCS replica (`your-bucket` PLACEHOLDER), `snapshot-interval: 24h`, `retention: 720h` (30 days), `sync-interval: 10s`, sized for the 5 GB free tier; GCS auth via the VM's ADC service account (no key in any file, DATA RULE 11). `ratesync.timer` (+ the `ratesync.service` oneshot it triggers) — the p14.2 deferred timer, Mon–Fri 18:30 UTC, `Persistent=true`.
  - **docs/deploy.md — runnable e2-micro walkthrough.** always-free e2-micro in a free-tier US region (us-central1), 30 GB pd-standard, firewall opening only 80/443, binary + Litestream install, non-root user + `/var/lib/cuento` data dir, first-run migrate + `cuento user add admin --admin` (password on STDIN, never argv), autocert first-request provisioning, Litestream setup, a **restore drill** (`litestream restore` to a scratch path → `PRAGMA integrity_check` + `cuento check --strict`) plus real point-in-time DR, the ratesync timer, and a backup-retention/operations summary table. All infra names are placeholders (`books.example.com`, `your-bucket`, `your-project`).

- **p18.3 (web: admin ops page)** — The Admin ops page (`GET /admin/ops`) surfaces three things and adds an audited backup action; two new routes on `internal/web/ops.go`, two new store methods on `internal/store/ops.go`, a new `ops.tmpl`, `admin.ops.*` catalog keys in both catalogs, and the `/admin/ops` link on the admin index. The `server` struct now retains the raw `*sql.DB` (`web.NewApp` already receives it) so the page can run the integrity suite and drive VACUUM INTO.
  - **Page contents.** (1) BUILD INFO — the running `cfg.Version` (the same ldflags string `/healthz` and the footer show, p18.1) plus `runtime.Version()` (the Go runtime). Build TIME was skipped (PLAN marks it "optional" and it is not wired anywhere), so only version + Go version render. (2) INTEGRITY CHECK — the page runs the SAME `ledger.Check` the `cuento check` CLI runs (rule 7's Z1–Z19 suite); `buildOpsModel` groups the returned violations by severity (errors first, then warnings incl. Z17–Z19), sorting each group by rule then detail to match the CLI's deterministic order (`printViolations`), and renders each as rule + detail. A clean db shows a "no violations" notice (`.ops-check-clean`). The check is READ-ONLY — no audit change for viewing. (3) A backup-snapshot action.
  - **Backup = VACUUM INTO a fresh temp path, streamed, then removed.** `POST /admin/ops/backup` calls `store.Backup(path)` which runs `VACUUM INTO ?` on the raw handle — SQLite's built-in consistent-snapshot primitive (works on modernc.org/sqlite; the path is a BOUND parameter, so rule 6 holds even for this const-SQL site). VACUUM cannot run inside a transaction, so `Backup` deliberately bypasses the write funnel (a read-side consistency op, like the config upserts under rule 2). The handler targets a UNIQUE path inside a per-request `os.MkdirTemp` dir (VACUUM INTO REFUSES an existing db file — "output file already exists" — verified in `TestBackupRefusesExistingTarget`; a unique path also makes concurrent backups collision-free), streams the file as `Content-Type: application/octet-stream` + `Content-Disposition: attachment; filename="cuento-backup-<ts>.db"`, and `defer os.RemoveAll(dir)` cleans up the temp dir (no leak). The LIVE db file is never served directly — VACUUM INTO gives a transactionally consistent copy even under concurrent writes.
  - **Backup is a POST, not a GET download link (recorded choice).** The action MUTATES the audit trail, and rule 13 requires cross-origin protection on all mutating routes — which the middleware applies to non-GET methods, not idempotent GET. A `GET .../backup.db` writing an audit row would be an unprotected mutating route (a defect even if tests pass). So the action is `POST /admin/ops/backup` whose response body IS the download; the e2e drives it via `page.request.post` (same session cookie + matching Origin ⇒ the guard passes).
  - **Backup is AUDITED, snapshot-first (rule 14).** `store.RecordBackup` writes exactly ONE `changes` row (kind `ops.backup`, the acting admin as actor) through the write funnel with a no-op fn — no versioned/live row (the same shape as the reconciliation-boundary and seed changes). The handler records the audit ONLY AFTER the VACUUM succeeds, so a failed backup leaves no misleading audit trace (mirroring the funnel's "rejected ops leave no audit row"). No Z-rule ties `changes` to a `*_versions` twin, so a version-less `ops.backup` change keeps `cuento check` clean (verified empirically before building, and by the store test).
  - **No new sqlc queries, no new deps.** The audit reuses the existing `InsertChange` (via the funnel); the VACUUM is the sanctioned raw-SQL/bound-param site; the tests read `changes` by kind via raw SQL (in-convention, p05.3) — so the sqlc query gotcha is sidestepped entirely. i18n keys are namespaced under `admin.ops.*` as TABLES with no bare `admin.ops` leaf (dotted-key/leaf-collision watch), parity green.
  - **Tests.** Store: `Backup` produces a file that opens + passes `PRAGMA quick_check` == "ok" + carries the schema/data (seeded system user); `Backup` refuses an existing db path; `RecordBackup` writes one `ops.backup` change naming the actor and requires an actor. Web (real mounted router + migrated db): GET renders version + Go version + the clean notice; non-admin 403 on GET AND on the backup POST (backup 403 writes no `ops.backup` change); THE key test — the backup POST body written to a temp file opens, `PRAGMA quick_check` == "ok", and the users table is present; the backup POST writes exactly one `ops.backup` change naming the admin; an induced Z17 warning (one leg flagged `intercompany` via raw SQL so its splits net non-zero per currency) renders with `data-rule="Z17"` + `data-severity="warning"` + its detail. The permission-matrix + registry-completeness tests pick up both new routes automatically (rule 8) — the matrix's admin persona actually runs the backup (200 octet-stream = allow), a non-admin gets 403. e2e `ops.spec.js`: an admin opens `/admin/ops`, sees the version + a `go\d…` runtime + the clean notice, and `page.request.post('/admin/ops/backup')` returns a 200 octet-stream attachment whose bytes begin with the SQLite magic header.

- **p18.4 (hardening sweep — COMPLETES Phase 18)** — A tests-plus-docs pass; no feature behavior changed. It locks the security posture (rule 13) against every current and future route, proves the strict CSP is honored across the whole UI, and confirms the dep/vuln/session/parity state. New: `docs/security.md` (threat model), `internal/web/headers_test.go`, `e2e/tests/csp-clean.spec.js`. One code touch: HSTS made prod-only in `internal/web/middleware.go`.
  - **Security-header sweep — the key test.** `TestSecurityHeadersEveryRoute` reuses the permission-matrix harness (`newMatrixApp`) and iterates the LIVE route registry as the Admin persona, asserting the header VALUES against the middleware's own constants (`contentSecurityPolicy` etc.) so test and middleware cannot drift. Because `secureHeaders` is the OUTERMOST middleware (chain), the headers land on EVERY response before enforce/handlers run — 200/302/403/404, `/healthz` JSON, `/static`, the ops octet-stream — so the sweep is STATUS-INDEPENDENT and needs no per-route exception. Asserted on every route: `Content-Security-Policy` (== the strict const), `X-Content-Type-Options: nosniff`, `X-Frame-Options: DENY`, `Referrer-Policy: same-origin`, `Cross-Origin-Opener-Policy: same-origin`. It is a LOCK-IN test (passes on first run; a route added later is covered with zero edits, rule 8) — verified to BITE by momentarily dropping `X-Frame-Options` (test went red on every route) then restoring.
  - **HSTS made prod-only (recorded choice).** The sweep revealed the one commonly-expected header absent: `Strict-Transport-Security`. It is now emitted (`max-age=31536000; includeSubDomains`) but ONLY outside `-dev`, gated on `!cfg.Dev` exactly like the Secure-cookie flag — sending HSTS over the `-dev` plain-HTTP server would pin a developer's browser to https for an http-only host. `secureHeaders` became `secureHeaders(prod bool)` (a closure); `TestHSTSDevVsProd` pins present-in-prod / absent-in-dev while confirming the always-on headers appear in both modes. No other header is conditional.
