  - **CSP console clean — the -dev click-through.** `e2e/tests/csp-clean.spec.js` logs in and walks every main page (phases 10–18) — including the richest server-rendered UI where an inline `style="…"` would hide: the transaction EDITOR (`/transactions/new`, the p12.2 split grid) and a concrete report DETAIL (`/reports/trial_balance`, column/total alignment) — plus the `-dev`-only styleguide gallery and an htmx-swapped partial, asserting ZERO CSP violations. Detector: `page.on('console')` + `page.on('pageerror')` matching the browser's CSP-refusal wording / `SecurityPolicyViolation` — navigation-safe (an `addInitScript` window-array resets per load, so it is not relied on alone). Verified NOT VACUOUS: a deliberately injected `style="color:red"` in `accounts.tmpl` made the spec go red with Chromium's "Refused to apply inline style … style-src 'self'" message; injection reverted. Clean on the real UI ⇒ no inline script/style slipped in across all phases (rule 12).
  - **Catalog parity — already enforced, confirmed green.** `internal/i18n: TestCatalogParity` already flattens both catalogs to go-i18n message IDs and compares BOTH directions with the final key set; no orphan (en-only or es-only) key. No second test written (would duplicate); confirmed passing.
  - **Deps — nothing to prune; D15 line updated.** The 10 DIRECT `require`s in `go.mod` all sit on the D15 allowlist: `modernc.org/sqlite`, `pressly/goose/v3`, `alexedwards/scs/v2` (+`sqlite3store`), `alexedwards/argon2id`, `golang.org/x/crypto` (autocert), `golang.org/x/time` (rate), plus the bilingual stack `nicksnyder/go-i18n/v2` + `BurntSushi/toml` + `golang.org/x/text` (D14). No stray direct dep; `go mod tidy` leaves `go.mod`/`go.sum` unchanged. `google/go-cmp` (D15's tests entry) is allowlisted but currently unused — allowed-but-absent, not a violation. The D15 SETTLED-DECISIONS ROW predated the i18n stack and omitted go-i18n/toml/x/text; updated in place to list them (a staleness fix, not a history rewrite).
  - **govulncheck green.** `govulncheck ./...` reports 0 vulnerabilities in cuento's code / imports; the one advisory in a required module is not reachable from our call graph. Noted in `docs/security.md`.
  - **Session lifetime — reviewed, unchanged.** `internal/web/session.go`: absolute Lifetime 12 h, IdleTimeout 2 h, cookie `HttpOnly` + `SameSite=Lax` + `Path=/` + `Secure` outside `-dev`. Sane for the bookkeeper workflow (a working day, an idle-tab de-auth, not indefinite); no change. Documented in `docs/security.md`.
  - **`make check` vs the go-live gate.** Hermetic `make check` (fresh migrated db → `cuento check`) is CLEAN. The strict `make golive-check` runs `cuento check --strict` on the LOCAL, gitignored `fixtures/sample.db` (D26 human-review gate, NOT routine CI). The local `sample.db` present in this environment is STALE — it predates the Phase-16 `reconciliations` migration, so `--strict` errors on `no such table: reconciliations`. That is a local-fixture-regeneration matter (`make fixture`, which reads the gitignored real export — a human step), NOT a code defect in this step; per PLAN the step is not failed on `sample.db` state.

- **p19.1 (db+store: named schedules + budget model — starts Phase 19)** — Budgets project revenue/expense FLOWS onto DISCRETE occurrence DATES (the amount lands in FULL on each date; NO pro-rata — reports p19.2+ bucket occurrences by their period and sum). Migration **00016** adds four versioned business tables (+ standard `_versions` twins, snapshot-from-live, mirroring the funds pattern 00009 EXACTLY) and the store CRUD; the PURE date-expansion engine lives in the new `internal/budget` package. Schema + versioned store CRUD + the expansion engine ONLY — no toolkit (p19.2), no web (p19.3).
  - **The schema.** `budget_schedules(id, name, kind CHECK(onetime/annual/monthly/semimonthly/biweekly/weekly/custom), day_of_month, day_of_month_2, ordinal, weekday, anchor_date GLOB YYYY-MM-DD, weekend_adjust CHECK(actual/prev_business_day/next_business_day) DEFAULT 'prev_business_day', notes)` — a NAMED, reusable recurrence; the kind-specific fields are nullable and validated PER KIND in the store (NOT via cross-field SQL CHECKs — the pure engine is the single source of the date-math rules). `budget_schedule_dates(schedule_id→budget_schedules, occurs_on GLOB YYYY-MM-DD, PK(schedule_id,occurs_on))` — the custom/imported explicit date list. `budgets(id, name, period_start, period_end, notes)` — a named period (horizon ≤ ~1 fiscal year is store-checked in p19.2+; the schema only shape-validates the dates). `budget_lines(id, budget_id→budgets, subsidiary_id→subsidiaries, account_id→accounts, fund_id NULL=unrestricted→funds, program_id NOT NULL→programs, amount INTEGER minor, currency→currencies, schedule_id→budget_schedules)` — one budgeted flow keyed by (sub, R/E account, fund, program) + amount-per-occurrence + a schedule. Each versioned table gets a `_versions` twin with the standard shape (entity_id, change_id→changes, valid_from, op CHECK(create/update/delete), then the full business-column snapshot with NO CHECK/FK — history, not live).
  - **program_id is NOT NULL on budget_lines (recorded choice).** The task annotates only `fund_id` as `NULL=unrestricted`. `program_id` is REQUIRED: the ledger already requires a program on every R/E split (Z15), a budget is of R/E flows, and p19.2's `ActualsVsBudget` matches per (sub,account,fund,program) — so every budget line names a program. `fund_id` stays nullable (unrestricted budgeting is a real case).
  - **amount is a POSITIVE magnitude, per occurrence (store-checked > 0, `ErrBudgetAmount`).** Direction/sign comes from the account TYPE at report time (revenue vs expense), not from the stored amount — so a line stores the flow's magnitude, always positive.
  - **budget_schedule_dates is versioned as a composite membership SET (like fund_subsidiaries), NOT left unversioned.** entity_id = schedule_id; `occurs_on` is BOTH the snapshot column AND part of the composite identity. Importing a date appends op='create'; removing one appends op='delete' captured BEFORE the live DELETE (the removal-op ordering — the live row must still exist to snapshot). This keeps the custom date list audited under the same discipline as every other business table and keeps Z3/Z5 clean, rather than carving a `splits.reconciliation_id`-style exemption for a genuinely versioned import.
  - **DeleteBudgetLine HARD-deletes with an op='delete' version (rule 14).** Rule 14's "soft-delete only for transactions" means everything ELSE that deletes hard-deletes WITH an audit version: `DeleteBudgetLine` appends the op='delete' snapshot BEFORE removing the live row, leaving no live row but a permanent snapshot. budget_lines is the first single-id business entity that hard-deletes; Z3's single-id block handles it (a deleted live row is simply absent — not flagged — while its 'delete' version legitimately persists).
  - **The expansion engine (`internal/budget.ExpandSchedule(s Schedule, from, to string) ([]string, error)`) is PURE and CLOCK-FREE.** Same inputs → same output; no DB, no `time.Now()` (the horizon is a param), UTC-only calendar math via stdlib `time` (no new dep). It returns sorted, DEDUPLICATED "YYYY-MM-DD" strings within the INCLUSIVE `[from,to]` horizon. Kinds: `onetime` (a single anchor); `annual` (the anchor's month+day each year — a Feb-29 anchor CLAMPS to Feb-28 in a non-leap year); `monthly` (EITHER a day-of-month, clamped for short months, OR an ordinal weekday e.g. "2nd Monday" / "last Friday"); `semimonthly` (two days per month); `biweekly` (every 14 days from the anchor, walked BOTH directions so an anchor before/after `from` is handled with no negative-modulo bug — naturally 3-in-a-month and crosses year boundaries); `weekly` (a weekday aligned to the anchor's week); `custom` (the imported list). Month-end uses the day-0-of-next-month idiom; a `-1` day-of-month / ordinal is the month-end / "last" sentinel.
  - **CLAMP THEN WEEKEND-ADJUST, in that order (the classic ordering bug).** A day-of-month past month-end clamps DOWN to the month's last day (day 31 → Feb 28), and only THEN does a weekend roll apply. E.g. day 31 in Nov 2025 → clamp to Nov 30 (a Sunday) → prev_business_day rolls to Nov 28 (Fri) — a table-tested combined case.
  - **Weekend adjustment applies to EXACTLY monthly-by-day-of-month and semimonthly.** Those are the only kinds that can land a chosen calendar day on Sat/Sun. `onetime`, `annual`, ordinal-weekday-monthly, `biweekly`, `weekly`, and `custom` are weekday-anchored or authoritative by construction and are NEVER adjusted (an annual/ordinal date landing on a weekend stays put — table-tested). Policies: `prev_business_day` (default) rolls a weekend date back to Friday; `next_business_day` rolls forward to Monday; `actual` keeps it. A roll CROSSES the month/year boundary (payroll semantics) and may move a date OUT of the horizon (dropped) or a near-edge date IN — membership is decided on the ADJUSTED date. WEEKENDS ONLY in v1 — NO holiday calendar (holidays → Phase 21 backlog).
  - **The four versioned twins enter the Z3/Z5 sets.** `internal/ledger/checks.go` gained a Z3 UNION-ALL block per new table (single-id blocks for budget_schedules / budgets / budget_lines comparing every business column; a composite membership block + a dangling-snapshot block for budget_schedule_dates, mirroring fund_subsidiaries) and four new Z5 entries (each `_versions` twin's change_id → changes). Proven both ways: `TestBudgetTablesCheckClean` builds a budget+schedule+line through the store and asserts the full suite stays clean on real versioned data (empty tables pass trivially — this gives the new blocks actual rows), and three bite tests corrupt a throwaway copy (`TestBudgetLineZ3Bites` tampers a live amount; `TestBudgetScheduleDateZ3Bites` deletes a live date leaving a dangling 'create'; `TestBudgetZ5Bites` points a version at a missing change) each asserting the right rule fires. NOTE: `reconciliations_versions` remains ABSENT from Z3/Z5 — a pre-existing Phase-16 gap, NOT touched here; the new twins do not replicate that omission.
  - **R/E validation + ref checks (store, inside the funnel's fn so a rejection rolls the change back).** A budget line's account must be revenue or expense (`ErrBudgetLineAccountNotRE` — a balance-sheet account is rejected: a budget is of R/E FLOWS); the budget/subsidiary/program/schedule/currency must exist and the fund must exist if set (`ErrBudgetRefMissing`); amount > 0 (`ErrBudgetAmount`). Schedule field consistency is validated by feeding the PURE engine a fixed 1-day horizon — its per-kind field validation runs regardless of whether an occurrence lands, so a missing/contradictory selector surfaces as `ErrScheduleInvalid` (keeping the single source of the rules in `internal/budget`, no duplicated per-kind checks in the store). Deliberately NOT added: the full ledger scope invariants (Z11/Z13/Z15 account-mapped-to-sub, fund-scoped-to-sub, program-in-fund-subtree) — not asked for at p19.1 and would be over-build; budgeting is a projection layer, and the ledger enforces those on the ACTUAL posted transactions.
  - **Versioned CRUD (AssertVersioned).** `CreateSchedule`/`UpdateSchedule` (+ importing/diffing the custom date list), `CreateBudget`/`UpdateBudget`, `CreateBudgetLine`/`UpdateBudgetLine`/`DeleteBudgetLine` — each ONE change through the write funnel, live-write-first then snapshot-from-live. Tests assert create→'create', update→'update', delete→'delete' via `testutil.AssertVersioned` (single-id) and a local composite helper for schedule dates; one-change atomicity is asserted by a change-count delta, and rejected ops are asserted to mint ZERO changes.
  - **No new deps; sqlc gotcha honored.** Stdlib `time` only. `internal/db/queries/budgets.sql` is pure ASCII; version-append queries use plain positional `?` (op, change_id, entity_id → Op/ID/ID_2; the composite date-version → Op/ID/ScheduleID/OccursOn); `make gen` regenerated `internal/db/sqlc`.
- **p19.2 (toolkit: occurrences, actuals-vs-budget, projections)** — Two budget methods on `reports.Toolkit` layered over p19.1 (`internal/budget.ExpandSchedule` + the budget store reads) and the p15.2 actuals toolkit. Both are PURE reads (rule 2), native currency (no conversion — like the other activity toolkits), int64 minor (rule 3), and CLOCK-FREE (the period is a param). New file `internal/reports/budget.go` (+ `budget_test.go`); one new sqlc read (`BudgetKeyActivity`) + its store wrapper; two new `Granularity` values.
  - **Signatures.** `BudgetVsActual(ctx, s Scope, budgetID int64, from, to string, g Granularity) ([]BudgetVsActualCell, error)` — this is the step's "ActualsVsBudget" (named `BudgetVsActual` in code). `CashflowProjection(ctx, s Scope, budgetID int64, from, to string) (map[FundCurrency]ProjectionSeries, error)`. Types: `BudgetKey{Subsidiary, Account, Fund (0=unrestricted), Program, Currency}`; `BudgetVsActualCell{Bucket, Key, Budgeted, Actual, Variance}`; `FundCurrency{Fund, Currency}`; `ProjectionSeries{Start, End, Buckets []string, At map[string]int64}`.
  - **NO pro-rata (the design point) — deterministic occurrence bucketing.** Each budget line's schedule is expanded (`ExpandSchedule` over [from,to]) to concrete occurrence DATES, and each occurrence's FULL amount lands in the SINGLE bucket its own date falls in — never spread. `bucketKey(date, g)` maps a date to its period-start "YYYY-MM-DD": week→the Monday on-or-before (ISO week start), month→YYYY-MM-01, quarter→Jan/Apr/Jul/Oct-01, year→YYYY-01-01. Actuals are bucketed by the SAME function (each split by its own date), so budgeted and actual share the bucketing. Asserted: a monthly-DoM-15 line over July 2026 shown WEEKLY puts its whole 100,000 in exactly ONE weekly bucket (Monday 2026-07-13), zero in every other week.
  - **Week + year granularity added.** `params.go` gained `GranWeek` (ISO Monday-start; the week's bucket key is the starting Monday's date) and `GranYear` (YYYY-01-01), APPENDED after `GranQuarter` so existing iota values / URL tokens don't renumber; `String()`/`ParseGranularity` round-trip "week"/"year". Bucketing does NOT route weeks through `ByPeriod` (which is calendar-month-anchored) — each occurrence buckets by its own date, which is what makes the no-pro-rata guarantee clean.
  - **Sign convention.** A budget line's stored amount is a POSITIVE magnitude; the toolkit signs it BY ACCOUNT TYPE into Activity's net-debit space — an EXPENSE line budgets a POSITIVE net-debit, a REVENUE line a NEGATIVE one — so budgeted and actual are directly comparable (types read once via `store.Tree`, as `FundPeriodStatement` does). **Variance = actual − budgeted** (positive = higher net-debit than budget: expense OVERSPEND / revenue UNDER-collection). `CashflowProjection` FLIPS the sign for a fund's spendable position: `delta = −(net-debit)`, so a revenue occurrence INCREASES and an expense occurrence DECREASES the fund (mirroring `FundPeriodStatement`'s Received/Applied folding).
  - **Actuals per (sub,account,fund,program) — new sqlc read, NOT DrillSplits.** The p15.2 `Activity` is account-only, and `DrillSplits` cannot isolate the unrestricted group (`FundID==nil` means "any fund", never "NULL only"). So p19.2 adds `BudgetKeyActivity(from,to,scopeSub)` — R/E splits grouped by `(t.subsidiary_id, sp.account_id, COALESCE(sp.fund_id,0), sp.program_id, t.currency, t.date)`, same scope-closure CTE and `t.deleted=0` as the other balance queries. The `COALESCE→0` matches `FundBalancesAsOf`/D20 and lets the fund-0 key be isolated. Asserted on the fixture's 2025-05-10 mixed-funding txn: the BecaAgua half (300,000) and the unrestricted half (200,000) resolve to SEPARATE keys, proving the fund-0 isolation a DrillSplits-nil impl would silently merge to 500,000. Keying by SUBSIDIARY: `BudgetKeyActivity` uses the scope descendant closure, so for a LEAF sub the key's subsidiary is exact; a parent-sub budget line consolidates its descendants (document, matching how the rest of the toolkit consolidates).
  - **Budgeted is NOT scope-filtered; actual is scope-closed (recorded).** `resolveBudgetLines` reads ALL of a budget's lines regardless of the query Scope, while `BudgetKeyActivity` is descendant-closed to the Scope. Each budgeted cell carries its own subsidiary in the key, so the report reconciles per key; the two agree wherever the query scope's closure covers the budget's subsidiaries (always true at root — the intended usage). At a leaf scope with out-of-scope budget lines, budgeted cells with zero actual can appear, which is a faithful "this line's subsidiary is outside the report scope" signal rather than a bug. p19.4 renders at the budget's natural (root/consolidated) scope.
  - **ByPeriod extended for the new granularities (regression guard).** Because `GranWeek`/`GranYear` join the SHARED `Granularity` enum that `ByPeriod` (compute.go, the p15.5 comparative-column driver) consumes, `ByPeriod` now handles them explicitly: `GranYear` → a 12-month step, `GranWeek` → a dedicated Monday-start weekly split (`byWeek`). Without this, a resolved `GranYear`/`GranWeek` would have fallen into the month-step path and silently produced monthly columns. The budget toolkit itself buckets via `bucketKey` (not `ByPeriod`), but the enum is shared so the driver had to keep pace.
  - **CashflowProjection start + roll-forward.** Start = the CURRENT actual net-asset fund balances `FundBalancesAsOf(from, scope)` per (fund, currency) — the period START, as-of `from`. Test fixtures are designed with NO occurrence on `from` (period starts 2026-07-01, after the last fixture txn 2026-06-10), so from-vs-(from−1) cannot move a number. Budgeted occurrences then roll FORWARD chronologically per (fund, currency), producing a running balance at each flow date and the final `End`. Hand-computed: BecaAgua/MXN start 9,700,000 + budgeted revenue 1,000,000 − budgeted expense 400,000 = end 10,300,000; BecaAgua/USD start==end==50,000 (no budgeted flow). Per fund and per currency, restricted (BecaAgua) tracked separately from unrestricted (fund 0), D20. BecaAgua spans US+MX, so the projection is run at ROOT scope to see its consolidated balance.

- **p19.3 (web: schedules + budget management)** — The management UI over p19.1: a schedule LIBRARY, a budget LIST + detail, and a budget-line EDITOR with sub-scoped fund/account selectors. Reports (forecast/actuals/cashflow) are p19.4 — deliberately NOT built here. New: `internal/web/budgets.go` (+ `budgets_test.go`), templates `schedules.tmpl` / `schedule_form.tmpl` / `budgets.tmpl` / `budget_form.tmpl` / `budget_detail.tmpl` / `budget_line_form.tmpl`, the kind-picker ES module `static/budgetkind.js` (+ `.test.js`), `error.budget.*`/`budget.*` catalog keys in both catalogs, the `nav.budgets` entry, two thin store read wrappers (`ListSchedules`/`ListBudgets` over the existing p19.1 sqlc queries — no new sqlc, no migration), and `e2e/tests/budgets.spec.js`. Recorded choices:
  - **Manage perm = TxnWrite (view = TxnRead).** Budgets are PLANNING/BOOKKEEPING data, exactly like fund GRANTS (p12.5) and programs (p11.5, D24): the VIEW routes (list, detail, schedule library) are TxnRead — they feed the p19.4 reports — and every create/edit/delete MUTATION is TxnWrite. Subsidiaries/users stay Admin (unchanged). Matches funds management; the permission-matrix test auto-covers the new routes, and a dedicated test asserts TxnRead→403 / TxnWrite→ok beyond the matrix.
  - **URL scheme: schedules at `/schedules`, NOT `/budgets/schedules`.** The task offered "`/budgets/schedules` or under `/budgets`". A budget line's routes are nested `/budgets/{id}/lines/...`; the Go 1.22 mux then CANNOT disambiguate `POST /budgets/{id}/lines` from `POST /budgets/schedules/{id}` (the `{id}` wildcard matches the literal `schedules`, so `/budgets/schedules/lines` satisfies both 3-segment patterns and neither is "more specific") — it panics at mount. Relocating schedules OUTWARD to top-level `/schedules` removes the overlap entirely; the schedule library is reached via a link on `/budgets`, not a nav section. Budgets: `/budgets`, `/budgets/new`, `/budgets/{id}` (detail), `/budgets/{id}/edit`; lines: `/budgets/{id}/lines/new`, `/budgets/{id}/lines/{lid}/edit`, POST `.../lines`, POST `.../lines/{lid}`, POST `.../lines/{lid}/delete`.
  - **Kind picker = show/hide ES module, NOT an hx-get re-fetch.** The schedule form renders ALL kind-specific field blocks at once (each tagged `data-kind-field="<kinds>"`, the weekend-policy block `data-kind-weekend="monthly semimonthly"`); `budgetkind.js` shows the block(s) for the chosen kind and hides the rest on a kind change, with NO server round-trip. The task offered this as the preferred alternative to a self-swapping hx-get precisely because it AVOIDS the htmx settle race on the kind select (the account-form type select's hazard): there is no swap on kind change, so nothing to wait for. The module re-initializes on `DOMContentLoaded` and `htmx:afterSwap`, guarded so importing under Node is side-effect free; its pure decision (`blockVisible`) is node-tested. Two consequences of rendering-all-then-toggling-visibility, both handled: (a) the module `<script>` is loaded by the LIBRARY PAGE (`schedules.tmpl`), NOT inside the swapped-in `schedule-form` partial — a `<script>` injected via htmx `innerHTML` does not execute, so the page-level module self-inits on `DOMContentLoaded` and re-runs on `afterSwap` when the form is swapped into `#schedule-form`. (b) `hidden` does NOT stop form submission (only `disabled` does), so a browser posts EVERY block's controls; controls that would otherwise share a field NAME across blocks (`day_of_month`, `weekday`, `anchor_date`) carry KIND-UNIQUE names on the later block (`sm_day_of_month`, `weekly_weekday`, `weekly_anchor`) and the handler reads the owning block's value per kind (`r.PostFormValue` returns the first-in-DOM control for a shared name — without this, semimonthly/weekly would read the hidden monthly block's defaults and 422). The handler test posts the way the real DOM serializes (adding the colliding default controls) so the collision is actually guarded, and every kind is smoke-covered; the e2e drives a real semimonthly kind SWITCH. The store's engine remains the sole validator of field consistency (`ErrScheduleInvalid`).
  - **Sub-scoped fund/account selectors on the line editor (server round-trip), like the transaction editor (p12.2).** The line form's account options are the R/E LEAVES in the chosen subsidiary (`AccountEditorOptions` filtered to revenue/expense — a budget is of R/E flows, so a balance-sheet account is never offered) and the fund options are `ActiveFunds(sub)` (D20). Changing the subsidiary re-fetches the line form via hx-get with the chosen `subsidiary`, so the SERVER re-filters (server is the source of truth for fund scope). This IS a swapping path, so the e2e waits for `e2e-settled` before driving the re-rendered selects and uses `saveAndReload`. Programs are NOT sub-scoped (all active, tree order) — matching the transaction editor's actual behavior (programs are a global dimension, not subsidiary-scoped); "reuse that approach" governs over the literal "fund/program scoped to the sub" wording. KNOWN LIMITATION (recorded, not fixed here): the sub-change re-fetch rebuilds the line form from only the `subsidiary` param, so it does NOT echo the user's in-progress account/fund/program/amount/schedule the way the txn editor preserves rows via `hx-include`+echo. In practice the subsidiary is the FIRST field chosen (it scopes the rest), so re-selecting it mid-entry is rare; preserving partial entry across the re-filter is a small follow-up (the txn editor's echo pattern applies) and does not affect correctness — the store re-validates every field on submit.
  - **Weekend policy is shown for the day-of-month kinds only.** The weekend-adjust select renders inside a block tagged `data-kind-weekend="monthly semimonthly"`, so the JS reveals it only for monthly and semimonthly (the only kinds that can land on a weekend; ordinal-weekday / biweekly / weekly are weekday-anchored by construction, per the engine). Default is `prev_business_day` (the engine + schema default).
  - **Occurrence preview: NOT built.** The task marked it "optional / nice for usability." CRUD + validation + perms + e2e are the required surface; a live `ExpandSchedule` preview was skipped to keep the step tight (it can land later without schema/route change). The schedule LIST does render a compact one-line summary of each schedule's key selector (day/anchor/ordinal-weekday) for scannability.
  - **Validation → field-error mapping (translation only; the store validates).** `ErrBudgetLineAccountNotRE`→`account_id`, `ErrBudgetAmount`→`amount`, `ErrBudgetRefMissing`→`schedule_id`, `ErrBudgetNotFound`/`ErrBudgetLineNotFound`→`account_id`; `ErrScheduleInvalid`→the kind select (so focus lands on the picker), `ErrScheduleNotFound`→`name`. Two edge checks the store does not own live at the form edge: an unparseable custom-date line (`error.budget.custom_date_invalid`) and budget period ordering/required (`error.budget.period_required`/`period_order`, a plain ISO string compare since `YYYY-MM-DD` sorts). All dates (anchor, custom list, period bounds) parse through `money.ParseDate` in the user's `date_format` and render back through `money.FormatDate` (rule 10 — no `input[type=date]`, no raw `time.Parse`/`strconv` on a date path); amounts through `money.Parse`/`money.Format`.

- **p19.4 (reports: forecast/actuals-vs-budget + cashflow projection — COMPLETES Phase 19)** — Two Phase-15-shaped reports over the p19.2 toolkit (`BudgetVsActual` / `CashflowProjection`), no new sqlc/migration. New `internal/reports/budget_reports.go` (+ `budget_reports_test.go` + goldens `testdata/actuals_vs_budget.{txt,csv}` / `cashflow_projection.{txt,csv}`); the new `budget` report group; a `Budget` report param + full web plumbing; the shared granularity select gains week/year options; catalog keys in both en/es. Recorded choices:
  - **New `budget` report GROUP (mirrors p16.4's `reconciliation`).** Added the single string `"budget"` to `reports.Groups()` — it flows automatically to `codeReportGroups()`→`SyncReportGroups` (report_groups), the admin grant UI, the permission matrix, and the /reports index (all iterate `Groups()`/`All()`). Both budget reports live in it, so an org can grant a budget owner the forecast/variance view without exposing the ledger statements. i18n label `reports.group.budget`. The registry-sync unit test's hardcoded expected set and the financial-grant index test's must-not-appear set were updated to include the new group/report ids; a budget-granted index test mirrors `TestReportsIndexReconciliationGrant`.
  - **TWO reports, not one with a mode.** The two concerns are distinct — a forecast/VARIANCE table vs. a projected-BALANCE series — so two reports (`actuals_vs_budget`, `cashflow_projection`) is clearer than one with a mode param. Both share the group and the `{Period, Granularity, Budget}` ParamsSpec.
  - **`Budget` param (mirrors Account/Fund/Program/Reconciliation).** `ParamsSpec.Budget`/`Params.Budget` + `?budget=` parse/validate against `ListBudgets` in `resolveParams`, a `budget` selector in the shared params form, options via `budgetReportOptions`. No budget chosen (Budget==0) → empty Table (nothing-to-show, a bare hit still 200s). **Default period = the chosen budget's own period:** when a budget is selected and the user has NOT supplied `from`/`to`, `resolveParams` reads the budget's `PeriodStart`/`PeriodEnd` (via the already-fetched `GetBudget`) as the from/to default — the natural forecast window, overriding the generic YTD default.
  - **Variance = Actual − Budgeted (p19.2 sign, reused verbatim).** Positive = higher net-debit than budget = expense OVERSPEND / revenue UNDER-collection. The report renders the toolkit's `BudgetVsActualCell.{Budgeted,Actual,Variance}` directly; a per-currency total row re-derives Σvariance = Σactual − Σbudgeted. Hand-verified numbers are the p19.2 fixtures REUSED: BecaAgua 2025-05 budgeted 250,000 / actual 300,000 / variance +50,000; the fund-0-isolated unrestricted actual 200,000 (budgeted 0, variance +200,000).
  - **NO pro-rata visible in the golden.** Rows are keyed by (bucket, budget-line key) with the bucket as the first column, so a MONTHLY line shows its full amount in exactly ONE bucket row (asserted: budgeted 250,000 appears in a single row across the year). Granularity defaults to month when unset (the report needs bucketing to show occurrences).
  - **Drill on the ACTUAL cell only; UNRESTRICTED cells NOT drillable.** The budgeted column is a plan (not transactions) → never drillable. The actual cell drills (`DrillPeriod`) to its contributing splits, filtered by the key's account+fund+program+currency and the BUCKET's date span **clamped to `[from,to]`** (`max(bucketStart,from)`/`min(bucketEnd,to)`) — a Monday-start week bucket can begin before `from`, so the clamp is what makes the drilled native sum equal the cell (reconciliation invariant; asserted on the restricted BecaAgua 300,000 actual). **The drill Scope is the KEY's own subsidiary, NOT the report scope:** `BudgetKeyActivity` groups actuals by `t.subsidiary_id` so each cell is per-subsidiary, while `DrillSplits` closes the descendant set of its Scope — drilling with a consolidated report scope would sum a sibling sub's matching splits and over-count. Using `key.Subsidiary` (closure `{itself}` for a leaf) makes the drilled sum equal the per-subsidiary cell at ANY report scope, by construction rather than by data coincidence. **Consequence (recorded):** at a consolidated (root) scope the table can carry two rows with identical account/fund/program/currency/bucket but different posting subsidiaries; they are correct and never double-count each other (each drills only its own sub), and the report is designed for the budget's natural root scope — a subsidiary column is a possible later refinement, not required here. An UNRESTRICTED (fund 0) actual cell is left non-drillable: the drill store query filters `sp.fund_id = ?`, which cannot express fund-IS-NULL (a nil `FundID` means "any fund" and would sum every fund, not reconcile) — the same p19.2-recorded `DrillSplits` limitation. Added a `bucketEnd`/`nextDay` helper pair to `budget.go`.
  - **Cashflow start + roll-forward + per-bucket sampling.** Start = `FundBalancesAsOf(from)` per (fund, currency); the report samples the projected running balance at each bucket's END (the `At` of the latest `FlowDate` ≤ bucket end, else `Start`), and End = `Start` + all budgeted flows. Columns: Fund | Currency | Start | <bucket-end date…> | End. Hand-verified: BecaAgua/MXN start 9,700,000 → 10,700,000 after the 2026-08 revenue → 10,300,000 after the 2026-09 expense = End 10,300,000 (root scope, since BecaAgua spans US+MX); BecaAgua/USD start==end==50,000 (no flow). No drill (a projection is a plan). Restricted (BecaAgua) vs unrestricted (fund 0) tracked separately, D20.
  - **Shared granularity select gains week/year (regression-checked).** The report.tmpl granularity control offered none/month/quarter; week+year (already in `ParseGranularity` and `ByPeriod`, extended at p19.2) were added as options with `reports.gran.week`/`reports.gran.year` in both catalogs. `ByPeriod` already handles them (verified in compute.go), so exposing them app-wide does not regress the income statement (its golden pins its own granularity; no test asserts the option set).

- **p20.1 (db+store: expense-report model + submit permission — starts Phase 20)** — A submission->review workflow DECOUPLED from book-editing: a low-privilege SUBMITTER drafts a report of proposed R/E lines (need NOT balance) and submits it; an editing REVIEWER (p20.3) CONVERTS it into a real balanced ledger transaction (linked via `posted_transaction_id`) or REJECTS it with a reason. Migration **00017** adds two versioned business tables (+ `_versions` twins, snapshot-from-live, mirroring the budgets pattern 00016 EXACTLY) and the standalone user capability; store lifecycle + perm plumbing only — NO submitter/reviewer web (p20.2/p20.3). Recorded choices:
  - **`ExpenseSubmit` perm + `can_submit_expenses` column, INDEPENDENT of txn_perm (D10).** A new `Perm` marker `ExpenseSubmit` (a package var like `AnyUser`) + `permExpenseSubmit` kind; `decide()` allows it iff `u.CanSubmitExpenses` (or admin, via the is-admin short-circuit) — it reads ONLY the flag, so txn_perm-independence is by construction: a pure submitter (`can_submit_expenses=true, txn_perm=none`, no grants) passes `ExpenseSubmit` yet is FORBIDDEN on `TxnRead`/`TxnWrite`/`ReportGroup`, and a bookkeeper (`txn_perm=write`, no flag) is FORBIDDEN on `ExpenseSubmit`. The capability is a per-user boolean `users.can_submit_expenses` (INTEGER NOT NULL DEFAULT 0), VERSIONED like the other user perm columns (rule 5 — perms are audited): the SAME column with the SAME default is ALTER-added to `users_versions`, so the pre-existing system-user backfill version row (00006, change_id=2) stays byte-equal to its live row and Z3 needs NO new backfill; `InsertUserVersion` + `UserByID` gain the column; `SetUserCanSubmitExpenses` is the versioned setter (op='update' naming the actor, refuses the system user). Admin manages it (p13.2 UI later); here just the column + setter + perm plumbing. Coverage: `TestDecidePolicy` gains the `ExpenseSubmit x persona` matrix (submitter ALLOW, bookkeeper/noaccess FORBID, admin ALLOW) AND the submitter-forbidden-on-Txn*/ReportGroup cases — asserting `decide` directly (per the step, no p20.2 feature route invented); a real "Submitter" persona is added to `buildPersonas` (inserted BEFORE Admin so `TestRouteRegistryComplete`'s last-persona-is-Admin assertion holds), which the HTTP matrix drives like NoAccess across every mounted route — empirically proving a submitter has no ledger access.
  - **State machine (store-enforced; schema CHECK is only a backstop).** `status IN (draft, submitted, rejected, converted)` — FOUR values; "resubmitted" in the prose is NOT a status (resubmit is `rejected -> submitted`). Transitions: `CreateExpenseReport`->draft; `SubmitExpenseReport` draft|rejected->submitted (validate >= 1 line, `ErrExpenseReportEmpty`); `RejectExpenseReport(reason)` submitted->rejected storing `review_notes=reason` (required, `ErrExpenseReportReasonRequired`); `ResubmitExpenseReport` rejected->submitted; `ConvertExpenseReport(txnID)` submitted->converted. Illegal transitions raise `ErrExpenseReportState` (leaving no audit trace — validation inside the funnel's fn rolls the change back). Lines are editable (add/update/remove) ONLY while draft|rejected (`requireEditable`): a submitted report's lines are frozen (`ErrExpenseReportState`); a converted report is TERMINAL/immutable (`ErrExpenseReportImmutable`). `review_notes` is PRESERVED across a resubmit so the submitter still sees the reviewer's reason (p20.2).
  - **`posted_transaction_id` set ONLY on convert; convert validates the txn EXISTS only.** The column is NULL until convert; `ConvertExpenseReport` is its sole writer (`SetExpenseReportConverted` sets status='converted' + the link together). Convert validates the transaction exists (`GetTransaction`, else `ErrExpenseReportTxnMissing`) — NOT that it balances or maps the report's lines: the reviewer BUILDS the balanced ledger txn in p20.3 and this store method just LINKS an existing one. Re-convert / submit / reject / line-edit on a converted report all reject with a typed error.
  - **Two open ambiguities resolved (smallest reversible choice): line `fund_id`/`program_id` NULLABLE, `amount` SIGNED.** Unlike a budget line (00016, which forces `program_id NOT NULL` + `amount > 0` BECAUSE it enforces R/E projection), an expense-report line does NOT enforce R/E and need NOT balance — a submitter may not know the restriction/program, and the reviewer resolves accounts/fund/program/sign when building the balanced txn at convert. So `fund_id`/`program_id` are nullable (validated to EXIST only if set) and `amount` is a signed int64 minor magnitude (rule 3). `validateExpenseReportLine` checks the account exists + fund/program exist if set (`ErrExpenseReportRefMissing`); no R/E or amount-sign rule.
  - **Versioning mirrors budgets (00016) EXACTLY.** `expense_reports` — single-id twin, mutable header, NO delete op (a report terminates as rejected/converted, never hard-deleted). `expense_report_lines` — single-id twin; a line CAN be hard-deleted with an op='delete' version captured BEFORE the live delete (rule 14: soft-delete is transactions-only). Every mutation runs through the write funnel as ONE change, live-write-first then snapshot-from-live version append. `AssertVersioned` covers create->submit->reject->resubmit->convert (each op='update' on the report) + line create/update. Z3 gains `expense_reports`/`expense_report_lines` blocks (+ the `can_submit_expenses` column on the users block) and Z5 gains both `_versions` twins, keeping `cuento check` complete and clean on the new tables.

- **p20.2 (web: submitter workspace)** — the low-privilege SUBMITTER's UI over the p20.1 store: a "my reports" list + an expense-report editor, gated ENTIRELY by the standalone `ExpenseSubmit` perm. Reuses the p20.1 lifecycle store methods verbatim; NO reviewer queue / convert (p20.3). Recorded choices:
  - **URL scheme + routes (all `ExpenseSubmit`).** `GET /expenses` (my reports + a "new report" subsidiary picker), `POST /expenses` (create a draft, redirect to the editor), `GET /expenses/{id}` (the editor/detail), `GET /expenses/{id}/lines/new` + `.../lines/{lid}/edit` (the inline line-form partials), `POST /expenses/{id}/lines` + `.../lines/{lid}` + `.../lines/{lid}/delete` (line CRUD), `POST /expenses/{id}/submit` + `.../resubmit`. Registered in `routes.go` so the permission-matrix + registry-completeness tests auto-cover them; the matrix seeds one draft report (id 1) + line OWNED BY the Admin persona so the `{id}`->1 reachability check resolves (the ownership guard 404s a not-owned id, so the report must belong to the reachability persona).
  - **Editor: LINE-AT-A-TIME, NO balancing, NO new JS (honest reuse).** The report detail = header + a lines table + one inline add/edit-line form (swapped via htmx into `#expense-line-form`) + Submit — the SAME shape as the p19.3 budget-line editor, over the p20.1 per-line CRUD (`Add/Update/RemoveExpenseReportLine`, each its OWN change). This DELIBERATELY avoids a single-Save multi-row grid: that would re-implement p12's trap-1 reconcile-by-hidden-line-id across N changes + a bespoke add-row ES module. So NO `txneditor.js` is reused (its DR/CR twin columns, functional-class gating, imbalance/totals bar, apply-fund-all, and payee autocomplete are all machinery an unbalanced R/E report does not want). What IS reused: the sub-scoped account/fund/program selector ROW (accounts = R/E leaves in the report's sub via `AccountEditorOptions` filtered to revenue/expense; funds = `ActiveFunds(sub)`; programs = all active — exactly `buildLineForm`), the p10.3 form-error convention (422 + partial + autofocus), the `.txn-grid` CSS on the lines table, and the money formatters. **NO balance check anywhere** — an unbalanced report submits fine (`TestExpenseUnbalancedSubmitOK` asserts a single-line, net-nonzero report reaches `submitted`); the reviewer balances it at convert (p20.3).
  - **One subsidiary per report, picked at CREATE.** A report binds ONE subsidiary at creation (a picker on the "new report" form, defaulting to the user's `default_subsidiary_id` else the root). The line editor's account/fund options are scoped to THAT fixed sub — so, unlike the budget-line editor, there is NO per-line sub picker and NO sub-change hx-get re-filter (the report's sub cannot change).
  - **Amount = positive magnitude, stored sign DERIVED from account type; exponent from the sub base currency.** The submitter enters a POSITIVE magnitude; the handler derives the stored signed amount from the chosen account's type (expense positive, revenue negative). Since the reviewer re-resolves accounts/sign at convert (p20.1), this is a DISPLAY convention, not a correctness constraint — the store keeps `amount` signed (p20.1) and imposes no sign rule. An expense-report line stores NO currency (p20.1 model), so amount parse/format resolves the minor-unit exponent from the report's SUBSIDIARY base currency (`reportExponent` -> `GetSubsidiary(...).BaseCurrency` -> `currencyExponent`, best-effort 2 on a blank/unknown base) — NOT a hardcoded 2, so a non-2-exponent base scales correctly (rule 3/10). The reviewer re-resolves the currency authoritatively at convert.
  - **Out-of-sub / non-R/E account is gated at the WEB EDGE (the store does not).** `validateExpenseReportLine` (p20.1) checks only that the account EXISTS — no subsidiary-membership, no R/E-type rule. So the handler gates it: the line's account must be one of the offered R/E leaves in the report's sub (`reportAccountType`, reusing the SAME `AccountEditorOptions` set the picker showed). A non-existent account (0 / bad id) OR an out-of-sub / non-R/E account → a 422 field error (`error.expense.account_not_offered`); a zero/empty magnitude → `error.expense.amount`. `TestExpenseLineBadAccountFieldError` covers both bad-account cases.
  - **OWNERSHIP + editability enforced in EVERY id-taking handler (404, uniform).** `GetExpenseReport` returns ANY report by id (p20.1), so the perm gate alone is not enough — `loadOwnedReport` 404s unless the report exists AND `SubmitterID == currentUser.ID`. A missing id and a not-owned id are BOTH 404 (no enumeration; matches how the matrix treats other `{id}` routes). `loadEditableReport` adds the state gate (line mutations only while draft|rejected; a submitted/converted report's line routes 404). `loadReportLine` confirms a line belongs to the path's report. This holds for an admin too: an admin passes the `ExpenseSubmit` gate (is-admin implies all) but still sees only THEIR OWN reports here — the reviewer surface that sees others' reports is p20.3 (TxnWrite), a different route family. `TestExpenseOwnershipBoundary` proves submitter A gets 404 on B's report (open/line-editor/submit) and on a nonexistent id.
  - **Access boundary asserted explicitly.** A pure submitter (txn_perm=none, no grants, can_submit_expenses) is 403 on `/accounts`, `/funds`, `/programs`, `/budgets`, `/import`, `/admin*`, and a concrete report route `/reports/trial_balance`; the `/reports` INDEX is `AnyUser` by design (it filters its contents by grant) so it renders but leaks NO report link. `TestExpenseAccessBoundary` asserts all of this; `TestExpensePermGate` proves a bookkeeper (txn_perm=write, NO flag) is 403 on `/expenses` while the submitter is 200 — the ExpenseSubmit decoupling. The nav (shell.go) gains `{"nav.myexpenses", "/expenses", ExpenseSubmit}`, so a pure submitter sees ONLY that entry (+ home/settings).
  - **Resubmit shows the reviewer's reason.** After a reject (p20.1 preserves `review_notes` across the resubmit transition), the detail page renders the reviewer's reason (`#expense-review-notes`) + a resubmit affordance; the list shows it too. A zero-line submit → a clean 422 with the localized `error.expense.empty` (the detail page re-rendered in context), never a 500. `TestExpenseRejectShowsReasonAndResubmit` + `TestExpenseZeroLineSubmit422` cover these.
  - **p20.1-deferred admin toggle for `can_submit_expenses` LANDS HERE.** p20.1 said "Admin manages it (p13.2 UI later)"; that UI is now a checkbox on the admin user-detail page (`POST /admin/users/{id}/can-submit`, Admin), wired to the existing versioned `SetUserCanSubmitExpenses` setter (naming the acting admin). This completes the p20.1 deferral AND is how the e2e seeds a pure submitter (admin creates the user → toggles the flag). Required extending `GetUserRow` (the admin-detail read query) with the `can_submit_expenses` column (sqlc regenerated; `AdminUser.CanSubmitExpenses` added) — the ONLY query change. `TestAdminCanSubmitToggle` proves the grant flips a user from 403 to 200 on `/expenses`, is versioned, and that a non-admin cannot use the toggle.
  - **How the e2e seeds a submitter + simulates a rejection.** The fixture seeds ONLY an admin, and a pure submitter has NO ledger access to create the R/E account a line needs. So `e2e/tests/expense-submit.spec.js` is two-phase (one login each, well under the per-worker login limiter): PHASE 1 (admin) creates a revenue account (via `/accounts`) + the submitter user (via `/admin/users`) + toggles its `can_submit_expenses` (the new admin toggle); PHASE 2 (submitter, after `clearCookies`) creates a report, adds an unbalanced line, submits, sees "Submitted". The reviewer REJECTION is simulated via a NEW seed/maintenance CLI verb `cuento expense-report reject <id> --reason "<text>"` — the CLI FACE of the p20.1 `store.RejectExpenseReport` (NOT the p20.3 reviewer web queue; it wraps a p20.1 store method), exposed to the spec as `server.rejectReport(id, reason)` (bound to the worker's `-db`). The reject CLI writes the SAME db `serve` holds open; WAL + busy_timeout (the p08.2 concurrency finding) handle the second-process write, so the server is NOT stopped. Then the spec reloads, asserts the reason + resubmit control, resubmits, and asserts the status flips. Deterministic + worker-scoped (unique usernames/account name; rejects the exact id it created; RULE 11 synthetic data).
  - **i18n both catalogs.** New keys under `expense.*` / `error.expense.*` (+ `nav.myexpenses`, `admin.users.submit_*`/`admin.users.form.can_submit`/`admin.users.save_submit`) in en + es — NO bare `expense` leaf beside the `expense.*` table (the go-i18n dotted-key/leaf collision watch). `TestCatalogParity` green.

- **p20.3 (web: reviewer queue → convert / reject)** — COMPLETES Phase 20 (the last feature phase). The editing user's side of the p20.2 submission→review workflow: an editing (TxnWrite) user works a queue of SUBMITTED reports across ALL submitters, opens one in the phase-12 editor prefilled with the report's splits (subsidiary LOCKED), balances + POSTS it into a real versioned ledger transaction linked via `posted_transaction_id`, OR rejects it with a reason routing it back to the submitter. This is the deliberate MIRROR of the p17.3 bank-import review→post (`imports_review.go`). Handlers on `internal/web/expenses_review.go`; the review queue template `expense_review.tmpl`; the p12 editor gains an `ExpenseReportID` mode on `txnEditorModel` + `transaction_form.tmpl`. Recorded choices:
  - **URL + perm: `/expenses/review**`, TxnWrite.** The reviewer queue (`GET /expenses/review`) + the review form (`GET /expenses/review/{id}`) + post/reject are ALL TxnWrite (reviewing = editing the books). This is a DISTINCT surface from the p20.2 submitter workspace (`/expenses**`, ExpenseSubmit): the 2-segment `/expenses/review` beats `/expenses/{id}` (a literal is more specific, Go 1.22+ mux), so a PURE submitter (ExpenseSubmit, `txn_perm=none`) hitting the review routes is gated by TxnWrite → 403 — the two roles are distinct (asserted by `TestReviewPermSubmitterForbidden` AND the auto permission matrix). The reviewer reads EVERY submitter's reports (`ExpenseReportsByStatus`), so the review handlers do NOT use the p20.2 `loadOwnedReport` (which enforces submitter==self); a missing id 404s (mirrors imports_review). `nav.expensereview` (TxnWrite) lights up now that `GET /expenses/review` is registered.
  - **ROUTING: the ACTION verbs live in path SEGMENT 3 as LITERALS** — `POST /expenses/review/post/{id}` and `.../reject/{id}`, NOT `.../review/{id}/post`. The `{id}`-in-middle shape collides with the p20.2 `POST /expenses/{id}/lines/{lid}` (both match `/expenses/review/lines/post` with neither dominating → a `ServeMux.register` PANIC at Mount). With the verb literal in seg 3 (`post`/`reject` can never equal `lines`), no path matches both patterns. (Only the 2-segment queue route relies on literal-beats-wildcard precedence; the action routes rely on the disambiguating literal, not on precedence.)
  - **Atomic post+convert in ONE change (`store.PostAndConvertExpenseReport`).** A NEW store method — the analogue of `PostImportRow` — runs `postTransactionTx` (creating the real balanced versioned txn) + `SetExpenseReportConverted(txnID)` + the version append inside ONE `write()`. Doing `PostTransaction` then `ConvertExpenseReport` as two calls would be two `changes` rows = a window where a converted report points at a not-yet/never-linked txn; this closes it. The report is RE-READ on the tx-bound `q` and must still be `submitted` (else `ErrExpenseReportState`/`ErrExpenseReportImmutable`) — this re-read, not atomicity alone, is the no-double-post + converted-immutability gate (mirrors `ErrImportRowNotPending`). An UNBALANCED/invalid post: `postTransactionTx` errors → the whole `write` rolls back → the report stays `submitted`, nothing linked → the web edge re-renders the editor at 422 (reusing `routeTxnError`/`renderFormError`). The p20.1 standalone `ConvertExpenseReport` (links an ALREADY-existing txn) is KEPT — p20.1 tests use it. `TestPostAndConvertExpenseReport` (store) + `TestReviewPostCreatesBalancedTxnAndConverts` (web) assert the balanced path converts + links a register-visible versioned txn AND the unbalanced attempt → 422 stays submitted; on success the reviewer is redirected to the created txn's history (p12.4).
  - **Review & post prefill = the p12 editor, subsidiary LOCKED.** `GET /expenses/review/{id}` opens `transaction_form.tmpl` (`ExpenseReportID` mode) prefilled one editor row per report line (account/signed-amount/fund/memo). The subsidiary reuses the SAME locked-select-+-hidden-carrier the import mode uses (`{{if or .ImportRowID .ExpenseReportID}}`). Because a report line carries NO functional class and its program is optional, the prefill DEFAULTS program (line's → account default → root, Z15) and functional class (account default on expense rows, Z16) so an untouched prefill is not spuriously rejected as an "imbalance"; a trailing EMPTY row is appended for the reviewer's cash/bank counter-side (mirrors `prefillImportRows`). The store re-validates authoritatively on POST. A non-submitted report's review-form GET redirects to the queue (nothing to post). RESTRICTED-FUND lines: the prefill copies a line's fund onto its R/E row but leaves the appended cash/bank counter row UNRESTRICTED, so if a line carries a restricted fund the reviewer must set the counter-side's fund by hand — the store's per-fund zero-sum gate (`ErrFundUnbalanced` → 422) enforces it (by design: "the reviewer adjusts splits to balance; the store's validation is the gate"). Not a defect; a future restricted-fund report's 422 is the intended flow, not a bug.
  - **Reject-with-reason: TRIM at the web edge.** `RejectExpenseReport` checks `reason == ""` WITHOUT trimming (unlike `DiscardImportRow`), so a whitespace-only reason would slip through; the handler `TrimSpace`es and short-circuits to a 422 (the queue re-rendered with `expreview.reject_reason_required`, a page-level notice since the reason input is per-row) before calling the store. A real reason → `submitted`→`rejected` with `review_notes=reason`, routed back (p20.2 shows it, the submitter resubmits). `TestReviewRejectRoutesBack` asserts both the missing-reason 422 (stays submitted) and the reason-stored reject.
  - **Converted immutability + txn link.** A converted report is terminal: its review-form GET redirects to the queue, and a re-post is rejected by the store re-read (`ErrExpenseReportImmutable`) → redirect to the queue, same txn linked (`TestReviewPostImmutableConverted`). The queue's HISTORY section (converted + rejected reports, kept minimal / "if clean") links a converted report to its posted txn (`/transactions/{txnID}/history`) — "the page shows the txn link".
  - **i18n both catalogs.** New keys under `expreview.*` (+ `nav.expensereview`) in en + es — NO bare `expreview` leaf (the dotted-key/leaf collision watch). Reused `import.posthdr_*` were NOT co-opted; the editor's locked-sub hint + title/intro/submit-label branch to `expreview.*` in expense mode. `TestCatalogParity` green.
  - **e2e (`e2e/tests/expense-review.spec.js`, new).** Phased (one login each): admin seeds an expense + cash account + a `can_submit_expenses` submitter; the submitter files TWO submitted reports; the admin (is_admin ⇒ TxnWrite ⇒ the reviewer) opens the queue, reviews & posts the first (the p12 editor prefilled + subsidiary LOCKED; adds the cash counter-side; posts → converts + links the txn, redirected to its history), then rejects the second with a reason; the submitter then sees the rejection reason. Reuses `page` (`e2e-settled`), `helpers.saveAndReload`, strict CSP (no `waitForFunction`), worker-scoped uniquely-named data (RULE 11). Stable across the full parallel suite ×15.
- **p22.4 (docs: deferred/pending/incomplete register)** — `docs/deferred.md` compiled: the Phase 21 backlog, the documented limitations/edges, open code markers, the pre-cutover human gates, and a ranked low-hanging-fruit list for p22.5. Verified each seeded follow-up against the code. **Two integrity-relevant OPEN findings:** (1) `reconciliations_versions` is written by the store but was NEVER added to the Z3/Z5 integrity checks in `internal/ledger/checks.go` (budgets p19.1 and expense_reports p20.1 twins WERE) — an integrity-coverage gap, low-hanging to close. (2) the p08.5 `// TODO(p16.1): repoint reconciliations` in `internal/store/merge.go` is a STALE-open deferral: the reconciliations table landed in p16.1 but merge still never repoints a split's `reconciliation_id` — merging an account with OPEN-recon'd splits leaves a cross-account clearing that trips Z8 (finalized-recon splits instead hit the 00014 trigger ABORT). Full repoint is backlog; a clean block-guard is the low-hanging slice. Docs-only change; `make lint test check` clean. Not a design decision, a register — recorded here as a pointer to `docs/deferred.md`.

- **p22.5 (release wrap-up: low-hanging-fruit sweep)** — four items from the p22.4 register (`docs/deferred.md`), each small/TDD'd; one commit. Recorded choices:
  - **(1) `reconciliations`/`reconciliations_versions` wired into Z3+Z5.** The p16.1 recon twin was written by the store (`InsertReconciliationVersion`, migration 00014) but MISSED from both integrity checks (budgets p19.1 and expense_reports p20.1 twins WERE wired). Added one Z3 single-id block (compares account_id/statement_date/statement_balance/currency/status/notes; op='update' on finalize/reopen, never hard-deleted so a missing/'delete' latest version is the violation — mirrors the expense_reports block) and one `reconciliations_versions` entry to the Z5 UNION. Pure integrity-coverage; no behavior change. Bites: `TestReconciliationZ3Bites` (raw balance tamper undetected pre-fix), `TestReconciliationZ5Bites`.
  - **(2) `Reopen` refuses a later-OPEN recon on the same (account, currency).** `Reopen` guarded only a later FINALIZED recon (`ErrReconciliationNotLatest`), not a later OPEN one — so reopening an earlier finalized recon while a later OPEN recon stood yielded TWO open recons (a state `StartReconciliation`'s one-open guard would refuse), with NO `cuento check` backstop (the D13 single-open invariant is store-guard-only). Added a `CountOpenReconciliations` check in `Reopen` reusing the EXISTING `ErrOpenReconciliationExists` sentinel (identical semantics + existing i18n key `error.recon.open_exists`); the recon being reopened is still 'finalized' at the check so it is not counted. Web `reconReopen` maps it to a 409 (alongside the existing not-finalized/not-latest conflicts — never a 500). This SUPERSEDES the p16.5 assertion in `TestReopenBlockedWhenLaterFinalizedExists` that reopening the earlier recon succeeds once the later is reopened — that old outcome was exactly the two-opens bug; the test now asserts `ErrOpenReconciliationExists` there and a new `TestReopenBlockedWhenOtherOpenExists` proves the guard in isolation. The no-other-open success branch stays covered by `TestReopenSingleFinalized`.
  - **(3) Account-merge block-guard for reconciled source splits.** `merge.go`'s `// TODO(p16.1): repoint reconciliations` was a STALE-open latent hole (p22.4): merging an account whose splits carry a `reconciliation_id` moved the split to dst but left it linked to a src-account recon → Z8 fires (open recon) or the 00014 split-lock trigger ABORTs (finalized recon). FULL repoint stays backlog (per-(account,currency) recon semantics, dst overlap, opening chain — a real design problem). Instead `MergeAccount` REFUSES the merge (new sentinel `ErrMergeSourceReconciled`, via a new `CountReconciledSplitsForAccount` query) when src has ANY reconciled split — checked inside `fn` on the tx-bound q (TOCTOU), before any write, so a rejected merge writes nothing and the ledger stays clean. Web `mergeErrorField` maps it to a 422 field error (`error.merge.source_reconciled`, both catalogs); the merge preview drops the misleading "0 reconciliations move" line and instead shows a BLOCKING note (`merge.consequence.reconciled_blocked`) with the reconciled-split count when > 0 (the old `merge.consequence.recons` key removed from both catalogs + template). Bites: `TestMergeBlockedSourceReconciled` (store, no partial mutation + ledger clean), `TestMergeReconciledSourceSurfaced` (web 422, not 500).
  - **(4) Account-ledger currency-in-range — INVESTIGATED, RECLASSIFIED, NO CODE.** deferred.md §2.4 feared a currency netting to zero at BOTH the opening (day before From) and the closing (To) but with mid-range activity would drop its section. This CANNOT happen: `SubtreeBalancesAsOf` has no `HAVING SUM<>0`, so it emits a zero-balance row for every (account, currency) with ANY split on-or-before the as-of date; a currency with in-range activity therefore ALWAYS appears at the closing endpoint (as-of To) with balance 0, so `unionCurrencies(opening, closing)` already includes it. The in-range currency set is provably a SUBSET of the closing set, so any "union in the range currencies" change is a no-op that cannot bite on revert (violating the TDD hard rule). Per AGENTS "a listed test that seems wrong: record the deviation" — item 4 ships as a documented non-issue with a labeled REGRESSION GUARD (`TestAccountLedgerMidRangeOnlyCurrency`, bespoke inline store: an account that receives+fully-spends EUR mid-range renders its EUR section on UNMODIFIED code) that would catch a future `SubtreeBalancesAsOf` change dropping zero rows. `make golden` unchanged.

- **go-live import: two `cmd/ledgerimport` capabilities added while finalizing the reviewed mapping (D26; real values live only in the gitignored source dir, rule 11).** (1) **Historical FX seeding** — a new optional `build -rates <csv>` flag (`rate_date,base,quote,rate,source`) loads reference rates via `store.PutRates` before the entity phases (the currencies it references are all migration-seeded). Without it the produced db has an EMPTY `exchange_rates` and can render NO converted (consolidated-currency) report, so seeding the historical rate series is a go-live prerequisite, not an afterthought. `make fixture` passes the file when present. (2) **Child-program tree from the raw class column** — the config gained `program_classes` (raw-class → program) and `program_parents` (program → parent program); a split's program resolves finest-first (raw class → the coarser category code → account default), and the class value takes precedence because it is BOTH finer AND more correct (a split whose category code says one subsidiary's bucket but whose class names a specific program of another is attributed to the program). `builder.programs` now creates a tree (parent-before-child, cycle-checked) instead of a flat list under root "General". Extends D24 (programs are a dimension) — the importer can now populate the tree's depth, not just the root's children. Tests: `TestReadRatesParses`, `TestBuildLoadsRates`, `TestProgramTreeFromKlass`.

- **Intercompany REVENUE/EXPENSE elimination on consolidation (D19 extension).** D19's intercompany collapse was BALANCE-SHEET only: due-to/due-from asset/liability accounts that net to zero per currency, collapsed by the balance sheet and checked by Z17. But a nonprofit that funds an operating subsidiary books an intra-group TRANSFER as revenue in one entity and expense in another — income-statement accounts, and typically in DIFFERENT currencies (the funder's USD expense vs the recipient's local-currency revenue). Those never net per currency, so the netting model does not fit. Resolution: (1) the consolidated income statement / functional matrix / program activity now EXCLUDE intercompany-flagged R/E accounts (each leg dropped independently — no cross-currency netting needed) at a consolidated (multi-sub) scope, and KEEP them at a leaf/single-sub scope where they are that entity's real external line (`Toolkit.consolidatedICExclusions`, applied in `Activity`/`FunctionalMatrix`/`ProgramActivity`); (2) **Z17 is restricted to asset/liability intercompany accounts** — R/E intercompany accounts are eliminated by exclusion, not netting, so requiring them to net per currency would be a false positive. The importer's account mapping gained an `intercompany` column so the historical build can flag the transfer accounts. Net income carries a small residual = the genuine cross-currency FX difference between the two legs (the transfer's converted value differs by the rate spread) — a real translation effect, not an error. Tests: `TestActivityExcludesIntercompanyConsolidated` (reports), `TestZ17IgnoresIncomeStatementIntercompany` (ledger), `TestAccountMapIntercompanyColumn` (import).

- **p23.3 (ux: flexible server-side date parsing)** — `money.ParseDate` gains a reference `now time.Time` and a forgiving short/partial fallback, applied to EVERY date input via the existing funnel (rule 10). Recorded choices:
  - **Signature change: `ParseDate(s, df, now)`.** The implied-year short form needs a reference year, and rule 10 keeps date logic server-side + deterministic, so the reference is PASSED IN (never a wall-clock read inside the funnel). All ~7 callers thread their clock: web handlers pass `s.now()`; `reports.resolveDate` reuses its existing `fallback time.Time`; free helpers (`parseEditorDate`/`parseUserDate`) gained a `now` param threaded from their `s`-method callers; `bankimport` (a PURE package, full-date bank cells that only ever match the strict layouts) passes the zero time so it reads no clock.
  - **Order: strict full layouts first, flexible fallback second.** The active-format layout then always-ISO (unchanged D16 behavior) own the unambiguous FULL renderings — so US/EU full dates are NOT reinterpreted. Only when both strict attempts fail does the flexible path run.
  - **Short forms parse BIG-ENDIAN regardless of `DateFormat`.** Dash/slash/dot-separated integers, most-significant first: 3 parts = Y-M-D, 2 parts = M-D (year = `now`'s). The user's examples (`26-6-1`→2026-06-01, `6-1`→2026-06-01) are big-endian, so short entry is big-endian for everyone — an EU user's `6-1` is June 1, not 6 Jan. Documented tradeoff: full EU/US dates still parse per the setting; only the terse shortcut is fixed-order.
  - **2-digit year pivot = strptime `%y`: 00–68 → 2000–2068, 69–99 → 1900–1999.** Fixed (not sliding off `now`) so it is deterministic; a 3-/4-digit written year is taken as-is.
  - **Forgiving separators supersede one old rejection test.** `2025/03/04` under df=ISO was previously REJECTED ("ISO wants dashes"); the flexible path now ACCEPTS it as big-endian Y/M/D. Per AGENTS ("a listed test that seems wrong: record the deviation"), `TestParseDateRejects`'s `wrongSeparators` case was removed and re-added as a positive case in `TestParseDateFlexible`. Impossible dates (Feb 30, month 13) still reject via a `time.Date` round-trip check.
  - The client-side date field (picker + GnuCash shortcuts, forgiving DISPLAY parse) is p23.4; this step is the server funnel only.

- **p23.4 (ux: reusable client date field)** — one shell-wide ES module (`datefield.js`) enhances EVERY `input.js-datefield` with a forgiving display parse/format (mirroring the p23.3 server funnel), GnuCash keyboard shortcuts, and a hand-written calendar popover (rule 10: never `input[type=date]`; rule 12: external module, no inline script/style; node-tested pure core + e2e-covered DOM glue, trap 2). Recorded choices:
  - **Global auto-enhancer + a marker class, not a per-field partial.** Loaded once in `shell-open` (like formfocus.js), it scans for `input.js-datefield` on load and after every `htmx:afterSwap`, and BUILDS the pick button + popover in JS — so retrofitting a date input anywhere is just adding the class (10 inputs across txn editor / reports / register / reconcile / budgets / schedules), no markup churn. Progressive enhancement: no-JS users keep a plain text input the flexible server parser still accepts.
  - **Per-user format + localized labels flow via `<body>` data-*.** `baseData.DateFormat` (from `dateFormatCode`) and the calendar month/weekday/pick labels (from the i18n catalog — new `cal.*` keys, both catalogs) are stamped on `<body>` once; `resolveFmt` reads the input's own `data-date-format`, else the nearest ancestor's (the txn form has one), else the body's. Keeps rule 9 (strings originate in the catalog) without each page re-emitting them or the JS calling `Intl` (which would pull non-catalog locale names).
  - **`-`/`+` stay LITERAL while a partial date is being typed.** The day-shift shortcuts collide with the `-` separator in `26-6-1` / ISO entry, so `applyShortcut` shifts a day ONLY when the field is empty or already holds a COMPLETE parseable date; mid-entry (non-empty + unparsed) it returns null so the key inserts literally. `[`/`]`/`h`/`t` never appear mid-number so they always act. This is what lets typing and shortcuts coexist on one field.
  - **Owns the txn editor's date input.** The old glue-local `t/+/-` handler + `shiftDate`/`today`/`parseDisplayDate` helpers were removed from `txneditor.js`; `#txn-date` just carries `js-datefield` now (single source of date behavior).

- **p23.5 (ux: two-level top nav)** — the header becomes two rows: the existing global nav on top, and a second SECTION bar under it carrying the current section's sub-pages (and the room where per-page filters/search land in later work). Recorded choices:
  - **Data-driven `SubNav`, mirroring `navSections`/`visibleNav`.** A `baseData.SubNav []navItem` is filled by `subNav(ctx,u,path)` from `subNavGroups()` — a list of `{Prefixes, Entries}` where a request under any prefix selects the group. Entries are filtered to registered+permitted (reusing `navPermits`, so the bar and route enforcement share one truth; no dead links), with the matching entry marked current. The template renders the second `<nav class="app-subnav">` ONLY when SubNav is non-empty, so sections without sub-nav stay single-row. A section lights up by appending a group here — the same incremental pattern as the top nav.
  - **Sections lit now: Admin and Budgets.** Admin's bar = Users/Subsidiaries/Currencies/Rates/Org/Ops (reusing the existing section-title catalog keys the admin index already renders, so ZERO new label strings there); Budgets' bar = Budgets/Schedules. Schedules is a distinct TOP-LEVEL path but belongs to the Budgets section, so the group carries both `/budgets` and `/schedules` prefixes — on `/schedules` the Budgets top entry isn't "current" (no top-level match) yet the section bar still shows and marks Schedules current. Only one genuinely new key: `nav.section_label` (the bar's aria-label), both catalogs.
  - **Frame first, filters later.** Wiring each page's existing filters/search (accounts, register, reports) INTO the section bar is deferred incremental work; p23.5 lands the frame + the two clearest submenus. `TestSubNavRendersPerSection` asserts the bar on /admin (+ current marking), its absence on /accounts, and the /schedules→Budgets-section behavior.

- **Go-live account chart from the export's `:` hierarchy + inactivation (import; D26).** The reviewed account mapping is regenerated from the source's `:`-delimited account paths, not a flat 2-level grouping. (1) **Posting accounts are always LEAVES** — a split on a non-leaf account is rejected by the leaf-active trigger AND `postBucket` swallows that rejection into a warning while still exiting 0 (silent-drop hazard), so a posting account's parent is its NEAREST PURE-GROUPING ancestor (a `:`-prefix that is not itself a posting account); contra/sub-accounts that post (accumulated depreciation) become SIBLINGS under the grouping node. Pure-grouping prefixes become placeholders; a depth-1 posting account is a top-level leaf (no redundant single-child placeholder). (2) **Number-free names** — the 4-digit account-number prefix is dropped (the org does not use it); a name that would COLLIDE with a sibling keeps its number as the minimal disambiguator. (3) **`(deleted)`/`(eliminado)`** accounts (inactivated in QuickBooks) are marked inactive via a new `active` account-mapping column; since an inactive account may still hold historical splits, the importer creates it ACTIVE, posts its splits, then DEACTIVATES it in a final phase (op='update', never delete — rule 14). Verified: asset/liability/revenue/expense grand totals match the source exactly after the restructure (the dropped-split detector — equity differs only by cuento's synthetic FX/opening counter-legs), and position balances still reconcile to the books. `source_acct` is never changed (the split-matching key). Test: `TestBuildDeactivatesInactiveAccounts`.

- **p23.10 (ux: page controls in the section bar + auto-apply)** — a page can move its filters/action buttons out of its body into the second-level menu (p23.5 section bar). Recorded choices:
  - **`baseData.SubNavControls` string + constant-name dispatch.** The handler sets `sp.Shell.SubNavControls = "accounts"`; the shell renders it with `{{if eq .Shell.SubNavControls "accounts"}}{{template "accounts-controls" .Page}}{{end}}` — CONSTANT template names guarded on the string, never a dynamic-name/partial helper (avoids html/template re-entrancy). The section bar now shows when `{{if or .Shell.SubNav .Shell.SubNavControls}}`. Each page contributing controls adds one guarded line + its own `*-controls` partial.
  - **Auto-apply via htmx, no Apply button, no-JS safe.** The accounts filter is one `<form class="subnav-filters" method="get" action="/accounts" hx-get="/accounts" hx-trigger="change" hx-target="#accounts-results" hx-swap="outerHTML">`: any child change fires the GET and swaps only the results. The real `method=get` form is kept (Enter submits, full reload) with a `<noscript>` Apply button, so it degrades without JS.
  - **Partial swap keyed on `HX-Target`, not `HX-Request`.** `HX-Request` alone can't distinguish a filter change from an hx-boosted nav click (both set it); the handler renders the `accounts-results` fragment only when `HX-Target == "accounts-results"`, else the full page. `#accounts-results` wraps ONLY the as-of + table, so a filter swap never wipes an open create/edit form in `#account-form` (which the New/Merge triggers — now in the bar — target).
  - Tests: `TestSubNavRendersPerSection` updated (accounts now has a controls bar; `/reports` is the no-bar case); `merge.spec.js` retargeted to the auto-apply filter.

- **p23.9 (ux: nav hub restructure)** — the top nav is made lean and the sections the user named are nested under a card hub. Recorded choices:
  - **One AnyUser "More" hub, per-card perm gating (the literal grouping).** The user asked for funds/programs/reconciliations/settings/admin under one parent whose page is cards. Rather than route around "Settings under Admin hides it from non-admins" by keeping them top-level, the More hub is `AnyUser` and each CARD is perm-gated (`visibleHubCards` reuses `navPermits`): the Settings card always shows, Admin only to admins, the ledger cards to ledger-readers. So the literal five (plus Budgets/Import as conscious adds — they cluttered the top nav and aren't primary workflows) live under `/more`. Top nav is now Accounts · Reports · My expenses · Expense review · More.
  - **The hub is a reusable card grid.** `hubCard`/`hubPageModel` + the `hub-cards` partial render a responsive tile grid (whole card is the link); other hub landings can reuse it. Card labels reuse the existing `nav.*` keys; only `nav.more`, `more.title/intro/empty`, and `more.desc.*` are new (both catalogs).
  - **Section bar mirrors the hub.** A single `subNavGroup` (prefixes `/more`,`/funds`,`/programs`,`/reconciliations`,`/budgets`,`/schedules`,`/import`,`/settings`) shows the same links as lateral sub-nav on every More-area page (perm-filtered). `/admin` keeps its OWN group (a sub-hub: Users/Subsidiaries/…); the More bar links out to it. Reports stays a top-level workflow (not in the user's list).
  - Tests retargeted: perm-gating (`TestNavPermGated`) now asserts the Admin card on `/more` (admin only) + Settings card (everyone); the top-nav localization tests use `nav.more`; the e2e shell/settings specs navigate via the More hub. Home's Accounts-current-on-`/` special case (p23.8) unchanged.

- **p26.3 (ux: combobox on txn fund/program + one fuzzy payee control)** — the txn fund and program selects gain the p26.2 combobox (`combo-input`); the payee dual control (native `<select>` + a separate `.txn-payee-autocomplete` search block) collapses to a SINGLE combobox over `#txn-payee`. Recorded choices:
  - **Payee stays TRANSACTION-LEVEL (header), not per-split.** Per-split payee would need a `splits.payee_id` migration + `splits_versions` churn; the user said "either way", so the smallest reversible choice holds — one payee per transaction, tagged in the header, unchanged from p12.3.
  - **`/payees/suggest` REMOVED (deviation from PLAN p26.3 "reuse the matcher for /payees/suggest ranking").** The editor already renders the FULL payee option list (`ListPayees`, no pagination — a small nonprofit) into `#txn-payee`, so the client combobox filters it in-browser with the shared `combofilter` matcher; the server suggest fragment had no other caller and became dead code. Retired: the `/payees/suggest` route, the `payeeSuggest` handler + `payeeSuggestModel`, the `payee-suggest` template define, and `TestPayeeSuggestHandler`. The store `SuggestPayees` (+ its sqlc query + `TestPayeeSuggestRanking`) is RETAINED unused — a reusable prefix-ranked reader with no generated-SQL churn to justify retiring it (note in `store/payees.go`). Making a dead endpoint fuzzy would have been new code for no caller, so client-side filtering was chosen.
  - **Combobox generalized with an opts hook (so p26.4 expense grid reuses it).** `enhance(select, opts)` gains `{ allowFreeText, initialText, onInput(text), onPick({value,label}) }`; account/fund/program pass NO opts (identical to p26.2). Payee passes `allowFreeText` (the overlay becomes the tab stop, the select drops out of tab order, and a typed brand-new name survives blur — it isn't reset to the empty selection), `onInput` (mirror the typed text into the hidden `#txn-payee-name`/`payee_name` and reset the id sink to 0 → find-or-create on save, unchanged), `onPick` (set `#txn-payee-name` to the picked name + run the existing `fetchAndApplyTemplate` grid autofill, gated by `allRowsEmpty`), and `initialText` (seed the box from `#txn-payee-name` on a 422 re-render of a typed-new payee). New `resyncCombos(root)` refreshes overlay text after any direct `select.value =` set (apply-fund-to-all, `gateRow`'s program prefill, `swapRowValues`); the payee combo carries `data-combo-manual` so `initCombos` skips it (txneditor enhances it once with its opts). The matcher (`combofilter.js`) is UNCHANGED.

- **p26.4 (ux: expense-report line grid overhaul)** — the editable expense grid gains the same combobox/spreadsheet UX as the txn grid, plus a per-row delete and amount reformat. Recorded choices:
  - **Delete-row RE-INDEXES the survivors (chosen over gap-tolerance).** The × button (`type="button"`, delegated on `#expense-rows`) removes the row, then rewrites every surviving row's `_i`/`-i` id/name suffixes + `data-row` to a contiguous `0..n-1` and updates `#expense-rows-count` — so the server handler (`expenseLinesSave`, which parses `account_i`/`amount_i`/… up to `rows`) is UNCHANGED. Re-index PRESERVES values (only suffixes change), unlike `addRow`'s clone-and-clear — clearing a surviving row's `line_id_i` would turn an existing line into a duplicate insert. Combos need no re-enhancement on re-index (their overlay listeners are closure-bound, not id-bound). **Deleting the only/last data row RESETS it in place** (clear inputs, `selectedIndex=0`, clear the hidden `line_id`, then `resyncCombos` that row) rather than removing it: `addRow` clones the last row and can't run at zero rows, and the grid invariant is one trailing empty row. An emptied sole row saves as "no line" → the store's replace-set deletes the underlying line, which is the delete's intent.
  - **Amount reformat-on-blur is US-format only (new pure `formatAmountGrouped` in `txnamount.js`).** On blur the `el-amount` input reformats `1000` → `1,000.00` by PARSING via the existing `parseAmountMinor` (US `.` decimal / `,` grouping) then re-emitting with thousands grouping + the currency's fraction width; a blank/mid-type/unparseable value is left untouched (display convenience, not a validator — the Go store parses per the user's number-format setting and stays authoritative). Client formatting being US-only means a non-US user's typed amount is reformatted US-style in the box; this matches the already-US-only `parseAmountMinor`/txn-grid amount inputs, and is beyond current client scope — a fuller locale-aware client formatter is deferred. `formatAmountGrouped` is node-tested (pure, no `document`).
  - **combobox `collectOptions` now INCLUDES the `value="0"` option (fixes the inherited p26.3 value-0 bug).** It previously skipped `value==='0'`, so after a real pick the overlay never re-offered the reset entry ("Unrestricted" / "None" / account-none); now only the empty-value (`''`) placeholder is excluded, so 0 is a normal selectable list entry and a user can re-pick it to clear back to none. Picking 0 fires `change` → `syncInputToSelection` → `currentLabel()` returns `''` for value 0, so the box blanks (empty == cleared, correct). This also surfaces the 0 entry in the txn grid's account/fund/program lists (intended); the payee freeText combo is unaffected (it owns its input). Covered by e2e (a value-0 re-pick in `expense-submit`), not a node test — `collectOptions` is DOM-glue in `combobox.js`, not pure `combofilter.js`.
  - **Subsidiary picker auto-submits on change (htmx, no inline script).** The `<select name="subsidiary_id">` gains `hx-post="/expenses/{id}/subsidiary" hx-trigger="change"`; `expenseSetSubsidiary` still PRG-redirects, and `redirectAfterForm` sets `HX-Redirect` on an HX-Request so htmx does a full navigation that re-scopes the sub-scoped account/fund/program option lists (target/swap are irrelevant under HX-Redirect). The "Set subsidiary" button and its `expense.detail.set_subsidiary` key are REMOVED (dropped from BOTH catalogs); a `<noscript>` submit keeps the no-JS fallback (mirrors the register/accounts filter pattern). The overlap bleed is fixed CSS-only by adding the `txn-cell` class to each grid `<td>` (the containment rules key on `.txn-grid td.txn-cell …`), plus `el-*-cell` width rules.
