New i18n key `common.delete_row` (both locales) is the delete button's accessible label. `expensegrid.js` now owns the combo wiring (`initCombos` on init + htmx swap; `stripCombo(clone)`+`initCombos(clone)` across `addRow`; `resyncCombos` after the sole-row reset) — combobox.js has no self-init.

- **p26.6 (ux: parent-account register rollup)** — a PLACEHOLDER (parent) account's register now lists the splits of ALL its descendant leaf accounts with one combined date-ordered running balance per currency. Recorded choices:
  - **ONE query, recursive descendant closure (no leaf/placeholder branch).** `RegisterPage`'s `WHERE sp.account_id = ?` becomes `WHERE sp.account_id IN (SELECT id FROM des)` where `des` is a recursive descendant CTE seeded at the requested account (mirroring `AccountDescendants`, which includes self). A LEAF's closure is just `{itself}`, so its register is byte-for-byte unchanged (same split set, order, window running balance → leaf reconciliation preserved, the existing `TestRegister*` tests pass unmodified); a PLACEHOLDER closes over all descendants and the existing `SUM(...) OVER (PARTITION BY currency ORDER BY date, split_id)` window accumulates the merged running balance in SQL — no Go-side merge. The account id stays the first positional `?` (now the CTE seed), so the store param binding and the hand-edited `balances.sql.go` params are unchanged apart from the SQL string + the new `account_id` projection column. sqlc v1.31.1 accepts the recursive-CTE-in-`IN` pattern (same as `DrillSplits`).
  - **Rows carry their OWN account id; counter-account is resolved per (txn, row-account).** `RegisterRow`/`RegisterPageRow` gain `AccountID` (the split's own leaf). `registerRows` passes `r.AccountID` (not the parent) to `resolveCounterAccount`, so the counter column names the actual OTHER leaf. The counter cache is keyed by `(txnID, r.AccountID)` because an intra-parent transfer surfaces one txn as two rows whose counters differ; for a leaf register the row account is constant, so this degrades to the previous per-txn behavior (no regression). Parents cannot hold their own splits (`ErrPlaceholderAccount` + ledger Z2), so no parent-level split double-counts.
  - **No new visible per-row account column (minimal, per PLAN latitude).** The rows are attributed via the existing subsidiary badge + the leaf-named counter-account column; `AccountID` is used internally only for counter resolution. Adding a visible own-account column was out of scope and would churn the register layout, so it was deferred.

- **p26.13 (store: an UNCHANGED now-inactive split account is savable on update)** — resolves the p26.10 OPEN QUESTION. A pre-existing split whose account is UNCHANGED from the persisted split may keep a now-inactive account on `UpdateTransaction`; a NEW split or a split whose account CHANGED still requires an ACTIVE account, and every split on create is still active-required. Rationale: lets users maintain historical transactions on deactivated accounts (edit date/memo/amount of the OTHER legs) without reactivating the account, while a fresh use of a dead account is still blocked. Recorded choices:
  - **Only the inactive rejection is relaxed, only for the exact-same account.** `resolveSplit` gains `allowInactiveAccount bool` that guards ONLY the `if acct.Active == 0` branch (`&& !allowInactiveAccount`); the missing (`ErrAccountMissing`), placeholder/leaf (`ErrPlaceholderAccount`), subsidiary-map, fund, program, and functional-class checks are untouched — an inactive account that is ALSO a placeholder still trips `ErrPlaceholderAccount` (that check precedes the active check).
  - **The "unchanged" predicate is computed by the caller from persisted state.** `validateAndResolve` takes a `map[int64]int64` of existing `split_id → persisted account_id`; `UpdateTransaction` builds it from `SplitsByTransaction` (loaded BEFORE validation, reusing the load it already needs for the diff + recon lock), `PostTransaction`/`postTransactionTx` pass `nil`. Per split: `allow := in.ID != nil && liveAccountByID[*in.ID] == in.AccountID`. A map-miss (bogus or absent id) yields `false` — the active check applies, and the bad id is caught later as `ErrSplitNotFound` — so the loosening can never be triggered by a fabricated id.
  - **Consistent with `cuento check` (no invariant loosened at rest).** There is NO at-rest active-account ledger check: Z2 is leaf-only, and the other `active` references are Z3 version-snapshot parity and the Z19 warning (active R/E leaves lacking 990 codes) — neither rejects a split on an inactive account. The synthetic fixture already carries txn 7 on inactive account 5 with `make check` clean, so the store guard was the only thing rejecting these edits; loosening it for unchanged accounts stays fully consistent with the ledger checks. Versioning/audit are unchanged (the diff/version-append path is identical). No e2e added — a store-level guard with table + negative store tests; noted.

- **p26.16 (import: per-split `description` from `desc`; stop minting payees)** — step 2 of the payee→per-split-`description` migration. The `cmd/ledgerimport` importer (which posts through `store.PostTransaction`, rule 2) now sets each split's `Description` from its own source row's `desc` in `resolveSplit` — a split's description is the description of the ledger ROW that produced it, so multi-row `tid` buckets give each split its own row's desc for free (no per-transaction collapse). Synthesized counter-legs (FX Clearing / Opening Balances), built in `postBucket` from no source row, carry an empty description. Recorded choices:
  - **`Config.PayeeColumn` REMOVED (not deprecated).** The struct field, the `payeeSource`/`payee` builder methods, the `b.payeeID` cache/field, and `PostTransactionInput.PayeeID` assignment are all deleted; `PostTransaction` leaves the transaction-level payee unset (nil). Removal was preferred over a parsed-but-ignored field because the ripple was modest and the bulk of it was payee-removal we were doing anyway. **Consequence flagged in `docs/golive.md`:** `ReadConfig` uses `DisallowUnknownFields`, so any live `mapping.json` still carrying `"payee_column"` now fails the build loudly — the go-live doc tells the reviewer to drop the key. (The loud failure is the intended behavior of `DisallowUnknownFields`.) The store's payee MODEL is untouched — this step only stops the importer from USING it; the payee table/entity removal is a later migration step.
  - **Memo left in place (coexists with description).** This migration is payee→description, not memo→description: `desc` still feeds `split.Memo` (and the txn memo) exactly as before, so mid-migration `split.memo == split.description` for imported rows. Any memo/description consolidation is a later reads/UI step, not pre-empted here. `--anonymize` hashes both memo and description (they share the one hashed local).
  - **Tests (synthetic, rule 11):** `testSource` tid 2's two rows carry DISTINCT desc ("office supplies" / "paid from checking") so per-SPLIT (vs. per-transaction) description is observable; `TestSplitDescriptionFromSourceRow` asserts each split carries its own row's desc, the synthesized counter-leg accounts carry `""`, and NO payees are minted (payee table empty, every txn `payee_id` NULL). The old `TestAnonymizeHashesPayeesAndMemos` became `TestAnonymizeHashesMemosAndDescriptions` (asserts hashed memos + descriptions, and zero payees). `go vet ./...`, `gofmt -l cmd/ledgerimport`, `go test ./cmd/ledgerimport/...`, `make test`, `make check` all green; no new dependency.

- **p26.18 (web: per-split description autocomplete + per-row prefill backend)** — step 4a of the payee→per-split-`description` migration: the server endpoints (`GET /descriptions/suggest`, `GET /descriptions/prefill`, both TxnWrite) the entry grids consume in 4b, modelled on the old payee autofill they replace (whole-grid payee template → per-ROW description prefill; the removed payee suggest → the description suggest). Recorded choices:
  - **Subsidiary is PREFERRED, not filtered.** Both queries take `sub` and float in-subsidiary matches first (`MAX(CASE WHEN t.subsidiary_id=? …) DESC` for suggest; `ORDER BY (t.subsidiary_id=?) DESC` for prefill) rather than filtering to `sub`. Filtering would hide genuinely useful cross-subsidiary descriptions/prefill from a user working a shared vendor across subs; preferring keeps them available but ranked below the local match. `sub=0` (no subsidiary chosen yet) makes the equality term uniformly false, so ordering falls to pure recency.
  - **Prefill amount is formatted in the MATCHED split's own transaction currency.** The prefill endpoint has no in-progress-transaction currency (its only inputs are `q` and `sub`), so the amount is formatted with the exponent of the matched split's OWN transaction currency (`t.currency`, returned by the query) — that is the true minor-unit scale of the stored amount — mirroring `payeeTemplate`'s display-only formatting. The prefill is display-only; the editor re-parses/re-validates the amount on save (if the row's currency differs, the client/editor handles it in 4b). Signed value (net-debit sign), user's number format.
  - **Returned account/fund/program ids are RAW and may be stale.** The prefill returns the split's raw `account_id/fund_id/program_id` even when the account is now inactive/placeholder or out of subsidiary `sub`. The endpoint does NOT filter or drop them — the editor's p26.10 option injection + save-time guard already handle display and validation of such ids, and the 4b client applies the prefill only when the row is otherwise empty. This is a deliberately clean per-row contract; flagged for the 4b UI step.
  - **No-match / blank query → 200 with an empty fragment (not 204/error).** Suggest renders an empty listbox; prefill renders `<div id="desc-prefill" data-found="0">`. The permission-matrix reachability sweep (`TestRouteRegistryComplete`) sends bare requests (no query params) to every route, so erroring on blank input would fail that gate; a 200 empty fragment is also the cleanest client contract ("nothing to prefill"). No new i18n keys — the fragments are pure data with no chrome text.

- **p26.20 (db: physically remove the payee entity)** — final step of the payee→per-split-`description` migration. The payee entity + data + columns + routes are dropped (migration `00021_drop_payee.sql`, forward-only). Recorded choices:
  - **Drill Description cell renders RAW (no `description → memo` fallback), unlike the account-ledger.** The task text said "switch the drill's payee column to description with a description → memo fallback, matching the account-ledger report." The account-ledger falls back to memo *because it has no separate memo column*. The drill report DOES have a separate Memo column (splitMemo → txnMemo), exactly like the register — so applying the fallback would render the memo text in BOTH the Description and Memo columns for description-empty rows. The drill therefore follows the REGISTER's shape (Description = raw `DrillRow.Description`, "—" when empty; Memo is its own column) rather than the account-ledger's fallback. Same rendering as `register.tmpl`.
  - **Bank-import dedupe: rename Go-side only; keep `parsed_payee`/`payee_col` as the mapping-config format.** `DedupeHash`'s text parameter + the `ParsedRow`/`StagedRow`/`ImportRow`/`ImportBatchRow` Go fields were renamed `Payee`→`Description`, but the hash FORMULA is unchanged (`account|date|amount|normalized(desc-text)|normalized(memo)`) so dedupe semantics are preserved (data isn't live, so any hash-value change is moot anyway). The `import_rows.parsed_payee` DB column, the `mapping_profiles.config` `payee_col` JSON field / `Config.PayeeCol`, and the `import.col.payee` label are KEPT (justified survivors): they are bank-statement STAGING metadata / the CSV column-mapping wire format, not the payee ENTITY. Renaming the column/config would need an ALTER + generated-code churn for zero functional gain and is outside the migration's scope. `LedgerSplitDedupeKeys` was rewritten to source the re-hash text from `s.description` (dropping the `LEFT JOIN payees` / `t.payee_id`, which referenced the now-dropped column); the bank-import edit&post WRITE path seeds the bank-account split's `Description` from the staged text so write and re-hash agree on the same split (proven by the bank-import e2e round-trip).
  - **Z3/Z5 parity holds without payee_id by construction.** `payee_id` was removed from `InsertTransactionVersion`'s snapshot INSERT, every `transactions_versions` as-of/history SELECT, the txn version structs, AND the Z3 current-vs-snapshot comparison; the whole `payees` Z3 arm and the `payees_versions` Z5 line were deleted from `internal/ledger/checks.go`. A `transactions_versions` row stays byte-identical to its live row, so `cuento check` is clean on a fresh fixture built through 00021.

- **p26.24 (money: per-currency symbol + placement in amount display)** — every amount now renders with its currency's symbol hugging the digits: USD/MXN prefix `$` (`$1,234.56`), EUR prefix `€`, HNL suffix `L` (`1,234.56L`), all with NO space. Added `money.FormatMoney(minor, currency, exponent, opts)` — a symbol-aware DISPLAY wrapper — alongside the existing bare `money.Format`. Recorded choices:
  - **Symbol comes from a money-package map; PLACEMENT is not DB-backed.** The `currencies` table already carries a `symbol` column (USD/MXN `$`, EUR `€`, HNL `L`), but has NO prefix/suffix column and the display call sites thread only the ISO code, not the DB symbol. So `currencySymbol(code)` in `internal/money/amount.go` owns BOTH symbol and position as a small deterministic switch, with the symbols mirroring the seed exactly (no divergence — only position is genuinely new). Adding a DB position column + threading it to every formatter was out of scope for a display-only change; the map is the smallest reversible choice (AGENTS ambiguity rule). Any UNMAPPED currency (e.g. a new one added via the admin currencies page) falls back to its ISO code as a PREFIX (`JPY1,234.56`) — this is today's `CODE ` convention minus the space, deterministic and crash-free.
  - **Sign wraps the symbol+magnitude, not the other way round.** `FormatMoney` composes the symbol onto the magnitude FIRST, then applies the user's negative style around the whole: negative USD is `-$1,234.56` (Minus) / `($1,234.56)` (Parens); negative HNL `-1,234.56L` / `(1,234.56L)`; DR/CR trails the composed unit (`$1,234.56 DR`, `1,234.56L CR`). Implemented by a shared `format(minor, exp, opts, affix)` where `affix` carries the symbol with a NUL placeholder marking the magnitude slot; `Format` passes an empty affix (bare, unchanged) and `FormatMoney` passes `"$\x00"` / `"\x00L"`.
  - **`Format`/`Parse` stay BARE — symbols are display-only, never re-parsed.** The `Format`↔`Parse` round-trip (property test `TestParseFormatRoundTrip`) is preserved: `Parse` is NOT taught to strip symbols, and every EDITABLE amount field (the txn/expense/import editor prefills — `Amount`/`AmountDR`/`AmountCR`/`AmountInput`, `budgets.go` `form.Amount`, `descriptions.go` `AmountInput`) keeps bare `money.Format` so a save-without-touch round-trips. Only the read-only DISPLAY cells (registers, reports, chart of accounts, statements, budgets, expense/drill/reconcile summaries, funds/programs balances, void review, history) switched to `FormatMoney`. Because the web display now emits the symbol WITHOUT the ISO code, USD and MXN both render `$…` in the UI — the ISO code is no longer shown per-cell (currency is disambiguated by column/context); the CSV export (`csv.go`) and the golden `.txt` KEEP the ISO-code prefix (the golden also ADDS the symbol, so `MXN $400,000.00`) so native-vs-converted stays unambiguous in those machine/review artifacts. The CSV golden is unchanged (machine-plain decimal, no symbol).
  - **`reports.golden.go` `dumpCell` = code + symbol.** The golden `.txt` renders `c.Currency + " " + FormatMoney(...)` (both the ISO code AND the symbol), so the reviewed golden diff is purely additive — every money cell gained its symbol and column widths re-aligned by one char; no value/order/label change except the p26.24 Task-2 label normalization below. No `L` appears in the goldens because the report fixture is USD+MXN only (HNL is go-live-import data); the suffix path is covered by the money unit test.
  - **Task 2: normalized the 8 `*.unrestricted` fund labels.** All eight keys (`fund.unrestricted`, `txn.fund.unrestricted`, `reports.{account_ledger,fund_activity,reconciliation_statement,budget}.unrestricted`, `budget.line.unrestricted`, `expense.line.unrestricted`) now read en `"Unrestricted"` / es `"Sin restricción"` (was a mix of "Unrestricted General"/"Fondo General …" and unaccented/variant Spanish). en/es key sets stay identical (parity test green). Only the account-ledger golden showed the old label text, and it already read "Unrestricted" — so no golden label churn beyond the symbol addition.
- **p26.26 (reports: nested account tree with rolled-up parent subtotals)** — every report that PRESENTS a list of accounts now shows the account hierarchy nested (parent rows containing indented children with rolled-up subtotals) and reuses the p26.25 collapse/expand tree control. In scope: trial balance (the flagship — was a flat one-row-per-(account,currency) list, now nested), balance sheet, income statement, functional expenses (the last three already emitted pre-order `Indent` trees with subtotal parents — they gained only the `data-depth` + tree-controls treatment). Out of scope (each is inherently single-account or a non-account grouping): account ledger, reconciliation statement, fund activity, program statement (accounts listed WITHIN a program, not the chart tree), form 990 (990-line grouping), activities by restriction (derives totals from the tree but lists no accounts). Recorded choice:
  - **The CONVERTED column is the roll-up column; a parent's native + currency cells are blank.** A `reports.Cell` holds exactly one (Minor, Currency), which is why the flat trial balance had one row per (account, currency): a leaf spanning currencies (FX Clearing holds USD+MXN) legitimately has two native figures. A tree needs ONE parent row per node, but a parent whose subtree spans currencies has NO single native sum — so the parent subtotal is carried on the CONVERTED column only (single target currency, sums cleanly under D12), with the native amount + currency cells left blank on placeholder rows. Leaf rows are unchanged (native + currency + converted). This keeps `parent == Σ children` true and hand-verifiable on the converted column, and is only meaningful under a real target currency — the bare-native-mode path (`TargetCurrency == ""`, exercised only by the scope test, which asserts leaf account sets, never parent arithmetic) leaves the parent converted cell in the empty target currency. The fold reuses the existing income-statement / balance-sheet `toTreeNodes`/`indexTree` rollup over `BalancesAsOf` (no new store query); parent rows are `RowSubtotal` so the balancing re-sums (`SumMoneyColumn`, RowData-only) stay leaf-only and the native-per-currency-zero / converted-grand-total-zero proofs are unaffected. Web: a `Report.Tree bool` flag gates `data-depth` + the shared `.tree-controls` + the `treetable.js` load in the ONE shared `report.tmpl`, so non-tree reports render byte-identically; `treetable.js`'s controls lookup was generalized (`findControls` resolves `.tree-controls` rather than the accounts-only `.accounts-controls`) so the p26.25 module enhances report tables unchanged.

- **p26.37 (ux: prefill the header balancing account on entry)** — a NEW transaction opens with its header (position-0 / balancing) account pre-selected as a data-entry convenience. Recorded choices:
  - **"Last-used header account" = most-recently-CREATED, per actor, not most-recent by business date.** From the top nav (no register origin) the header account is prefilled from `LastHeaderAccountForActor` (new READ-ONLY sqlc query `last_used.sql`): the position-0 split account of the transaction the current user MOST RECENTLY ENTERED, joined via `transactions_versions.op='create'` + `changes.actor_id` and ordered by `changes.id DESC` (monotonic insertion order). Recency is by create order, NOT the transaction's business `date` — a backdated entry should not become "last used". Scoped to the current actor (never leaks another user's last account). Soft-deleted transactions are excluded. Zero rows → 0 → the header is left blank. This is the smallest reversible reading of an underspecified "last-used" (AGENTS ambiguity rule); the alternative (a per-user stored preference column) would need a migration + write-path plumbing for a pure convenience.
  - **From a register, the register's account wins over the last-used lookup.** When the editor is opened via `?from=/accounts/<id>/register` (the register's new-transaction link, already sanitized to a same-site path by `sanitizeOrigin`), the header account is that register's account, parsed from the origin path (`accountIDFromRegisterPath`), taking precedence over the last-used store lookup. Only the first-load path prefills; the subsidiary re-filter path already rehydrates `MainAccount` from the posted `main_*` hidden fields, so prefilling there would clobber the user's chosen header on every subsidiary change. `injectMainAccount` makes the prefilled account selectable even if it is now inactive / out-of-subsidiary (p26.10).

- **p26.38 (ux: expense-grid zebra + same-row prefill + per-subsidiary description autocomplete)** — three related entry-grid fixes. Recorded choices:
  - **Description suggest/prefill switched from subsidiary-PREFER to subsidiary-FILTER (reverses the p26.18 decision).** p26.18 deliberately PREFERRED (sort-first) the in-subsidiary match so a cross-sub description stayed available. But per-subsidiary accounts differ, so a cross-sub prefill carries an out-of-sub account/fund/program — surfacing subsidiary B's descriptions/prefill while entering in subsidiary A is wrong. Both `SuggestDescriptions` and `PrefillDescription` now FILTER to the subsidiary via `AND (? = 0 OR t.subsidiary_id = ?)` (the sub id bound TWICE, positional), dropping the `CASE`/prefer ordering. `sub=0` (no subsidiary chosen yet) stays UNSCOPED — the guard's `? = 0` arm passes all rows — preserving the reachability-sweep and single-sub store tests. sqlc isn't installed, so `descriptions.sql.go` was hand-synced to the `.sql` (query const + the extra positional arg). The web handler tests were rewritten from prefer-assertions to filter-assertions (a sub2-only description does NOT appear/prefill under sub1).
  - **The locked-subsidiary case is threaded via a `data-sub` carrier on the grid form.** Once an expense report has a saved line its subsidiary LOCKS and the `#er-sub` picker is replaced by static text — so `descfield.subOf()` (which reads `#txn-subsidiary, #er-sub, [name="subsidiary"]`) would match nothing and fall back to `sub=0` = UNSCOPED, defeating the filter exactly when adding subsequent lines. Fixed by rendering `data-sub="{{.SubID}}"` on `#expense-grid-form` and having `subOf()` fall back to it when no live sub select/value exists. (A hidden `[name="subsidiary"]` would also POST to the lines handler, which ignores it, but `data-sub` is collision-free.)
  - **The expense-grid same-row prefill needed NO code change — it was already correct post-p26.32.** The reported "prefill lands on the alternating row" symptom predates p26.32's two-`<tr>`-per-`<tbody>` restructure. descfield's row resolution (`closest('.txn-row, .el-row')` → the tbody, `querySelector` descending both `<tr>`) is shared and grid-agnostic, and the txn grid exercises it identically (combo-descprefill txn tests pass). A valid Playwright repro (a POSTED transaction as the prefill source — draft expense LINES are not `splits` until the report is reviewed & posted — then a filled line 0 + a description typed/picked on the trailing line 1) lands the prefill on the SAME line. Added the regression assertion (passing) rather than fabricating a fix; the p26.32 tbody grouping already corrected the targeting.
  - **The per-split zebra selectors gained `.el-row`.** The p26.32 zebra rule targeted only `.txn-grid-2row tbody.txn-row:nth-of-type(even)`; the expense grid uses the same `.txn-grid-2row` table but `<tbody class="el-row">`, so it was unbanded. Added the `.el-row` / `.el-row-error` / `.el-delete-cell` twins to the zebra + top-rule selectors (presentational only). The editable expense table has only `.el-row` tbodies, so `nth-of-type` counts splits.

- **p26.40 (import: marker-driven "Restore the Way" campus fund, assigned per split by `kat=campus`)** — the importer creates one restricted fund, **"Restore the Way"**, and tags every historical split whose source `kat` is `"campus"` with it. Recorded choices:
  - **Restriction type = `purpose` (purpose-restricted).** The sensible default for a campus/capital fund (a use-restriction, not a time or perpetual-endowment restriction). Matches the store's `purpose|time|perpetual` CHECK; the user did not specify, so the smallest sensible choice holds (AGENTS ambiguity rule).
  - **`kat=campus` takes PRECEDENCE over the donor fund.** The user directed "treat splits with kat campus as Restore the Way". In `resolveSplit` the donor→fund lookup runs first, then a `kat=="campus"` split OVERWRITES `FundID` with the campus fund regardless of donor — so a campus row that also carries a donor still resolves to Restore the Way, never a donor fund. The kat→PROGRAM path is UNCHANGED and additive: `kat` still feeds the program dimension (a campus split also gets the "Campus" program); this step adds a fund path, it does not replace the program path.
  - **The fund is a NEW dedicated config field, not a donor entry.** `Config.CampusFund *FundConfig` (json `campus_fund`, nil = feature off) lives outside the donor-keyed `Funds` map because it is marker-driven, not donor-driven. It is created in the scaffold (`builder.campusFund`, after the donor funds) and its id is carried on `BuildResult.CampusFundID`; `reloadState` rehydrates it by name for the separate-process per-subsidiary import path.
  - **Subsidiary scope = ALL configured child subsidiaries (a programmatically-derived superset).** The store requires a transaction's subsidiary to be within its fund's subsidiary set (rule 7). The scaffold reads NO source rows, so the campus-posting subsidiary set cannot be observed at scaffold time; instead the fund is scoped to `configuredSubsidiaryNames(cfg)` — every configured child subsidiary. That is provably a superset of any subset of subsidiaries that post a campus split, and was verified against the go-live data as EXACTLY the child set (campus splits post to both children, none to the root). The `campus_fund` config's own `subsidiaries` list is intentionally ignored (documented on the struct) so a mis-scoped config can never narrow the fund below the campus footprint.
  - **The accepted self-heal is UNCHANGED and its campus plug leg is made countable.** ~53% of campus transactions' campus subset does not net to zero on its own; the existing per-fund residual self-heal (`postBucket`) already appends an Opening-Balances counter-leg tagged with the campus fund so the fund group nets to zero, and warns. The user has ACCEPTED these plug legs, so the warning is NOT suppressed; it now carries a distinct `[campus-plug]` marker so the operator can COUNT how many campus transactions needed a plug apart from other imbalances.
  - **Real-data verification (counts only, rule 11):** the campus fund was created (purpose-restricted, subsidiary set size 2 = both children); 5,752 splits were tagged with it (≈4.3k source campus splits + the Opening-Balances plug legs); 928 distinct transactions triggered a `[campus-plug]` counter-leg. `cuento check` on the produced db is clean — **0 errors, 1 warning (Z18: the campus fund's aggregate asset balance is negative)** — expected: the plug legs route campus residuals to equity rather than a real asset inflow, so the fund reads "overspent" in aggregate; Z18 is a warning (restricted-fund overspend), not an error, so the non-strict go-live gate passes.
  - **Test (synthetic, rule 11):** `TestCampusFundAssignedByKat` on the synthetic fixture — extended `testConfig` with a `campus_fund` and a `campus`→`Campus` program, `testSource` with a fully-campus self-balancing txn (tid 7) and a mixed txn whose campus subset does not self-balance (tid 8, whose campus split also carries a donor to prove the override) on a dedicated `Campus Costs` account — asserts (a) the fund is created purpose-restricted with the child-superset subsidiaries, (b) campus splits carry it AND the Campus program (donor overridden), (c) the mixed txn imports via the Opening-Balances self-heal with a `[campus-plug]` warning and the fund-tagged counter-leg, and `ledger.Check` is Error-clean, (d) the non-campus split stays unrestricted.

- **p26.41 (ux: one combined program/class control per split, replacing the separate program select + functional-class select)** — the transaction editor's body rows now offer ONE control where the user picks either a program node or Admin/Fundraising, instead of choosing a program AND a class. Recorded choices:
  - **Encoded option values, decoded server-side into the UNCHANGED SplitInput contract.** The combined `<select name="progclass_<i>">` carries `c:management` (Admin) / `c:fundraising` (Fundraising) / `p:<programID>`. `decodeProgClass` maps these into the existing `Program` + `Class` inputs, so the store's rule-7 invariants (program defaults on R/E; functional class required on expense, forbidden elsewhere) are untouched — this is a UI + handler-decode change only, no store change. `p:<id>` yields class=`program` on an EXPENSE row and no class on a revenue row (the row account's type is threaded to `parseSplitForms` via `model.acctTypeMap()`).
  - **A hidden `program_<i>` carrier guarantees idempotency (the load-bearing decision).** The Restore-the-Way import (p26.40) creates `management`/`fundraising` expense splits that carry a SPECIFIC (non-root) program. If Admin/Fundraising meant "no program", opening such a split and re-saving would silently default its program back to root and churn a `splits_versions` row. So a hidden carrier round-trips the stored program verbatim; a `c:*` pick keeps it; a `p:<id>` pick overwrites it (and the client keeps the carrier in step so a later switch to Admin retains the last program). Load→save-unchanged is byte-identical even when the program is non-root (`TestTxnProgClassNonRootIdempotent`).
  - **Labels: "Admin" and "Fundraising" in this control; "Management & general" stays for reports.** New i18n keys `txn.progclass.{admin,fundraising}` (both catalogs). `functional.management` = "Management & general" is UNCHANGED — the 990 reports use the formal term. So the same class reads "Admin" in the fast-entry control and "Management & general" on a report; deliberate.
  - **combobox.js compatibility.** The encoded values are never the empty string and never value-`0` (program ids are non-zero, and `c:`/`p:` are non-empty), so combobox's `currentLabel`/`resyncCombos` blank/value-0 special-casing (p26.31) is not tripped — every option displays its label, never blank. The control stays a `combo-input` (type-to-filter over ~27 options).
  - **p26.42 (the expense-report DRAFT grid) SKIPPED as not applicable.** `expense_lines` (migration 00017) has `program_id` but NO `functional_class` column — a draft line genuinely cannot carry a class; the reviewer assigns it at review&post, where the editor already renders `transaction-form` and thus already inherits this combined control. Adding a class to the draft line would be a schema/store change, out of scope, and would contradict the p26.39 "draft omits functional class" decision. So the combined choice lands exactly where the class is resolved.

- **p26.43 (import: "Restore the Way" as a live restricted fund with a chronological drawdown cap — SUPERSEDES the p26.40 whole-transaction campus plug)** — the p26.40 model tagged EVERY `kat=campus` split to the fund and let the per-fund self-heal route the ~53% residual to equity: 928 plug legs and a NEGATIVE (~-$180k) aggregate fund asset balance → a `Z18` restricted-fund-overspend warning. The user decided to instead treat RtW as a fund that CANNOT overspend its revenue, so its asset balance stays ≥ 0 and Z18 is clean. Recorded choices:
  - **A GLOBAL, CHRONOLOGICAL, PER-CURRENCY drawdown pool decides RtW-vs-unrestricted per campus R/E split (Pass 1, `campus.go`).** Campus revenue received is restricted until spent, so we walk every campus revenue/expense split in DATE order (tie-broken by tid then group index) maintaining a running pool balance. A campus REVENUE split is always RtW and GROWS the pool by its magnitude (the fund may end positive — unexpended restricted resources). A campus EXPENSE split is RtW only if the pool covers the WHOLE split, drawing it down; once the pool is exhausted, later campus expenses OVERFLOW to unrestricted (an overspent campus cost is an ordinary unrestricted expense; its would-be donor fund is dropped too). The pool is keyed PER CURRENCY because campus posts in USD and HNL and adding minor units across currencies is meaningless. It runs over the SAME skip-filtered `groups` used for posting, so the `(tid, group-index)` decision keys align with the resolve loop; and because every per-subsidiary import process is handed the FULL export and sorts deterministically, each derives the identical plan — the cross-subsidiary state is reproduced, not shared.
  - **Offset PAIRING replaces the plug for the normal case (Pass 2, `offsetRtW` in `postBucket`).** For the RtW campus splits in a currency bucket, the offset legs must sum to the negation of their total so the campus-fund group nets to zero (rule 7/Z10) with NO plug. We draw that from the bucket's UNRESTRICTED balance-sheet (asset/liability) splits in source order, same side only, DIVIDING a balance-sheet split into an RtW portion + an unrestricted remainder (two `SplitInput`s on the SAME account, different fund — the store allows this: per-fund and overall zero-sum are the only balance invariants) when it only partially offsets. Because the whole bucket already nets to zero and the RtW subset nets to zero, the unrestricted remainder nets to zero automatically — so genuinely unrelated (non-campus) splits stay unrestricted with their own offset portion, no extra bookkeeping. **Offset candidates are restricted to `fund==nil` balance-sheet splits** (a donor-tagged split is never divided): dividing a donor split would unbalance that donor group and the store would REJECT the whole transaction (silent data loss), worse than a plug. The real data has zero donor-tagged balance-sheet splits inside campus buckets, so this restriction never changes the result there; it is a safety rail for future data.
  - **The p26.40 campus plug is kept ONLY as the rare pathological fallback (spec B).** When a bucket's balance-sheet splits cannot supply the offset on the correct side — a multi-currency campus tid whose only counter-leg is the equity FX Clearing account (D3), or restricted revenue booked straight against a non-campus expense with no cash leg — the leftover falls through to the existing per-fund self-heal (a fund-tagged `[campus-plug]` Opening-Balances leg). The generic self-heal code is unchanged; it just becomes UNREACHABLE for the normal case (the per-fund residual loop computes 0 for a fully-offset campus group). This is NOT the spec's stated "plugs → ~0": on the real data 457 buckets still plug to Opening Balances (+250 multi-currency FX-Clearing legs), because the dominant campus pattern is restricted revenue offset by a NON-campus expense (447 buckets) or a campus split with no balance-sheet leg at all (256, largely the 256 multi-currency campus tids). This is expected, documented, and does NOT drive the fund asset negative — the offset that DID land keeps the asset backing positive.
  - **`resolveSplit` now takes `(tid, idx, r)` and consults the plan; the kat→program path is untouched.** A campus R/E split assigned RtW takes the campus fund (overriding the donor); one that overflowed stays unrestricted. Campus BALANCE-SHEET splits get no fund in `resolveSplit` — they are offset candidates the Pass-2 pass may retag. Every campus split (RtW or overflowed) still gets its Campus program (kat feeds program as before).
  - **Real-data verification (counts only, rule 11):** 2,253 campus R/E splits assigned RtW, 30 overflowed to unrestricted, 980 balance-sheet offset portions (147 of them divided splits), 457 `[campus-plug]` Opening-Balances legs + 250 FX-Clearing multi-currency legs (down from 928 plug transactions under p26.40), 0 store rejections (no data loss). The campus fund's aggregate asset balance flipped from ~-$180k to **+$51,393,034 USD minor (+$513,930.34) / +134,355,053 HNL minor (+HNL 1,343,550.53)** — both ≥ 0. `bin/cuento check` on the produced db is fully clean (0 errors, **the Z18 restricted-fund-overspend warning is GONE**).
  - **Test (synthetic, rule 11):** `TestCampusFundAssignedByKat` rewritten to exercise every branch — campus revenue builds the pool + RtW cash offset; a campus expense within the pool → RtW with a DIVIDED cash offset (no plug); a campus expense exceeding the pool → overflow to unrestricted; a cash split shared between a campus and non-campus expense DIVIDED so each portion carries the right fund; `ledger.Check` Error-clean AND the CAMPUS fund's Z18 gone with a ≥0 asset balance (a synthetic GRANT1 MXN transfer legitimately trips its OWN Z18, so the assertion is scoped to the campus fund); non-campus splits stay unrestricted. `TestCampusOffsetFallbackPlug` (bespoke tiny source) covers the pathological plug fallback: an un-offsettable campus subset still posts, stays balanced, and carries the `[campus-plug]` marker.

- **p26.46 (import: account-driven campus marker for campus FIXED-ASSET accounts — land / buildings-under-construction / a campus building held BY the campus project)** — the user identified three source fixed-asset accounts as campus capital that must belong to the "Restore the Way" restricted fund, though their source `kat` is not `"campus"` (they are asset lines, not revenue/expense). The p26.43 campus path is R/E-only, so these splits were never caught. Recorded choices:
  - **A new config field `Config.CampusAssetAccounts []string` (json `campus_asset_accounts`) lists the source_acct keys** of campus fixed-asset accounts whose splits join the campus fund regardless of `kat`. It is matched by the exact `source_acct` key the importer already uses to resolve an account (`b.res.AccountIDs[r.Acct]`) — a full-string chart-account key, NOT a fragile name substring. Empty/nil = the account-driven path is off (kat=campus behaviour unchanged). The set is built once in `transactions()` from `cfg` (always loaded, so the separate-process per-subsidiary reload path inherits it with no extra rehydration). The three real codes live ONLY in the local gitignored mapping config (rule 11); committed code and the synthetic test carry invented account names.
  - **The R/E (`isRE`) guard WAS the gap, and the account marker bypasses it.** Both `buildCampusPlan` (Pass 1) and the kat-driven `resolveSplit` branch skip anything that is not revenue/expense (`if !isRE { continue }`) — which is exactly why these asset splits were never assigned RtW. `resolveSplit` gains a SEPARATE branch (before the kat branch): a split on a configured campus-asset account is tagged RtW directly, overriding any donor, bypassing the isRE guard. It sets `campusRtW = true` (the load-bearing flag) so Pass-2 `offsetRtW` includes the asset in `rtwSum` (pairing its cash counter-leg onto the fund) AND excludes it as an offset candidate — the campus subset nets to zero with no plug.
  - **A campus asset purchase is an asset SWAP within the fund, so it must NOT touch the drawdown pool.** `buildCampusPlan` (pool = campus revenue − campus expense) is left UNCHANGED: these accounts are assets with a blank/non-campus `kat`, so both the `kat != "campus"` filter and the `isRE` guard already exclude them from the pool. Only the direct `resolveSplit` assignment tags them — the spendable revenue pool is unaffected (Dr Asset / Cr Cash neither adds nor subtracts restricted spendable revenue).
  - **Real-data verification (counts only, rule 11; measured against a same-data baseline build with the marker removed, not against a stale figure):** the 3 marker accounts hold **7** splits; baseline 0 of them were RtW, with the marker **all 7** are RtW (a net **+7** marker-account splits, +14 total RtW splits counting each asset's paired counter-leg retagged RtW). **Plug legs: 457 with the marker vs 457 baseline — delta 0 (NO new campus plug leg).** 0 store rejections in the full build log and all 7 marker splits are present in the produced db (no data loss). The campus fund's asset balance stayed POSITIVE, rising from +185,748,087 to +191,191,287 USD minor (still ≥ 0). `bin/cuento check -db bin/dev-rtw3.db` is fully clean (0 violations, no new Z18). Because a campus fixed asset can only add asset backing, it can never drive the fund negative here.
  - **Test (synthetic, rule 11):** `TestCampusFundAssignedByKat` extended with a campus CAPITAL purchase (`Campus Land`, a marker asset account, Dr 1000 / Cr Checking 1000) dated between the campus revenue and the campus expense and carrying a donor to prove the marker overrides it. Asserts the Land split is RtW (not the donor fund), its Checking offset is retagged RtW, the txn is one balanced transaction with NO plug, the pre-existing pool assertions (the Sep campus expense still RtW, the Oct one still overflows) stay green — so the 1000 asset did NOT drain the pool — and `ledger.Check` stays Error-clean with the campus fund asset ≥ 0.

- **p26.47 (import: FX-NORMALIZE the campus drawdown pool to USD + widen the campus fixed-asset account set)** — two orthogonal fixes to "Restore the Way", decided with the owner and validated against their Capital Campaign report (restricted net assets +$295,817, positive every quarter). Recorded choices:
  - **Fix 1 — the p26.43 drawdown pool is now FX-NORMALIZED to a single USD number, not per-currency.** The p26.43 pool was keyed PER CURRENCY (one USD bucket, one HNL bucket) and chronological at split granularity, which STARVED it: USD donations could not fund Honduran (Lempira) construction, so ~30 campus expense legs wrongly overflowed to Unrestricted even though the campaign never overspent in aggregate. The drawdown CONCEPT is kept, but the pool is now a SINGLE running `int64` in the org base currency (USD): a campus expense overflows to unrestricted ONLY if its USD-converted amount exceeds the USD-converted accumulated revenue. `campus.go buildCampusPlan` collapses `pool map[string]int64` → one `int64`, and each campus R/E split's pool contribution is converted by the new `recordAmountUSD` helper.
  - **The pool converts on the SAME rate path the consolidated-USD REPORTS use** — `store.RateOn(native, base, split-date)` (on-or-before the split's date) + `money.ConvertMinor` (D12) — mirroring `reports.Toolkit.ConvertMinorAt`, so the pool basis reconciles with the report figures by construction. `PutRates` already runs before `transactions()` in `build.go`, so the builder reuses the store's rate table directly. A split already in the base currency short-circuits (identity, no rate lookup).
  - **STORED split amounts stay NATIVE (rule 3); only the overflow DECISION is USD.** `resolveSplit` still posts `NetDebit(db,cr)` in native minor units and `offsetRtW` still balances buckets natively; the USD figure is used ONLY by `buildCampusPlan`'s RtW-vs-overflow decision. So the DB never stores a converted amount.
  - **The task assumed the `fdb`/`fcr` columns are USD; the DATA proved otherwise, so we took the task's alternative "existing rate conversion" branch.** Empirically (aggregate checks over `fixtures/source`, rule 11 — no values here): `fdb`/`fcr` is each split's amount in its SUBSIDIARY's FUNCTIONAL currency, NOT a common USD basis — USD for the US subsidiary but **HNL for the Honduras subsidiary** (whose base_currency is HNL). So HNL-subsidiary HNL legs carry `xrt=1` and `fdb==db` (both HNL) with NO USD figure anywhere in the row. `native × xrt` also fails for those same legs (xrt=1). The only basis that yields USD for every leg — and the basis the report uses — is `currency` + a dated HNL→USD rate from `rates.csv`. Hence the rate-conversion path above.
  - **The pool converts each split at ITS OWN date (on-or-before), not at a single as-of closing rate.** This is a deliberate, more-principled basis (each restricted donation valued in USD at its receipt-date rate), and is one reason the fund's USD net-assets figure will not match the report's +$295,817 exactly (the report converts at one as-of rate). `rates.csv` covers 2016-01-01 onward and every campus HNL R/E split is 2022+ , so no `RateOn` miss occurs on the real data.
  - **Fix 2 — the campus fixed-asset account set was widened to the report's construction universe + Casa Retoño.** The set was `1610`(land) `1650`(building-under-construction) `1683`(Casa Retoño); it is now the UNION `1610 1650 1651 1652 1653 1670 1680 1683` (added `1651` Materiales Directos, `1652` Mano de Obra, `1653` Otros Costos, `1670` Vehículos, `1680` Edificios). This is a CONFIG-ONLY change (`campus_asset_accounts` in the gitignored `mapping.json`, rule 11); the p26.46 account-driven marker code already honours a multi-account set, so no committed code changed for the set. These are balance-sheet assets → per p26.46 they are tagged RtW with offset pairing but do NOT enter the revenue−expense pool (asset swap); verified still holds (no new plug legs).
  - **`1683` (Casa Retoño) is KEPT even though the owner's report OMITS it from the campus fixed-asset universe.** The owner explicitly named Casa Retoño as campus capital in the p26.46 instruction; the report's omission is flagged here for later OWNER CONFIRMATION — if the report is authoritative, `1683` should be dropped from `campus_asset_accounts`.
  - **Real-data verification (counts only, rule 11; built to a temp db, `bin/cuento check` clean, 0 store rejections):** overflow campus R/E legs **30 → 15** — the HNL overflow is ELIMINATED (69,422 HNL native → **0**) but the USD overflow is UNCHANGED ($13,901.43 USD, 15 legs). **This is NOT the spec's "overflow ≈ 0" target, and the residual is FLAGGED for an owner decision.** The residual is a DIFFERENT root cause the FX fix was never meant to address: it is a chronological **inception-timing** artifact — all 15 legs are USD (so rate-independent), clustered in Q1 2021, where campus EXPENSE ($14,020) precedes campus REVENUE ($128) in date order, so the pool (starting at 0) cannot yet cover them. This contradicts the owner's "positive every quarter" report and suggests the import lacks early restricted revenue the report reflects (pledge-vs-cash timing, or a carried-forward opening balance) — an OWNER QUESTION. Not self-fixed: seeding the pool or allowing a transient-negative pool is a design change not authorized by this step. Plug legs **457** (unchanged from the p26.46 baseline — no new plug from the FX change or the widened asset set). The 5 new campus-asset accounts hold **47 HNL splits (HNL 456,394.82 ≈ $17,072) all now RtW**. Campus fund asset balance stays POSITIVE (**+$568,362.34 USD / +HNL 1,275,128.31**), so **no Z18**. Fund restricted net assets ≈ **+$437,773.74 USD** (at the latest closing rate) — positive and directionally consistent with the report's +$295,817 (higher because ~$122k of dropped 'consolidating' legs is a SEPARATE pending decision and because of the per-split-date vs single-as-of rate basis).
  - **Z18 stays PER-CURRENCY and untouched (shipped ledger invariant, out of importer scope).** A synthetic risk surfaced during test design: because offsets are same-currency (D3) but the pool is cross-currency, a currency whose RtW expense exceeds its OWN revenue would drive that currency's Z18 asset column negative. On the real data both currencies are self-sufficient in aggregate (USD rev $711k > exp $295k; HNL rev 981k > exp 781k) so no column goes negative and Z18 is clean; the synthetic test is written as a TIMING BRIDGE (foreign revenue funds a domestic expense at spend time, domestic revenue arrives later to restore the column to ≥ 0), NOT a permanent subsidy, to stay Z18-clean without weakening the assertion.
  - **Test (synthetic, rule 11):** `TestCampusFundAssignedByKat` extended: (a2) a NON-USD (MXN) campus revenue (tid 12) whose USD-converted value funds a later USD campus expense (tid 13) that NO per-currency USD pool could cover (total USD campus revenue < the expense) — proving the FX-normalized pool bridges currencies; a LATER USD campus revenue (tid 15) restores the USD Z18 column to ≥ 0; (b3) a SECOND marker fixed-asset account (`Campus Building`, a `1670`-style line) tagged RtW with its offset, proving the widened set is not special-cased and an asset swap does not drain the pool. The pre-existing overflow assertion (tid 10) stays green (its date precedes the MXN bridge, so the global pool is still exhausted there). `buildInto`/scaffold test paths now seed a synthetic MXN→USD rate (`testRates`) so the cross-currency pool conversion fires.

- **p26.51 (reports: a cuento-native Capital Campaign report reproducing `campus.py`, parameterized by restricted fund)** — a new `funds`-group report (`capital_campaign`) that structurally matches the owner's Python quarterly capital-campaign statement but computes it the cuento way (per-subsidiary, closing-rate), scoped to ONE restricted fund via the `fund` param (reusable, not hardcoded). Recorded choices:
  - **Land and Fixed Assets are COLLAPSED into one "Capitalized" line + a per-account detail section, NOT split by rule.** campus.py isolates Land (1610) from the fixed-asset rollup (1650…) by hardcoded account NUMBERS. cuento's chart nests Land UNDER a "Fixed Assets" placeholder parent and the report layer has no rule-clean way to isolate "Land" or "the fixed-asset subtree": rule 11 bars the numbers and p26.46 bars name-substring matching. So the quarterly matrix carries ONE combined **Capitalized assets** line (= campus.py Land + Fixed Assets), and a trailing **capital-detail** section lists each capital asset account by its stored NAME (`TextCell`, exactly like the balance sheet's account rows) — "Land" appears purely because the chart names an account Land, never by a report branch. This ties the real-data Land line to campus.py's **$166,482.00 to the penny** with zero classification logic.
  - **The line items map 1:1 onto the shipped p15.8 `FundStatement`, so RNA is an already-tested quantity.** Per quarter: Gross Revenue = `Received` (−Σ revenue), Gross Expenses = `AppliedExpense`, Capitalized = `Capitalized`/non-expense applications, and **Restricted Net Assets = the spendable `Closing`** — because the fund opens at 0, `Closing = Rev − Exp − Capitalized`, which IS campus.py's RNA formula. Capital vs spendable-cash asset classification reuses `FundPeriodStatement`'s non-revenue-debit detection (computed over the full span so a quarter's view isn't clipped). Engine = one `store.FundLedger` read bucketed by the existing `Toolkit.ByPeriod(GranQuarter)` — no new toolkit helper was needed (quarter bucketing already exists), so this is ONE commit, not a toolkit-split pair.
  - **FX basis = per-quarter-end / report-date CLOSING rate (`ConvertMinorAt`, D12), NOT campus.py's per-split-date.** Flow lines convert at the quarter-end rate; balance lines (Capitalized, RNA) convert as-of quarter-end. This is cuento's standard per-period-end convention and yields a small EXPECTED residual vs the consolidated Python report (the report is per-subsidiary + closing-rate; it will NOT tie to the penny to campus.py, by design — the accepted scope of a "native report"). The residual is visible in the golden (RNA cumulative $7,758.39 vs Rev−Exp−Cap $7,758.38 — a 1-cent per-currency rounding residual). With no target currency the report renders native, single-currency (summing native across currencies is meaningless — the params default guards this).
  - **The CUMULATIVE-total flow figures reconvert at the report-date rate and therefore do NOT equal the sum of the per-quarter converted cells — this is intended, not a bug.** In the golden, per-quarter Gross Revenue Q1 $20,000.00 + Q2 $5,772.50 = $25,772.50, but the Cumulative total shows $25,645.96 (the MXN grant reconverted at the report-date 2025-12 rate rather than its 2025-06 receipt rate — a ~$127 FX artifact). This is a direct consequence of the closing-rate basis (a cumulative figure is a single as-of conversion, not a running sum of dated conversions) and is exactly why the cuento cumulative will not tie to campus.py's per-split-date `cumsum`. A report that wanted the summed-per-quarter total would have to abandon the single-as-of basis; we deliberately keep the closing-rate basis consistent with the balance sheet / income statement.
  - **On REAL data the "Capitalized" line is BROADER than campus.py's Land + Fixed Assets: the non-revenue-debit heuristic also sweeps in fund-tagged RECEIVABLES** (e.g. "Cuenta por Cobrar" pledge/undeposited-adjacent accounts that took capitalizing debits on disbursement txns). So cuento's Capitalized = the fund's ENTIRE non-cash asset position and RNA = its TRUE spendable balance, whereas campus.py's RNA subtracts only Land + Fixed Assets. This means the cuento-vs-campus.py RNA divergence is a CLASSIFICATION difference (what counts as "deployed") layered on top of the FX-basis difference — not FX alone. The per-account capital-detail section makes this visible (each such account shows by name), and the Land line itself still ties exactly because Land is a distinct fund-tagged account. Documented rather than "corrected": excluding receivables would require a rule-clean asset sub-classification cuento's chart does not expose (the same rule-11 constraint that collapsed Land/Fixed Assets).
  - **Pledges Due / Undeposited (campus.py lines) are OMITTED, not partially shown.** A prior review found cuento fund-tags only a SUBSET of the pledge/undeposited splits (pledge acct only; ~330/19,082 undeposited splits tagged), so a fund-scoped figure would be materially incomplete. The report does NOT fabricate the untagged portion and does NOT present a misleadingly-partial line; the omission is documented here. (The fund-tagged receivable accounts that took capitalizing debits DO surface in the capital-detail section as ordinary fund-tagged asset positions, faithfully summed — including the negative import-artifact balances from p26.43's offset/divided legs, which are NOT "cleaned".)
  - **Scope note:** cuento is per-subsidiary; a campaign fund lives only in its member subsidiaries (no synthetic CONS entity). The report reflects that eliminated/per-sub view.
  - **DATA via an opt-in fixture SEAM `(*Fixture).ExtendCapitalCampaign`, mirroring `ExtendRates`/`ExtendReconciliation`.** `New()` does NOT call it, so the base fixture and every existing golden/tally stay byte-identical (the only golden that changed is `capital_campaign.{txt,csv}`). The seam adds a "Restore the Way" restricted fund with multi-quarter USD+MXN revenue, a Land purchase, and Construction (fixed-asset) purchases; it layers cleanly with `ExtendRates` for a converted run.
  - **Real-data sanity check (counts/figures only, rule 11; `bin/dev.db`, NOT committed):** running the report for the live "Restore the Way" fund converted to USD ties the **Land detail row EXACTLY to $166,482.00** (campus.py's figure) and yields cumulative Gross Revenue ≈ **$748,659.32** / Gross Expenses ≈ **$310,885.58** — directionally consistent with campus.py's ~$714.7k / ~$243k, the higher figures reflecting the documented FX (per-split-date vs closing-rate) + scope (per-subsidiary + p26.43-47 import) residual. `go vet ./...` / `gofmt -l` (empty) / `make test` / `make check` green.

- **p26.54 (reports: program statement gains an OPTIONAL currency selector; native stays the default)** — the program statement was native-only per its p15.10 design (per-currency rows, no conversion — a program is a mission dimension read in the money it occurred in). The user asked for a currency selector like the converting reports. Recorded choices:
  - **Native is the DEFAULT; conversion is opt-in.** A new `ParamsSpec.CurrencyOptional` flag (distinct from `Currency`, which defaults the target to the scope base and ALWAYS converts) leaves `TargetCurrency` EMPTY unless the user explicitly picks a currency; the select carries a leading "— native —" choice (`reports.currency.native`, both catalogs). This preserves BOTH the report's documented native-figures rationale AND the golden rule: the golden test builds Params with no currency → native → the `program_statement.{txt,csv}` goldens stay BYTE-IDENTICAL (verified: `make golden` shows zero diff). Reversing the default to always-convert would have silently changed the golden numbers and broken the exact-3-column e2e assertion.
  - **Converted view = income-statement/trial-balance shape.** When a target is picked the Currency column DROPS and each account collapses to ONE converted row per program column (via `ProgramActivity` with `RateClosing` at the period end, D12 — the same closing-rate basis the balance sheet / capital campaign use). A converted cell sums across an account's native currencies, so (like the trial balance) it is NOT drillable; the native default keeps the per-currency drills. Rejected the convert-in-place variant (keep the currency column, convert amounts) — its per-currency total/net rows become incoherent.
  - **Reachability:** the converted path has no golden (native is the default), so a bespoke `TestProgramStatementConverted` (with `ExtendRates`) asserts the Currency column is gone, rows collapse (fewer than native), every money cell is the target currency, and no converted cell drills.
  - **STICKY headers (CSS-only):** the shared `report.tmpl` wraps the table in `.report-scroll`; `@media screen` makes `thead th` sticky-top and the first column sticky-left (opaque backgrounds + a z-index stack, top-left corner highest) so a wide/tall matrix keeps its row + column headers visible while scrolling. Scoped to `@media screen` so print/PDF is never clipped by the max-height; goldens (the Table, not this shell) and the CSV are unaffected. This is generic (helps every report), not program-statement-special.
  - `go vet ./...` / `gofmt -l` (empty) / `make test` / node `--test` / i18n parity / reports + accounts + csp-clean e2e green.

- **p26.56 (import: a non-USD split's stored native amount comes from the FOREIGN `fdb`/`fcr` columns, not the base `db`/`cr` columns — a data-corruption fix)** — the importer derived every split's native amount from `NetDebit(r.Db, r.Cr, exp)` and posted it under `currency = r.Currency`. In the export `db`/`cr` carry the org-BASE (USD) figure and `fdb`/`fcr` the FOREIGN native figure (docs/ledger-export.md "Amounts"; parse.go already documented `Fdb // foreign debit, authoritative`), so every non-USD (HNL) split stored its USD magnitude MISLABELED as HNL native, and reports converted that already-USD figure HNL→USD a second time — shrinking the xrt≠1 HNL balance-sheet subset ~24×. Recorded choices:
  - **A currency branch is REQUIRED — "uniform fdb/fcr" is WRONG.** A new `nativeNetDebit(r, exp, base)` helper (parse.go) uses `db/cr` when `r.Currency == cfg.BaseCurrency` (USD) and `fdb/fcr` otherwise; both amount call sites (`transactions.go resolveSplit`, `campus.go recordAmount`) route through it, and `NetDebit(db,cr,exp)` stays a tested low-level primitive. The task's premise that "for USD splits fdb==db so uniform fdb/fcr is safe" was FALSIFIED against the real export: `db != fdb` on ~14.6k USD debit rows (whose fdb holds the FOREIGN HNL counterpart) and on ~8.3k HNL rows (whose db holds the base USD counterpart). `db`/`cr` is ALWAYS the base pair and `fdb`/`fcr` ALWAYS the foreign pair, regardless of which reads larger — a uniform column choice corrupts whichever side it isn't. So the USD/non-USD branch is mandatory, not cosmetic.
  - **Multi-currency stays balanced with a LOCALIZED change (no FX refactor, no STOP).** The importer buckets splits by `r.Currency` and balances each currency bucket independently through FX Clearing (D3) WITHOUT ever using `xrt` to relate the legs; `xrt` is parsed but unused in amount math. Switching a bucket's legs to their native pair keeps every currency bucket self-balancing, so the fix is a one-helper change touching only the two amount derivations — the task's "STOP and report if multi-currency makes this non-trivial" escape hatch did NOT apply. Verified: single-currency HNL source groups net to zero on `fdb-fcr`; the real import produced **0 store rejections** (the store's per-transaction + per-fund zero-sum is the safety net).
  - **The campus test fixture's one divergent foreign row was corrected to the real convention.** The synthetic `testSource` tid 12 (an MXN campus revenue) had encoded a THIRD, subsidiary-base convention (MXN in `db/cr`, USD in `fdb/fcr`), which happened to hide the bug — the only fixture row where the conventions differ in VALUE. It was flipped to the real export convention (base USD in `db/cr`, native MXN in `fdb/fcr`) so the fixture exhibits the bug under the old code and the fix under the new. Two new tests (`TestNativeNetDebitSelectsColumnPairByCurrency`, `TestForeignSplitStoresNativeAndConvertsForReport`) assert the stored native equals the fdb figure for a non-USD split with `db≠fdb`, the USD figure for a USD split with a ~24× foreign fdb, that the drawdown pool converts the native MXN→USD correctly, and that a single-currency non-USD txn nets to zero — all proven to FAIL under the old `db/cr` path.
  - **Real-data verification (figures reported to the coordinator only, rule 11; temp `bin/dev-hnl.db`, `bin/cuento check` clean, 0 store rejections):** the four vetted HNL balance-sheet accounts now tie EXACTLY as-of 2021-12-31 at the period-end rate (Pledges Receivable-HNL **12,754.89**, Petty Cash Blue Bag **4,500.99**, Banco Occidente 2 **292.08**, Banco Atlantida **61.25** — each was ~24× too small before). USD accounts are UNCHANGED (Land **166,482.00** exact). FY2021 total revenue is **1,081,291.31** (income statement ties, no regression). The "Restore the Way" campus fund figures from p26.43/p26.47/p26.51 were computed on the corrupted HNL data and are SUPERSEDED — the corrected per-currency native fund balances are re-reported to the coordinator for campaign re-verification (fund per-currency net-debit still zero-sum; asset backing stays positive → no Z18).
  - `go vet ./...` / `gofmt -l` (empty) / `make test` / `make check` green.
- **p26.60 (bank import mapping renamed "payee" → "description")** — the CSV-import mapping's descriptive column and its i18n/form vocabulary were renamed from "payee" to "description" to match the app's post-p26.20 naming (the payee ENTITY was retired then; this catches the mapping UI up). `bankimport.Config.PayeeCol` → `DescCol` and its JSON tag `payee_col` → `desc_col`; form field `payee_col` → `desc_col`; i18n `import.col.payee` → `import.col.desc`. The JSON-tag change means any dev-created `mapping_profiles.config` blob written with the old tag would decode `DescCol` as 0 — acceptable because per RULE 11 no real data exists and profiles are locally created; there is nothing to migrate. The stored DB column `import_rows.parsed_payee` and the `DedupeHash` internals keep their names (already surfaced as `Description` in Go; a forward-only column rename is out of scope and risk-free to defer).
- **p26.63 (import mapping profile delete is a SOFT delete, not a hard DELETE)** — `import_batches.profile_id` is `NOT NULL REFERENCES mapping_profiles(id)` and every batch (including the throwaway "import DATE" profile `importConfirm` creates on each confirm) references a profile at BIRTH, so with `foreign_keys=ON` (db.go DSN) a hard `DELETE` of any real profile trips the FK. It is also the rule-14 spirit: the mapping that produced a batch is that batch's audit. So "delete" is a **deactivate**: migration `00024` adds `mapping_profiles.active INTEGER NOT NULL DEFAULT 1` (a plain in-place ADD COLUMN — mapping_profiles is a non-versioned operational table, DECISIONS p17.1, so no version trigger), `ListMappingProfiles` gains `WHERE active = 1`, and a new `DeactivateMappingProfile` (`:execrows`, guarded `AND active = 1`) flips it to 0 through the write funnel. The deactivated row and every batch FK into it survive; the profile just stops being offered. `POST /import/profiles/{id}/delete` (TxnWrite, registry) drives it; a missing/already-gone id is `ErrMappingProfileNotFound` → 404. Save was already working (importConfirm persists a named profile that ListMappingProfiles then offers, and GetMappingProfile restores the Config) — a new round-trip test locks that in.
- **p26.64 (horizontal column mapping — label your real columns instead of typing indices)** — the mapping UI was re-oriented: instead of typing a zero-based column NUMBER per field on GET /import, the user uploads first, and POST /import/preview parses the HEADER and renders the file's ACTUAL columns HORIZONTALLY (header name + a row-1 sample) each with a "maps to" `<select>` (Date / Description / Amount / Debit / Credit / Ignore). The index-based `bankimport.Config` is DERIVED server-side (`ConfigFromRoles`), and a loaded profile reverse-maps to pre-select the dropdowns (`RolesFromConfig`, out-of-range-safe). Recorded choices:
  - **Enrich the existing 2-step flow, don't add a stage.** The map+preview co-render in ONE bare workspace fragment (`import-map-preview`) on the EXISTING /import/preview; changing a role or the mode re-POSTs that fragment (htmx, csv_b64 carried so no re-upload); confirm (/import) is UNCHANGED (it still reads the derived `*_col` hidden fields). No new route, no 3rd stage.
  - **Two server paths, discriminated by the presence of legacy `*_col` fields.** The shipped UI never emits `date_col/amount_col/...`, so only the pre-p26.64 Go handler tests hit the LEGACY path (typed indices → `mappingFrom` → 200 preview | bare `import-error` 422, byte-identical old behavior, all 4 kept green untouched). Everything else takes the NEW path. A bad column MAPPING on the new path is an IN-FRAGMENT hint (selects stay), NOT a workspace-wiping 422 — that stays reserved for FILE-level problems (no file / too large / unreadable / zero rows), preserving p26.62's no-nesting guarantee on every path.
  - **Mode→option gating is SERVER-SIDE, superseding p26.61's client toggle.** The amount MODE select lives IN the fragment; changing it re-POSTs and the server renders only the mode-appropriate "maps to" options (Amount in single; Debit + Credit in debit_credit) and coerces any now-invalid role pick to Ignore. This makes `importmapping.js` + the `data-amount-field` blocks DEAD, so they were DELETED (p26.61's checkbox stays ticked — it shipped and was real — but its mechanism is replaced; the client toggle is gone). Plain htmx (already loaded), no new module; NO-JS works via the visible "Preview" submit button.
  - **Memo was omitted from the p26.64 role set, then RESTORED in p26.65.** p26.64's role set was Date/Description/Amount/Debit/Credit/Ignore — no Memo — so `ConfigFromRoles` hard-set `MemoCol = -1` and a staged row's memo was always empty (a conscious scope call at the time). **p26.65 reverses this:** Memo is back as an OPTIONAL, mode-independent role (see the p26.65 entry below). This bullet is kept for history; the current behavior is p26.65's.

- **p26.65 (Memo restored as an OPTIONAL mapping role)** — reverses p26.64's memo omission. A new `bankimport.RoleMemo` ("memo") joins the role set; `ConfigFromRoles` maps a Memo-tagged column to `Config.MemoCol` and `RolesFromConfig` emits it, so a mapped memo column ROUND-TRIPS through profile save/load and the horizontal UI pre-selects it (just like Date/Desc/Amount). The parser already read `MemoCol` into `ParsedRow.Memo` (untouched since p17.2), and the review editor already prefills the posted split's `memo` from the staged row's memo — so the only gap was the p26.64 UI dropping the role; wiring it back reconnects the full pipeline. Choices: (1) **Optional, never required** — the default stays Ignore/`MemoCol = -1`; `requiredRolesMapped` is unchanged (memo is not a required role), so an import with NO memo column parses and stages cleanly (empty memo, no validation error). (2) **Mode-independent** — like Date and Description, Memo is offered in both single and debit/credit modes (`roleValidInMode`'s default-true branch already covered it; only `importRoleOptions` needed the entry with no `AmountMode`). (3) **Description stays the primary text field** — memo is a distinct, secondary optional field (the p26.60 desc-not-payee split description remains the dedupe-hash source and primary line text). New i18n key `import.role.memo` (both catalogs). Tests: bankimport `columns_test.go` gains memo-optional + memo-round-trip cases (the existing parse tests already prove a mapped memo sets the split memo and an unmapped one is empty); e2e bank-import.spec gains a mapped-memo-previews-and-imports + omitting-memo-still-works case. FULL `make e2e` stays green.
- **p26.67 (import: guard the reverse-convention FX edge case — Caja Moneda Extranjera)** — a second-pass reconciliation found ONE `default_currency=USD` account (Caja Moneda Extranjera, 5 rows in the whole export) stored in LEMPIRA, not USD. The p26.56 base branch (`nativeNetDebit` → `db/cr` when `currency == base`) trusts the documented base invariant (`xrt = 1`, `db == fdb`, `db/cr` = USD). These 5 rows VIOLATE it: `xrt ≈ 24.8`, and `db/cr` holds the LEMPIRA figure while `fdb/fcr` holds the true USD — exactly backward from every other base row — so the base branch stored the lempira magnitude mislabeled as USD (~24× too large). Recorded choices:
  - **A NARROW guard, not a reversal of p26.56.** `reverseConventionBaseRow(r, exp)` fires ONLY when ALL hold: `currency == base`, `xrt != 1`, both net-debits nonzero and unequal (the `db == fdb` invariant is broken), AND the base magnitude is the LARGER one equal to the foreign magnitude scaled by xrt: `|net(db,cr)| == |net(fdb,fcr)| * xrt` (within 2%). When it fires, native comes from `fdb/fcr`; otherwise the normal `db/cr` base path is unchanged. The task's suggested discriminator (`xrt != 1 AND db != fdb`) was FALSIFIED against the real export: it matches ~22.4k USD rows (every USD row with a genuine HNL counterpart — where `db/cr` correctly holds the SMALLER USD and `fdb/fcr` the larger HNL), not just the 5 reverse rows. The distinguishing tell is the DIRECTION: a normal USD row's `db/cr` is the smaller USD side (`|base| < |foreign|`), whereas a reverse row's `db/cr` is the larger xrt-scaled side. Adding the `|base| > |foreign|` + `|base| == |foreign|·xrt` clauses isolates PRECISELY the 5 rows / 1 account. Only `xrt` (a rate, the one permitted float, D12) and the scaling comparison touch float; the STORED amount still comes exactly from `fdb/fcr` via `money.Parse`.
  - **Real-data verification (figures to the coordinator only, rule 11; temp db, no `--anonymize`; `cuento check` clean, 0 rejections).** Caja Moneda Extranjera now ties py at **172.00 USD** as of 2022-12-31 (was 4266.45). A full old-vs-new per-account balance diff shows EXACTLY two accounts move: Caja Moneda Extranjera (+213.58 whole-span) and its balancing FX Clearing counter-leg (−213.58, equal and opposite — the D3 multi-currency re-balance of the 5 corrected splits). NO revenue/expense account changes, so FY2021/FY2022 income-statement totals are unchanged.
  - Synthetic tests (`TestNativeNetDebitReverseConventionBaseRow`): a reverse row (`db/cr` HNL scaled, `fdb/fcr` USD, `xrt ≈ 24.8`) stores the USD from `fdb/fcr`; a normal base row (`db==fdb`, `xrt=1`) and a normal USD row (USD in `db/cr`, larger foreign in `fdb/fcr`) are BOTH unchanged (guard does not fire); a reverse debit + reverse credit balance to zero. `go vet` / `gofmt -l` (empty) / `make test` / `make check` green.
- **p26.68 (reports: Capital Campaign Capitalized + RNA lines — route through FundPeriodStatement)** — a report-vs-py reconciliation found two internal inconsistencies in the p26.51 Capital Campaign report (`internal/reports/capital_campaign.go`): (1) the Capitalized COLUMN netted fund LIABILITY splits into itself (`q.capitalized -= r.Amount`) while the detail section listed only ASSET accounts, so the column could not be reconciled from the rows shown; (2) RNA was accumulated as an independent spendable-asset running balance instead of its documented formula `Rev − Exp − Capitalized`, double-counting a construction liability. Recorded choices:
  - **Root cause + fix: derive every line from the shipped p15.8 `FundStatement` instead of an inline classifier.** The report re-implemented fund classification (revenue/expense/asset/liability folding) inline, diverging from `FundPeriodStatement` (compute.go), whose liability handling routes a DRAW to `Received` and a paydown to `AppliedNonExpense` — coherently, never into `Capitalized`. `runCapitalCampaign` now calls `FundPeriodStatement` per quarter: flows (Gross Revenue=Received, Gross Expenses=AppliedExpense) over [qFrom,qTo]; balances (Capitalized=Capitalized, RNA=Closing) over [start,qEnd]; the cumulative-total row uses a whole-span statement. The inline `capitalAssetAccounts` helper and the per-currency `switch acctType` bucketing are deleted (`FundStatement.CapitalAccounts` now supplies the capital-account set for the detail section). The report stays parameterized by fund + quarterly.
  - **Both invariants now hold BY CONSTRUCTION.** `FundStatement.Capitalized` accumulates ONLY capital ASSET accounts (its `CapitalAccounts` set), and the detail section lists exactly those accounts — so the Capitalized COLUMN == the sum of the detail ROWS. And because the fund opens at 0, `Closing == Received − AppliedExpense − Capitalized`, which for a campaign whose liability activity is a draw (a receipt, not a paydown) is exactly `Rev − Exp − Capitalized` — the RNA formula. **Gross Revenue now includes liability loan proceeds** (resources received per D20), and Capitalized stays asset-only, so NO liabilities sub-section is needed in the detail (the task's parenthetical fallback does not apply under the FundStatement mapping).
  - **Fixture + golden.** `ExtendCapitalCampaign` gains a Construction Loan liability that DIRECTLY financed a Construction purchase (DR Construction / CR Loan, NO cash leg — a cash leg would trip FundStatement's asset-debit capital heuristic and misclassify Checking as capital, which is a shared pre-existing quirk, not this bug). This exercises the two bugs, so `make golden` MOVES (reviewed): Gross revenue carries the $2,000 loan proceeds in Q3, Construction rises to $7,000 (5,000 cash + 2,000 loan), Capitalized $15,000 native (Land + Construction, loan excluded), cumulative Capitalized column == Land + Construction detail sum, cumulative RNA == Rev − Exp − Capitalized (native exact; converted carries the accepted 1-cent FX residual, p26.51).
  - **Verify-by-stash proves the tests discriminate.** With the report change stashed (old inline code) against the new fixture, `TestCapitalCampaignColumnReconciles` FAILS for the right reasons — Capitalized column ($20,387.58) ≠ detail sum ($18,387.58) because the loan is netted in, and RNA ≠ Rev − Exp − Capitalized (off by the loan). It passes on the new code; the bridge test passes on both (FundStatement itself was always correct — the report misused it). Tests added: `TestCapitalCampaignColumnReconciles` (column==detail + RNA==formula on the emitted table); `TestCapitalCampaignFundStatementBridge` already ties the engine to FundPeriodStatement. `go vet` / `gofmt -l` (empty) / `make test` / node `--test` / `make check` / reviewed golden diff / capital-campaign report e2e green.
- **p26.70 (reports: present the intercompany residual as a Cumulative Translation Adjustment (CTA) equity line)** — the balance sheet appended a bare footnote "Intercompany accounts do not net to zero: $X" whenever the D19-eliminated intercompany accounts left a nonzero residual on a consolidated scope. On real data that residual grows $43k (2023) → $95k (2025) → $101k (2026-H1) and reads as a scary unexplained error, but it is mostly a legitimate ASC-830 FX TRANSLATION ADJUSTMENT (retranslating accumulated foreign — HNL — intercompany balances at the closing rate) plus a stable ~$40k genuine-imbalance core (a year-boundary cutoff timing item being fixed separately in the import). Recorded choices:
  - **Computation: a new toolkit method `IntercompanyResidualSplit` (compute.go) decomposes the residual, converted to the target, into `Closing` and `Historical`.** `Closing` = `IntercompanyNet`'s native per-currency residual converted at the as-of CLOSING rate (the balance-sheet treatment). `Historical` = the SAME intercompany positions valued FLOW-wise — the intercompany-flagged accounts' cumulative activity to the as-of date, converted month-by-month at each month's rate, unrounded-then-half-even-once per currency (the D12 RateTxnDate grain). A NEW path is required because `Activity` applies `consolidatedICExclusions` and returns NOTHING for intercompany accounts on a consolidated scope, so the historical leg walks them directly like `IntercompanyNet` does. **CTA = Closing − Historical** (the retranslation gain/loss); **reconciling difference = Historical** (the genuine imbalance, which → 0 once the import cutoff fix lands). A same-currency-as-target residual has Closing == Historical → CTA 0, all in the reconciling component (USD 1:1 at every date). The rates are reachable via `RateOn`/`ConvertMinorAt` — this is a new computation, not missing rate data, so it did NOT trip the task's STOP clause.
  - **SCOPED to the intercompany residual (not a full ASC-830 CTA across ALL translated balances).** A complete CTA would retranslate every foreign balance (assets, liabilities, all equity) at closing vs historical and post the aggregate difference to an equity CTA account — a larger refactor of how every converted line is computed. This change presents ONLY the intercompany residual's FX-translation component as CTA and its historical-rate core as the reconciling line, which already fixes the misleading "does not net to zero" presentation the task targets. The boundary is the scope call the task permitted.
  - **Presentation carves the residual OUT of the without-restriction line; the plug (net-assets total) and the identity are UNTOUCHED.** The residual is currently absorbed INTO the plug: eliminating the intercompany legs leaves consolidated assets short by the residual, and net assets (defined as the plug, assets − liabilities) follows, so the without-restriction figure is distorted by −closing. The CONVERTED (single-target) view reclassifies that distortion into two labeled net-asset lines — a **Cumulative Translation Adjustment** line and an **Intercompany reconciling difference** line — while restoring the without-restriction line to its undistorted value. The three added deltas sum to EXACTLY zero: `+closing` (restore without) `+ (historical − closing)` (CTA) `+ (−historical)` (reconciling) `== 0`, so `without + CTA + reconciling + with` still foots to the plug and `assets == L + NA` holds exactly.
