The residual is a converted (target-minor) quantity — injecting `{target: v}` into the native without-map converts identity (target→target 1:1), so the restoration lands exactly on the converted total.
  - **The displayed CTA/reconciling signs (`historical − closing` and `−historical`) are FORCED by the double-entry identity, not a stylistic contra-equity choice.** Once the without-restriction line is restored to its undistorted value `NA_clean`, `without_clean + CTA + core + with == NA_clean + (CTA+core)` must equal the plug `= NA_clean − R` (the plug is short by the residual R because the eliminated legs left assets short), which forces `CTA + core == −R`. The task's suggested "`CTA + core == old residual`" holds in MAGNITUDE (`|CTA + core| == R`); the sign is the only solution that keeps `A == L + NA` with a restored `without` (empirically, the `+R` reading drives the without-restriction figure ~2×R AWAY from its clean value — a directional failure the CTA test guards against). So the displayed CTA is `historical − closing` and reconciling is `−historical` — the negation of the raw components, a forced consequence recorded here so the reviewer does not read it as an inverted formula.
  - **The NATIVE (per-currency detail) view has no single rate, so there is no translation component — and the split gate MUST exclude it.** `showCTA` gates on `consolidated && hasNonzero(icNet) && target != "" && !detail`: the `!detail` clause is load-bearing, because the detail view runs WITH a target (it shows native + converted columns) and, without the exclusion, the target-currency CTA injection would pollute the native figures and render a converted residual where the native residual belongs. In detail mode the report falls through to the reconciling-difference line PER NATIVE CURRENCY (the old warning row, relabeled from the bare "do not net to zero" key to `reports.balance_sheet.na.ic_reconciling`), so the residual is NEVER hidden in either view — just labeled honestly. `TestBalanceSheetCTADetailNoSplit` guards this combination. A LEAF/single-sub scope is not a consolidation and never reclassifies (its intercompany accounts are genuine due-to/due-from balances).
  - **Net-asset lines may foot to ±1 minor unit/currency against the plug on a nonzero MULTI-currency residual — an accepted rounding artifact, not a balance break.** The plug converts each currency's whole asset/liability sum ONCE (half-even), while the CTA/reconciling lines convert the residual separately; on a nonzero multi-currency residual (real data) `conv(without)+conv(with)+conv(CTA)+conv(reconciling)` can differ from `conv(plug)` by a minor unit per currency — the same `conv(a)+conv(b) ≠ conv(a+b)` half-even artifact that already appears elsewhere (income-statement footing note). The change does NOT introduce it (the added deltas sum to exactly zero as integers) — it only surfaces it in the converted nonzero-residual view. `A == L + NA` remains EXACT (both use the plug); chasing the line-level cent would require restructuring the whole per-currency net-asset computation (STOP-clause territory), so it is left as a conscious call. Zero on the clean fixture (residual zero → no lines).
  - **Golden byte-identical; tests.** On the clean synthetic fixture the intercompany accounts net to zero (residual zero), so no CTA/reconciling rows are emitted and `make golden` does NOT move — the balance-sheet golden is byte-identical. The `IntercompanyResidualSplit` call is gated behind `hasNonzero(icNet) && target != ""`, so the common (balanced) path pays nothing for the historical month-walk. New i18n `reports.balance_sheet.na.cta` + `.na.ic_reconciling` (both catalogs). Tests: `TestBalanceSheetCTASplit` (corrupted-copy MXN residual — bare warning GONE, `A == L + NA` exact, CTA + reconciling reclassify the whole closing residual, without moved TOWARD its undistorted value); `TestIntercompanyResidualSplitSameCurrency` (USD residual → CTA 0) + `TestIntercompanyResidualSplitTranslation` (MXN residual → nonzero CTA, both legs == ConvertMinorAt at the closing / txn-date dates); the native `TestBalanceSheetIntercompanyWarning` updated to the reconciling label. `go vet ./...` / `gofmt -l` (empty) / `make test` / node `--test` / `make check` / i18n parity / report e2e green.
- **p26.71 (reports: functional-expenses + 990 Part IX at the transaction-date rate, so Part IX ties the income statement)** — a cross-report reconciliation found the functional-expenses grand total and the 990 Part IX grand total did NOT equal the income statement's total expenses whenever intra-year FX rates move (on real data the FY2025 gap was ~$5,034.66). The income statement (`income_statement.go`) converts expense FLOWS at each transaction's-date rate (`RateTxnDate`, the P&L treatment, D12), but `functional_expenses.go` and `form_990.go` Part IX converted the same flows at the single period-end CLOSING rate — and inside form_990 itself, Part VIII revenue (txn-date) and Part IX expenses (closing) sat on DIFFERENT bases, so the package did not internally reconcile. An expense is a period flow measured at the rate in force when it occurred; the closing rate is for point-in-time BALANCES (the balance sheet), not flows. Recorded choices:
  - **Fix: a `RateTxnDate` branch on `Toolkit.FunctionalMatrix` (compute.go), mirroring `Activity`'s TxnDate path EXACTLY, then flip both call sites off `RateClosing`.** The branch decomposes [from,to] into calendar months (`ByPeriod(GranMonth)`), converts each month's native (account,class) activity at that month's on-or-before rate, accumulates the UNROUNDED `float64(amount)·rate·10^(exTo−exFrom)` per (account,class), and rounds half-even ONCE per cell — the same `RateOn(pTo)` / exponents / half-even-once grain `Activity` uses, and the same intercompany exclusion (already applied in both). `functional_expenses.go` (~line 84) and `form_990.go` partIX (~line 372) change `Mode: RateClosing` → `RateTxnDate`. FE == 990 Part IX is exact and automatic (both consume the identical rounded cells); FE == income-statement total expenses is exact at GranNone.
  - **The tie is exact only when both sides round at the same grain — compare against the income statement at GranNone.** A quarterly income-statement run rounds per (account,quarter) then sums (the documented 4,099,507-vs-4,099,506 footing note); the functional matrix rounds once over the whole period. So the tie test (`TestFunctionalExpensesTiesIncomeStatement`) runs the income statement at GranNone (round once, whole period) and asserts FE grand == IS total expenses == 990 Part IX grand as an IDENTITY (all three computed, no literal pinned). On the multi-currency multi-rate fixture all three tie at 2,377,088.
  - **Grain caveat (bounds the "exactly" claim honestly).** `FunctionalMatrix` rounds per (account×CLASS); `Activity` rounds per account. For an account whose splits span MORE THAN ONE functional class, `Σ round(class) ≠ round(Σ classes)` by up to a minor unit — so on a real multi-class chart a sub-dollar residual between FE and the income statement can remain, ORTHOGONAL to the FX-basis gap ($5,034.66) this change actually closes. Every synthetic fixture expense account is single-class, so the tie is exact there and the tests pass; FE's internal footing (Σ converted cells == the grand total, per row and overall) holds regardless of grain. The boundary is recorded here so the claim is not overstated.
  - **Golden + docstrings.** Reviewed `make golden`: ONLY `functional_expenses.{txt,csv}` and `form_990.{txt,csv}` move, and only their MXN-bearing cells shift to the higher txn-date basis (Program Supplies 237,624→238,971, Food Purchases 19,890→20,617, IX.24e 417,514→419,588, grand 2,375,014→2,377,088); every pure-USD cell (Salaries, Bank Fees, Occupancy, Event Costs, Insurance) is byte-identical, and the balance sheet / income statement / other goldens do not move. The FE + 990 docstrings that claimed the closing-rate "year-end rollup" was intentional were replaced with the txn-date/flow rationale and the tie statement. `go vet ./...` / `gofmt -l` (empty) / `make test` / `make check` / reviewed golden diff green.
- **p26.72 (import: config-driven manual adjustment entries)** — the mechanical CSV import cannot express journal entries the owner's consolidation worksheet requires but the source books do not carry balanced within one fiscal period — e.g. a year-end IN-TRANSIT transfer whose sending leg posts one fiscal year on one subsidiary's books and whose receiving leg posts the NEXT year on another subsidiary's, so cuento mis-TIMES the recognition. Recorded choices (mechanism only — the specific corrective values live ONLY in the gitignored `fixtures/source/mapping.json`, rule 11):
  - **A GENERAL primitive, not a one-off hack.** A new `corrections` list on the importer config (`Config.Corrections`, `[]Correction` in `mapping.go`) holds fully-specified, self-balancing adjustment transactions the owner can extend for any future legitimate consolidation/cutoff entry. Each `Correction` is one transaction: `date`, `subsidiary` (name), `currency`, optional `memo`/`description`, and a `splits` list. Each `CorrectionSplit` is `account` (a source_acct key in the account-mapping CSV), `amount` (the EXACT signed net-debit in the currency's minor units — int64, Dr +/Cr −, NEVER a float or the lossy source `v`, rule 3), and optional `fund` (donor key), `program` (name), `functional_class`, `description`.
  - **Posts through the store like any other transaction (no special path).** `builder.corrections` (`corrections.go`) runs in the all-in-one `runBuild` AFTER every subsidiary's transactions (so every account/fund/program it references is live), resolves the human-readable keys against the same id maps the import already built (`res.SubsidiaryIDs`/`AccountIDs`/`FundIDs`/`ProgramIDs`), and calls `PostTransaction`. So an adjustment is versioned (rule 5) and passes every ledger invariant (rule 7: single currency + subsidiary, per-transaction AND per-fund zero-sum, program-on-R/E-only, class-on-expense-only). UNLIKE a source group, a correction gets NO synthesized Opening-Balances / FX-Clearing plug leg: it is human-authored and MUST already balance, so a residual is a config error surfaced as a LOUD build failure (`correction N (date): store rejected adjustment: …`), never plugged or warned-and-continued.
  - **Representation of the cutoff (values gitignored).** The correction encoded in the local config is TWO balanced entries on the Honduras (UPH) books in HNL, keyed on human-readable account names: (1) at FY2021 close, recognize the in-transit transfer as intercompany income — Cr the intercompany revenue account (the same `Donaciones del Exterior` that is BOTH the income account and the D19-eliminated receiving leg, so one credit satisfies "FY2021 income reflects it" AND "the intercompany residual drops"), with the receiving program on that revenue leg (rule 7 requires a program on a revenue split — a program-less correction is REJECTED, which is why the representation MUST name it); Dr the per-subsidiary Opening-Balances equity account as the in-transit counter (no dedicated due-from asset exists on the receiving books, and Opening Balances is the D22 adjustment account). (2) At the FY2022 receipt date, the exact REVERSE, so when the real receiving leg imports the recognition is not double-counted (all-time net on the revenue account from the pair is zero; only the FY2021-vs-FY2022 TIMING shifts). The amount is the EXACT integer from the sending transfer (tid 23486's native HNL figure, not the lossy CONS `v`).
  - **Verification (temp real db, counts/figures to the coordinator only, rule 11; no `--anonymize`).** Built the full real export WITH the two corrections: build exits 0, **2 correction transactions post** (the FY2021 recognition + the FY2022 reversal), **0 store rejections**, `cuento check` **clean (no violations)**. FY2021 income on the intercompany revenue account, which was zero before (the receipt only posted FY2022), now carries the recognized HNL amount — Honduras FY2021 income reflects the transfer. As-of FY2021-close, the intercompany historical-core residual DROPS toward zero: the recognition's revenue leg converts (at the closing HNL→USD rate) to ≈ the UPLAM `Transfers To Honduras` intercompany expense it offsets, so the ~$40k genuine-imbalance core the p26.70 reconciling-difference line reported nets out, while the small closing-vs-transfer-rate FX gap remains as the retained CTA translation component. The all-time intercompany net is unchanged (steady state FY2022+ intact). Synthetic tests (rule 11): `TestCorrectionPostsBalancedAdjustment` (a config `corrections` entry posts a balanced fund-tagged correction with the exact integer amounts/accounts/program, ledger.Check clean) and `TestCorrectionRejectsUnbalanced` (a non-zero-sum correction FAILS the build loudly). `go vet ./...` / `gofmt -l` (empty) / `make test` / `make check` green.
- **p26.73 (import+fixture: drop the statement-tier parent accounts from the stored chart)** — the p26.12 stmt→typ derivation stored a top `<stmt super-parent>` tier (Assets/Liabilities/Equity/Revenue/Expenses) above the `(stmt,typ)` intermediates as REAL root accounts. But every report ALSO injects those tiers as its own section headers, so the stored chart DOUBLED the header ("Assets → Assets…"), and the stmt tier is redundant with each account's `type` field (also derived from `stmt`). Recorded choices:
  - **Stop storing the stmt tier; re-parent the type-level intermediates to ROOTS.** `runAccounts` (`accounts.go`) no longer emits the `::super:` super-parent rows: the `(stmt,typ)` intermediate is created with a nil parent, and a blank-`typ` (or unknown-stmt) leaf is itself a root. Each account keeps its `type` — that is what display grouping keys on (a follow-up injects the type-tier header into the chart + account selector; reports already inject their own section headers, so this simply removes the doubling). Dead code removed: `stmtToSuperParent` (mapping.go), `superParentKey`/`superKeyPrefix` (accounts.go). `build.go`'s topo-sort is unchanged (a root intermediate is just a shorter chain).
  - **The in-scope ripple: `reloadAccounts` had to key on (type, name-path), not name-path alone.** The split-import `reloadAccounts` (build.go) matches each mapping row to its scaffolded db account by full NAME PATH. The dropped stmt tier was silently DISAMBIGUATING two same-named type tiers: the real chart has both a revenue "Transfers" tier and an expense "Transfers" tier, distinct only by their `Revenue`/`Expenses` super-parent prefix. Re-parenting both to root collapsed their paths to a bare "Transfers" → the reload aborted with "duplicate name path" and the de-tiered build produced 0 transactions. Fix (contained to build.go, a file the step names in-scope): prefix every path key with the account's cuento TYPE (`typedAccountKey`). Type is constant along a chain (a leaf parents under an intermediate of its own type), so keying on the self's type is consistent between the db and mapping sides; a completing import over the real data (49.5k txns) is the uniqueness proof. This was NOT the feared balance ripple — the 5 stmt-tier accounts held ZERO splits (verified) — just a name-collision the tier had been masking.
  - **Fixture unchanged because it never had the tier — verification is the real-data balance diff, not the byte-identical golden.** The synthetic fixture (Appendix D) has no stmt-tier super-parents: its asset/liability/equity accounts are direct roots and its "Revenue"/"Expenses" placeholder parents are TYPE-level roots. So the fixture already models the target, needed no edit, and CANNOT exhibit the doubling — `make golden` is byte-identical, which proves the fixture was unaffected, NOT that the change works. The real proof is a temp-db build of the actual export with a de-tiered account map (values gitignored, rule 11): `cuento check` clean, 0 store rejections, 49,546 transactions (identical to the tiered build), the 5 stmt-tier accounts gone, both same-named "Transfers" tiers present as distinct-typed roots, 0 orphaned `parent_id` FKs, and an old-vs-new per-leaf balance diff (keyed by type+terminal-name+currency, since old-db leaf paths carry the dropped prefix) that is IDENTICAL across all 237 leaf balances — no number moved (the stmt tier carried no balances/rollup).
  - **Tests.** `TestRunAccountsEmitsTypTierRoots` (renamed from `…TwoLevelChain`; the `(stmt,typ)` intermediate is a root, a blank-typ leaf is a root, NO `::super:` rows emitted, same-typ-different-stmt tiers stay distinct) + `TestRunAccountsLeafSpansTypsSubsetSubs` (the intermediate is a root and still a superset of the leaf's subs) + `TestRunAccountsTypCollidesWithLeafName` (unchanged) + `TestReloadDisambiguatesSameNamedTypeTierRoots` (two same-named "Transfers" ROOTS of different types scaffold + import without a reload collision, resolving to distinct ids; ledger.Check clean). `docs/ledger-export.md` "Account tree derivation" updated to the one-level model. `go vet ./...` / `gofmt -l` (empty) / `make test` / node `--test` / `make check` / reviewed golden diff (byte-identical) green.
- **p26.74 (ux: inject type-tier grouping into the chart of accounts + the account selector)** — after p26.73 the type-level accounts (e.g. "Fixed Assets", "Cash") are ROOTS carrying their `type`; the statement-tier grouping is now a PRESENTATION concern the chart and the account selector inject, keyed off each account's `type`, not stored data. Recorded choices:
  - **Chart: server-injected display-only headers, whole-block bucketing.** `groupRowsByType` (web/accounts.go) splits the pre-ordered `store.Tree` rows into ROOT BLOCKS (a null-parent row + its subtree), buckets whole blocks into the canonical statement order (asset, liability, equity, revenue, expense) — EXPLICIT bucketing, not boundary-detection, so a user's interleaved account-creation order still lands both asset blocks under one Assets header — prefixes each non-empty type with a header `acctRow{Header:true}` at depth 0, and shifts every real row's depth +1 (type-level roots → depth 1). A type with zero blocks emits NO header (an empty depth-0 header would read as a phantom account-less row). The header row is display-only: `acct-type-header` class, no register link / edit / deactivate / balances, so it is not selectable and is not a real account. treetable collapse/expand works on it for free (its depth-0 position makes it the block parent; its name cell has no `<a>`, so p26.55 name-click toggles it) — treetable.js untouched.
  - **Selector: `<optgroup>`, NOT a visual prefix — the combobox is unaffected.** `HTMLSelectElement.options` flattens optgroup children, so `combobox.js`'s `collectOptions` still sees every option and `combofilter.js`'s fuzzy ranking is byte-for-byte unchanged; the account-fuzzy e2e scopes by option text, not group. So all three account selects (transaction body row `account_i`, transaction `main_account`, expense line `account_i`) wrap their options in `<optgroup label="Assets">…` per type (via `groupTxnAccountsByType` / `groupExpenseAccountsByType`), value="0" placeholder OUTSIDE any group, `Unavailable` force-included options landing in their type bucket. `model.Accounts` stays a FLAT slice, so `injectRowAccounts` and the JS data-attr consumers (txngrid subsidiary re-filter, gating) are untouched. NO combobox.js / txngrid.js edit — verified those read options via `querySelectorAll('option[data-account-option]')` (descendant-based, optgroup-safe), never `select.children`/`option.parentNode`. The expense grid offers only R/E leaves, so only the Revenue + Expenses optgroups appear there.
  - **Labels: new PLURAL `account.section.*` keys, not the singular per-account `account.type.*`.** The task named `account.type.*`, but those are SINGULAR ("Asset", "Liability") and load-bearing in the per-row Type COLUMN (accounts.tmpl); the visible header strings the task lists are PLURAL ("Assets", "Liabilities", …) and must match the report section labels (`reports.balance_sheet.section.*` / `income_statement.section.*`) per the "same labels as reports" constraint. Added five plural `account.section.{asset,liability,equity,revenue,expense}` keys to BOTH en.toml + es.toml (rule 9 parity), Spanish sourced verbatim from the existing report section es values (Activos/Pasivos/Ingresos/Gastos) + `account.type.equity` (Patrimonio). All three grouping builders + the chart header key point at `account.section.*`, so chart headers and selector optgroups group under the same words as the reports.

  - **Rides the existing filter form + persists like sub/active (p26.14).** A `<select name="type">` (All + the five types) joins the `accounts-controls` subsidiary/active filter form, so it auto-applies on change (the same htmx GET swapping `#accounts-results`) and degrades to the no-JS submit. The handler reads `type` INSIDE the existing `q.Has("sub")` branch — the `sub`-presence discriminator between a deliberate submit and a bare nav is UNCHANGED (the type select submits alongside `sub` on every real submit) — sanitizes it via `validAccountType` (unknown/blank → "All"), and persists it in a new `sessionAcctTypeKey` scs value restored on a bare visit (mirroring `sessionAcctSubKey`/`sessionAcctActiveKey`). Pure UI convenience, no DB column.

The type-option labels reuse the plural `account.section.*` keys (matching the injected headers); two new chrome keys `accounts.filter.type` / `accounts.filter.all_types` added to both catalogs (rule 9).

- **p26.79 (db: seed a fuller set of common budget schedules)** — 00025_common_schedules.sql seeds five more common recurrences on top of the four 00022 (p26.28) seeded, none duplicating an 00022 name: Weekly (Monday), Biweekly, Semimonthly (1st & 15th), Monthly (15th), Annual (Jan 1) — 9 seeded schedules total. Recorded choices:
  - **Quarterly / semi-annual DELIBERATELY OMITTED.** The recurrence model — the 00016 `budget_schedules.kind` CHECK enum (`onetime,annual,monthly,semimonthly,biweekly,weekly,custom`) and the pure engine `internal/budget.ExpandSchedule` — has NO >monthly interval kind and no generic "every N months" stride (`expandStride` is hardcoded to 14 for biweekly). A `quarterly`/`semiannual` row would fail the 00016 CHECK on insert and, if forced, hit ExpandSchedule's unknown-kind error (which `TestStandardSchedulesEngineValid` catches). Adding them is an ENGINE change (a new enum member — SQLite cannot ALTER a CHECK, so a table recreate — plus a new expander), out of scope for a pure `db:` seed step. Seed only what the model expresses; the two are deferred (smallest reversible choice, AGENTS §Ambiguity).
  - **Mirrors 00022 exactly.** budget_schedules is a versioned business table (00016), so each seeded row gets its op='create' `_versions` snapshot copied INSERT…SELECT from the just-written LIVE row (byte-identical to live, Z3 can never diverge) tied to ONE `changes` row via a UNIQUE note (`'seed common budget schedules'`, distinct from 00022's `'seed standard budget schedules'` so the snapshot WHERE-note resolves exactly one change). AUTOINCREMENT ids (no hardcoded PKs) so it applies CLEANLY to an already-populated dev/sample db on the next migrate-on-startup; pure ASCII. Names are stored English DATA (proper-noun treatment, rule 9 — a bilingual org renames freely), NOT i18n catalog keys, so no catalog change.
- **p26.80 (testutil+ops: a sample budget — fixture golden coverage + a reusable dev seed)** — the budget-group reports (actuals_vs_budget / cashflow_projection) had no canonical fixture BUDGET; each report test built one inline. Recorded choices:
  - **Opt-in fixture seam, not unconditional.** `(*Fixture).ExtendSampleBudget(t)` mirrors ExtendRates / ExtendReconciliation / ExtendCapitalCampaign: New() does NOT call it, so adding a fixture budget churns ZERO existing goldens (a budget touches no balance/activity aggregate, but the seam is opt-in anyway for consistency and to keep the base fixture minimal). Only the two seam-driven report goldens (`actuals_vs_budget_sample.*` / `cashflow_projection_sample.*`, NEW filenames) change; the existing inline-budget goldens are untouched. The seam resolves the p26.79 seeded common schedules BY NAME (not CreateSchedule), so it exercises the seed and stays aligned with it. Synthetic amounts (rule 11); each line's currency = its account's default, so a line always references an existing currency. Consequence recorded: the restricted BecaAgua lines are USD-budgeted while the fixture's BecaAgua activity is MXN, so they read as pure PLAN; the USD unrestricted lines carry the visible variance. weekend_adjust=prev_business_day makes a weekend-first monthly occurrence roll into the prior month (visible doubling/absence in the golden).
  - **Reusable dev seed = a store-built CLI subcommand, not raw SQL.** `cuento devseed budget -db <db>` builds the sample budget on the STORE (write funnel + invariants, rule 2) so it tracks schema changes automatically. It MIGRATES first (so a db built before the schedule-seed migrations can resolve them by name — the single command is self-sufficient), resolves subsidiary / program / R-E leaf accounts / fund / schedules DYNAMICALLY from whatever the db already contains (no hardcoded real names, rule 11), and is IDEMPOTENT (skips if the sample budget name already exists) so `make dev-db` reruns and standalone reruns never duplicate. Wired into `dev-db` (dev builds auto-seed) and runnable standalone against the current `bin/dev.db` WITHOUT a re-import (stop the :3390 server first — it holds the file open and devseed migrates). The fixture seam (test-only, imports testing, uses fixture IDs) and devseed (queries a live db) are necessarily SEPARATE builders (the binary cannot import the fixture package); both resolve the seeded schedules by name.
